3. ADVANCED — Deep Topics
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Advanced I/O and Performance
----------------------------------------
Reading files efficiently:
  # Slow (spawns subshell per iteration):
  for line in $(cat file); do ...done

  # Fast (reads line by line in current shell):
  while IFS= read -r line; do
    echo "$line"
  done < file.txt

  # Process CSV with field splitting:
  while IFS=, read -r col1 col2 col3; do
    echo "Name: $col1, Age: $col2"
  done < data.csv

  # Read entire file into array (bash 4):
  mapfile -t lines < file.txt       → IFS-aware; handles blank lines
  readarray -t lines < file.txt     → alias for mapfile

  # Read null-delimited (safe for filenames with spaces/newlines):
  while IFS= read -r -d '' file; do
    echo "$file"
  done < <(find . -name "*.log" -print0)

co-processes (bash 4+):
  coproc BGPROC { tail -f /var/log/app.log; }
  while IFS= read -r line <&"${BGPROC[0]}"; do
    [[ "$line" =~ ERROR ]] && alert "$line"
  done

CONCEPT: Regular Expressions in Bash
--------------------------------------
  Bash uses ERE (Extended Regular Expressions) in [[ =~ ]]

  [[ "abc123" =~ ^[a-z]+[0-9]+$ ]] && echo "matched"
  [[ "192.168.1.1" =~ ^([0-9]{1,3}\.){3}[0-9]{1,3}$ ]] && echo "IP"

  Capture groups via BASH_REMATCH:
  if [[ "2024-01-15" =~ ^([0-9]{4})-([0-9]{2})-([0-9]{2})$ ]]; then
    year="${BASH_REMATCH[1]}"
    month="${BASH_REMATCH[2]}"
    day="${BASH_REMATCH[3]}"
  fi

  Glob patterns (NOT regex — used in case, file expansion):
    *       → any string
    ?       → single char
    [abc]   → character class
    [a-z]   → range
    ?(pattern) → zero or one (extglob)
    *(pattern) → zero or more (extglob)
    +(pattern) → one or more (extglob)
    @(p1|p2) → exactly one of (extglob)
    !(pattern) → anything except (extglob)

  Enable extglob: shopt -s extglob
  shopt -s globstar    → ** matches recursively (like find)
  shopt -s nullglob    → glob that matches nothing → empty (not literal)
  shopt -s dotglob     → include hidden files in globs

CONCEPT: Process Management from Scripts
------------------------------------------
Background processes & job control:
  cmd &
  bgpid=$!
  wait $bgpid                  → wait for specific PID
  wait                         → wait for all background jobs

  # Run N jobs in parallel with throttling:
  max_jobs=4
  for item in "${items[@]}"; do
    process_item "$item" &
    # throttle: if we have max_jobs running, wait for one to finish
    while (( $(jobs -r | wc -l) >= max_jobs )); do
      sleep 0.1
    done
  done
  wait   → wait for all remaining

  # xargs for parallelism:
  printf '%s\n' "${items[@]}" | xargs -P 4 -I {} bash -c 'process_item "$@"' _ {}

  # Timeout a command:
  timeout 30 command_that_might_hang
  timeout --kill-after=5 30 command  → SIGKILL after 35s if still running

Process substitution patterns:
  # Join two command streams:
  join <(sort -k1 file1) <(sort -k1 file2)

  # Log to file AND stdout simultaneously:
  exec > >(tee -a "$LOG_FILE") 2>&1

  # This redirects all stdout/stderr to tee for rest of script:
  # Great for scripts that need to log everything

CONCEPT: Advanced Functions & Libraries
-----------------------------------------
  Script as library pattern:
  # lib/common.sh
  # Guard against double-sourcing:
  [[ -n "${_COMMON_SH_LOADED:-}" ]] && return
  readonly _COMMON_SH_LOADED=true

  # Consumer script:
  source "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/lib/common.sh"

  BASH_SOURCE vs $0:
    $0          → name of the script being RUN
    ${BASH_SOURCE[0]} → name of the CURRENT file (even when sourced)
    Use ${BASH_SOURCE[0]} in libraries to get library's own path

  Stack trace on error:
  print_stacktrace() {
    local i=0
    echo "Stack trace:" >&2
    while caller $i >/dev/null 2>&1; do
      caller $i >&2
      (( i++ ))
    done
  }
  trap print_stacktrace ERR

  Memoization:
  declare -A _memo_cache
  expensive_func() {
    local key="$1"
    if [[ -v _memo_cache["$key"] ]]; then
      echo "${_memo_cache[$key]}"
      return
    fi
    local result
    result=$(do_expensive_work "$key")
    _memo_cache["$key"]="$result"
    echo "$result"
  }

CONCEPT: Arithmetic & Math
----------------------------
  (( result = 5 + 3 ))       → arithmetic (integers only)
  result=$(( 10 / 3 ))       → integer division: 3
  result=$(( 10 % 3 ))       → modulo: 1
  (( count++ ))               → increment
  (( arr[idx]++ ))            → increment array element
  (( result = base ** exp ))  → exponentiation

  Floating point (bash has no native float):
  result=$(echo "scale=4; 10/3" | bc)      → 3.3333
  result=$(echo "sqrt(2)" | bc -l)          → 1.4142...
  result=$(awk 'BEGIN { printf "%.2f\n", 10/3 }')

  printf for formatting:
  printf "%05d\n" 42          → 00042
  printf "%-20s %s\n" "key" "value"   → left-align
  printf "%08.3f\n" 3.14159  → 0003.142

CONCEPT: Networking in Scripts
--------------------------------
  curl patterns (production-grade):
  http_get() {
    local url="$1"
    local -i max_retries=3
    local -i retry=0
    while (( retry < max_retries )); do
      if curl -sf --connect-timeout 5 --max-time 30 "$url"; then
        return 0
      fi
      (( retry++ ))
      sleep $(( 2 ** retry ))    → exponential backoff
    done
    return 1
  }

  curl -o /dev/null -s -w "%{http_code}" "$url"  → get only status code
  curl -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
       -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
       -d '{"key":"value"}' \
       -X POST "$API_URL"

  Checking port availability:
  wait_for_port() {
    local host=$1 port=$2 timeout=${3:-60}
    local elapsed=0
    while ! nc -z "$host" "$port" 2>/dev/null; do
      (( elapsed++ ))
      (( elapsed >= timeout )) && return 1
      sleep 1
    done
  }

  IP validation:
  is_valid_ip() {
    [[ "$1" =~ ^([0-9]{1,3}\.){3}[0-9]{1,3}$ ]] || return 1
    IFS=. read -r a b c d <<< "$1"
    (( a <= 255 && b <= 255 && c <= 255 && d <= 255 ))
  }

CONCEPT: Script Testing with bats
-----------------------------------
BATS (Bash Automated Testing System):
  # test/deploy.bats
  #!/usr/bin/env bats

  setup() {
    tmpdir=$(mktemp -d)
    export TEST_DIR="$tmpdir"
  }

  teardown() {
    rm -rf "$tmpdir"
  }

  @test "script exits 0 on valid input" {
    run ./deploy.sh --env staging
    [ "$status" -eq 0 ]
  }

  @test "script errors on missing argument" {
    run ./deploy.sh
    [ "$status" -ne 0 ]
    [[ "$output" =~ "Usage:" ]]
  }

  @test "creates expected files" {
    ./setup.sh "$TEST_DIR"
    [ -f "$TEST_DIR/config.yaml" ]
  }

  bats test/          → run all tests in dir

HANDS-ON TASKS (Advanced):

  2. Write a parallel job runner with max-concurrency throttling
  3. Build a retry function with exponential backoff and jitter
  4. Create a bash library (common.sh) with logging, error handling, and
     argument validation — source it in 3 different scripts
  5. Write regex to extract structured data from log files using BASH_REMATCH
  6. Implement a script that streams logs and alerts on error patterns

4. EXPERT LEVEL — Production-Grade Knowledge
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Production Script Architecture
-----------------------------------------
Complete production script template:
  #!/usr/bin/env bash
  # ==============================================================================
  # script.sh — Description
  # Usage: script.sh [OPTIONS] <argument>
  # ==============================================================================
  set -euo pipefail
  IFS=$'\n\t'

  # Constants
  readonly SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"
  readonly SCRIPT_NAME="$(basename "$0")"
  readonly TIMESTAMP="$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)"
  readonly LOG_FILE="/var/log/${SCRIPT_NAME%.sh}.log"
  readonly LOCK_FILE="/var/run/${SCRIPT_NAME%.sh}.lock"

  # Colours (only if terminal supports it)
  if [[ -t 1 ]] && [[ -n "${TERM:-}" ]]; then
    readonly RED='\033[0;31m'
    readonly GREEN='\033[0;32m'
    readonly YELLOW='\033[1;33m'
    readonly NC='\033[0m'
  else
    readonly RED='' GREEN='' YELLOW='' NC=''
  fi

  # Logging
  log() {
    local level="$1"; shift
    printf "[%s] [%s] [%s] %s\n" \
      "$(date +'%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S%z')" "$SCRIPT_NAME" "$level" "$*" \
      | tee -a "$LOG_FILE"
  }
  info()  { log "INFO " "$@"; }
  warn()  { log "WARN " "$@" >&2; }
  error() { log "ERROR" "$@" >&2; }
  die()   { error "$@"; exit 1; }

  # Cleanup & Locking
  cleanup() {
    local exit_code=$?
    info "Cleanup triggered (exit code: $exit_code)"
    rm -f "$LOCK_FILE"
    [[ -n "${tmpdir:-}" ]] && rm -rf "$tmpdir"
  }
  trap cleanup EXIT
  trap 'die "Interrupted"' INT TERM

  acquire_lock() {
    if ! mkdir "$LOCK_FILE" 2>/dev/null; then
      die "Another instance is running (lock: $LOCK_FILE)"
    fi
  }

  # Dependency checks
  require_commands() {
    local missing=()
    for cmd in "$@"; do
      command -v "$cmd" &>/dev/null || missing+=("$cmd")
    done
    (( ${#missing[@]} == 0 )) || die "Missing commands: ${missing[*]}"
  }

  main() {
    acquire_lock
    require_commands curl jq aws kubectl
    # ... actual logic
  }
  main "$@"

CONCEPT: JSON Processing with jq
----------------------------------
jq is the standard tool for JSON in bash scripts.

  # Parse JSON output from API/CLI:
  aws ec2 describe-instances | jq '.Reservations[].Instances[] | {id: .InstanceId, ip: .PrivateIpAddress, state: .State.Name}'

  jq '.'                                 → pretty-print
  jq '.key'                              → extract key
  jq '.items[]'                          → iterate array
  jq '.items[] | select(.status == "running")'  → filter
  jq '.items[] | .name'                  → map: extract field
  jq '[.items[] | .name]'                → collect into array
  jq '.items | length'                   → array length
  jq 'keys'                              → object keys
  jq '.name // "default"'               → default value
  jq --arg name "Alice" '.name = $name'  → inject bash variable
  jq --argjson val 42 '.count = $val'    → inject number
  jq -r '.name'                          → raw output (no quotes)
  jq -e '.key'                           → exit 1 if null/false

  # Build JSON from bash:
  jq -n --arg host "$HOST" --arg port "$PORT" \
    '{host: $host, port: ($port | tonumber)}'

  # Update a field in a JSON file:
  jq '.version = "2.0"' config.json > config.json.tmp && mv config.json.tmp config.json

CONCEPT: YAML Processing (yq)
-------------------------------
  yq '.spec.replicas' deployment.yaml          → read value
  yq '.spec.replicas = 3' -i deployment.yaml   → in-place update
  yq '.spec.template.spec.containers[0].image' deployment.yaml
  yq eval-all 'select(fileIndex == 0) * select(fileIndex == 1)' base.yaml override.yaml → merge

  # Iterate over YAML from bash:
  yq '.services | keys | .[]' docker-compose.yml | while read -r svc; do
    echo "Service: $svc"
  done

CONCEPT: Working with AWS CLI in Scripts
------------------------------------------
  # Always set region and handle pagination:
  aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --region us-east-1 \
    --query 'Reservations[].Instances[].{ID:InstanceId,Name:Tags[?Key==`Name`]|[0].Value}' \
    --output json

  # Pagination (--no-paginate fetches all pages):
  aws s3api list-objects-v2 \
    --bucket my-bucket \
    --no-paginate \
    --query 'Contents[].Key' \
    --output text

  # Wait for AWS operations:
  aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids "$instance_id"

  # SSM Parameter Store for secrets (no hardcoded secrets):
  db_password=$(aws ssm get-parameter \
    --name "/prod/db/password" \
    --with-decryption \
    --query 'Parameter.Value' \
    --output text)

  # Handle AWS CLI errors:
  if ! aws s3 cp file.txt s3://bucket/; then
    die "S3 upload failed"
  fi

CONCEPT: Deployment Script Patterns
--------------------------------------
Blue-Green switch:
  deploy_and_switch() {
    local env="${1:?env required}"
    local image="${2:?image required}"

    info "Deploying $image to $env"
    kubectl set image deployment/app app="$image" -n "$env"
    kubectl rollout status deployment/app -n "$env" --timeout=300s \
      || { kubectl rollout undo deployment/app -n "$env"; die "Rollout failed"; }
    info "Deployment complete"
  }

Canary deploy check:
  check_error_rate() {
    local namespace="$1"
    local threshold=5  # 5% error rate

    error_rate=$(curl -sf "http://prometheus:9090/api/v1/query" \
      --data-urlencode 'query=rate(http_requests_total{status=~"5.."}[5m]) / rate(http_requests_total[5m]) * 100' \
      | jq -r '.data.result[0].value[1]' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")

    if (( $(echo "$error_rate > $threshold" | bc -l) )); then
      warn "Error rate ${error_rate}% exceeds threshold ${threshold}%"
      return 1
    fi
  }

Database migration with safety:
  run_migration() {
    local migration_file="$1"
    local db_name="${DB_NAME:?DB_NAME required}"

    # Backup first
    pg_dump "$db_name" > "/backups/${db_name}_$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S).sql" \
      || die "Backup failed — aborting migration"

    # Run migration in transaction
    psql "$db_name" <<SQL
  BEGIN;
  \i $migration_file
  COMMIT;
  SQL
  }

CONCEPT: Advanced Debugging
-----------------------------
  bash -x script.sh                  → trace all commands (PS4 prefix)
  bash -v script.sh                  → verbose: print each line before executing
  bash -xv script.sh                 → both

  Customize PS4 for richer trace:
  export PS4='+(${BASH_SOURCE}:${LINENO}): ${FUNCNAME[0]:+${FUNCNAME[0]}(): }'
  Now trace output shows: +(deploy.sh:45): deploy(): kubectl apply ...

  shellcheck — static analysis for bash:
    shellcheck script.sh              → list all warnings/errors
    shellcheck -S error script.sh    → only errors
    # shellcheck disable=SC2086       → suppress specific warning inline

  Install: apt install shellcheck / brew install shellcheck
  Integrate with CI:
    - run: shellcheck $(find . -name "*.sh")

  Profiling bash scripts:
  # Add at the top of script:
  PS4='$(date +%s%N) '
  exec 3>&2 2>/tmp/bashstart.$$.log
  set -x
  # At end:
  set +x
  exec 2>&3 3>&-
  # Analyze: awk '...' /tmp/bashstart.$$.log

CONCEPT: Security-Hardened Scripts
------------------------------------
  # Validate ALL external input before use:
  validate_env() {
    case "$1" in
      dev|staging|production) return 0 ;;
      *) die "Invalid environment: $1 (must be: dev|staging|production)" ;;
    esac
  }

  # Never eval user input:
  # DANGEROUS: eval "$user_input"
  # SAFE: Use arrays, case statements, lookup tables

  # Avoid shell injection in variable expansion:
  # DANGEROUS: ls $dir              (word splits, glob expands)
  # SAFE:      ls -- "$dir"         (quoted, -- prevents flag injection)

  # Path traversal prevention:
  safe_path() {
    local path
    path=$(realpath -m "$1")    → resolve without requiring existence
    [[ "$path" == /allowed/base/* ]] || die "Path outside allowed dir: $path"
    echo "$path"
  }

  # Use read -r always:
  # Without -r: backslash is escape character
  # With -r: read literally

  # Restrict script to specific users:
  [[ "$(id -u)" -eq 0 ]] || die "Must run as root"
  [[ "$(id -un)" == "deploy" ]] || die "Must run as deploy user"

  # Mask sensitive values in xtrace:
  {
    set +x
    password="$SECRET_VALUE"  → this won't appear in trace
    set -x
  }

CONCEPT: CI/CD Integration Patterns
--------------------------------------
Scripts called by CI must:
  1. Exit with correct codes (0=success, 1-255=failure)
  2. Write structured output (parseable logs)
  3. Be idempotent (safe to re-run)
  4. Respect CI environment variables
  5. Handle CI-specific paths and tooling

  CI detection:
    [[ -n "${CI:-}" ]]          → generic CI flag
    [[ -n "${GITHUB_ACTIONS:-}" ]]
    [[ -n "${GITLAB_CI:-}" ]]
    [[ -n "${JENKINS_URL:-}" ]]

  GitHub Actions annotations from script:
    echo "::error file=app.js,line=10::Something went wrong"
    echo "::warning::This is a warning"
    echo "::notice::FYI"
    echo "::set-output name=version::1.2.3"  (deprecated)
    echo "version=1.2.3" >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"  (current)

  GitLab CI artifacts from script:
    # Write to GITLAB_STEP_SUMMARY equivalent via artifacts

REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS:
  SCENARIO A — Deploy script with zero downtime:
    1. Pull new image from ECR
    2. Run DB migrations (with backup)
    3. Deploy to staging, smoke test
    4. Deploy to production with canary (10% → 50% → 100%)
    5. Monitor error rate at each stage
    6. Auto-rollback if error rate exceeds threshold
    7. Send Slack notification on success/failure
    All implemented as a single idempotent bash script called by CI.

  SCENARIO B — Incident response script:
    On-call engineer runs: ./incident.sh diagnose --service api --env prod
    Script:
      1. Collects: pod logs, node stats, recent deployments, error rates
      2. Checks: disk space, memory, network connectivity
      3. Generates: incident-$timestamp.tar.gz with all artifacts
      4. Posts summary to Slack channel
    Reduces MTTD (mean time to detect root cause) from 20min to 2min.

  SCENARIO C — Infrastructure drift detection:
    Script runs on cron every hour:
      1. Query AWS for actual resource state (EC2, SGs, IAM policies)
      2. Compare against Terraform state file (terraform show -json)
      3. Report diffs (resources added/removed outside Terraform)
      4. Send alert if drift detected
    Prevents shadow IT and untracked infrastructure changes.

================================================================================
1. FOUNDATION — CI/CD Concepts (Tool-Agnostic)
================================================================================

CONCEPT: What CI/CD Actually Means in Production
--------------------------------------------------
Continuous Integration (CI):
  Developers integrate code into a shared repository frequently (multiple times
  per day). Each integration is verified by an automated build + test pipeline.
  Goal: detect integration bugs early, reduce "integration hell".

Continuous Delivery (CD):
  Every passing build is automatically deployable to production.
  A human approves the final release.

Continuous Deployment (CD):
  Every passing build is automatically deployed to production.
  No human gate. Requires high test coverage and confidence.

Pipeline stages (typical production pipeline):
  Source → Build → Test → Static Analysis → Security Scan →
  Package → Publish Artifact → Deploy to Staging → Integration Tests →
  Deploy to Production → Smoke Tests → Monitor

CONCEPT: Key CI/CD Principles
-------------------------------
  Fail fast:          Run fastest checks first (lint → unit → integration → e2e)
  Idempotent builds:  Same code always produces same artifact
  Immutable artifacts: Build once, promote through environments (never rebuild)
  Pipeline as code:   Pipelines defined in version-controlled files
  Separation:         Build, test, and deploy are distinct stages
  Secrets management: Secrets never in code; injected at runtime from vault
  Artifact versioning: Tag with git SHA, not "latest"

CONCEPT: Artifact Management
------------------------------
  Container images → Docker Registry (ECR, Docker Hub, GCR, Harbor)
  Java artifacts   → Nexus, Artifactory (Maven/Gradle)
  npm packages     → npm registry, Nexus
  Helm charts      → OCI registry, Chartmuseum
  Generic files    → S3, Artifactory, Nexus

  Tagging strategy:
    git-sha tag:   myapp:abc1234   → immutable, traceable
    semver tag:    myapp:v2.3.1    → human-readable release
    branch tag:    myapp:main-123  → branch builds (mutable)
    Never rely on: myapp:latest    → non-deterministic in prod

================================================================================
SECTION A: JENKINS
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Jenkins Architecture
-------------------------------
Jenkins is a self-hosted, open-source automation server.

Components:
  Controller (Master):
    - Orchestrates pipelines, stores config, schedules jobs
    - Runs on JVM; serves the web UI on port 8080
    - NEVER run builds on controller in production (security + stability)
    - Stores: $JENKINS_HOME (jobs, builds, configs, plugins, credentials)

  Agents (Nodes/Slaves):
    - Execute the actual build steps
    - Connect via JNLP (Java), SSH, or Kubernetes pod agents
    - Can be labeled: linux, windows, docker, gpu, high-mem
    - Ephemeral (Kubernetes pod agents) or persistent (EC2 instances)

  Executor:
    - A single build "slot" on an agent
    - An agent can have multiple executors (N parallel jobs)
    - Controller should have 0 executors in prod

Communication:
  Agent ← Controller: HTTP polling (agent initiates) OR SSH (controller initiates)
  Kubernetes agents: Jenkins spins up a pod per build, deletes after

CONCEPT: Jenkins Installation & Configuration
----------------------------------------------
  # Docker (for learning):
  docker run -p 8080:8080 -p 50000:50000 \
    -v jenkins_home:/var/jenkins_home jenkins/jenkins:lts

  # Production: use Jenkins Operator on Kubernetes OR official Helm chart
  helm repo add jenkins https://charts.jenkins.io
  helm install jenkins jenkins/jenkins -f values.yaml

  Critical configuration:
    - JENKINS_URL (Manage Jenkins → System)
    - Global Tool Config: JDK, Maven, NodeJS, Docker
    - Credentials store (Manage Jenkins → Credentials)
    - Number of executors on controller: 0
    - CSRF protection: enabled
    - Agent protocols: disable older JNLP1/2; keep JNLP4-connect
    - Install recommended plugins on first run

CONCEPT: Jenkins Plugins (Essential)
--------------------------------------
  Pipeline               → Declarative + Scripted pipeline support
  Git                    → Git SCM integration
  GitHub / GitLab        → Webhook triggers
  Credentials Binding    → Inject credentials into builds
  Docker Pipeline        → Build/push Docker images from pipeline
  Kubernetes             → Dynamic pod-based agents
  Blue Ocean             → Modern pipeline UI
  Build Timeout          → Kill hung builds
  Timestamper            → Add timestamps to console output
  Workspace Cleanup      → Clean workspace before/after builds
  JUnit                  → Parse test results
  HTML Publisher         → Publish HTML reports
  Slack Notification     → Send alerts to Slack
  Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) → Fine-grained permissions
  Job DSL                → Generate jobs programmatically

CONCEPT: Jenkinsfile — Declarative Pipeline
---------------------------------------------
Declarative pipeline (structured, opinionated, recommended):

  // Jenkinsfile
  pipeline {
    agent { label 'linux' }

    options {
      buildDiscarder(logRotator(numToKeepStr: '30'))
      timeout(time: 30, unit: 'MINUTES')
      disableConcurrentBuilds()
      timestamps()
    }

    environment {
      APP_NAME   = 'myapp'
      ECR_REPO   = '123456789.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/myapp'
      IMAGE_TAG  = "${env.GIT_COMMIT[0..7]}"
      AWS_REGION = 'us-east-1'
    }

    parameters {
      choice(name: 'DEPLOY_ENV', choices: ['staging', 'production'], description: 'Target env')
      booleanParam(name: 'SKIP_TESTS', defaultValue: false, description: 'Skip tests?')
    }

    triggers {
      pollSCM('H/5 * * * *')            // poll every 5 min (prefer webhooks)
      githubPush()                       // webhook trigger
      cron('H 2 * * 1')                  // every Monday at ~2 AM
    }

    stages {
      stage('Checkout') {
        steps {
          checkout scm
          sh 'git log --oneline -5'
        }
      }

      stage('Build') {
        steps {
          sh 'docker build -t ${ECR_REPO}:${IMAGE_TAG} .'
        }
      }

      stage('Test') {
        when { not { expression { params.SKIP_TESTS } } }
        steps {
          sh 'go test ./... -v -coverprofile=coverage.out'
          sh 'go tool cover -html=coverage.out -o coverage.html'
        }
        post {
          always {
            junit 'test-results/*.xml'
            publishHTML(target: [reportDir: '.', reportFiles: 'coverage.html', reportName: 'Coverage'])
          }
        }
      }

      stage('Security Scan') {
        steps {
          sh 'trivy image --exit-code 1 --severity HIGH,CRITICAL ${ECR_REPO}:${IMAGE_TAG}'
        }
      }

      stage('Push') {
        steps {
          withCredentials([[$class: 'AmazonWebServicesCredentialsBinding',
                            credentialsId: 'aws-ecr-creds']]) {
            sh '''
              aws ecr get-login-password --region ${AWS_REGION} | \
                docker login --username AWS --password-stdin ${ECR_REPO%/*}
              docker push ${ECR_REPO}:${IMAGE_TAG}
            '''
          }
        }
      }

      stage('Deploy Staging') {
        when { branch 'main' }
        steps {
          sh 'kubectl set image deployment/${APP_NAME} ${APP_NAME}=${ECR_REPO}:${IMAGE_TAG} -n staging'
          sh 'kubectl rollout status deployment/${APP_NAME} -n staging --timeout=5m'
        }
      }

      stage('Deploy Production') {
        when {
          allOf {
            branch 'main'
            expression { params.DEPLOY_ENV == 'production' }
          }
        }
        input {
          message 'Deploy to PRODUCTION?'
          ok 'Yes, deploy!'
          submitter 'admin,release-team'
        }
        steps {
          sh 'kubectl set image deployment/${APP_NAME} ${APP_NAME}=${ECR_REPO}:${IMAGE_TAG} -n production'
          sh 'kubectl rollout status deployment/${APP_NAME} -n production --timeout=10m'
        }
      }
    }

    post {
      success { slackSend color: 'good', message: "BUILD OK: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}" }
      failure { slackSend color: 'danger', message: "BUILD FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}" }
      always  { cleanWs() }
    }
  }

CONCEPT: Scripted Pipeline (Groovy)
--------------------------------------
Scripted pipeline gives full Groovy power when declarative is insufficient:

  // Jenkinsfile (Scripted)
  node('linux') {
    def image
    def gitSha = ''

    try {
      stage('Checkout') {
        checkout scm
        gitSha = sh(script: 'git rev-parse --short HEAD', returnStdout: true).trim()
      }

      stage('Build') {
        image = docker.build("myapp:${gitSha}")
      }

      stage('Test') {
        image.inside('-v /tmp:/tmp') {
          sh 'make test'
        }
      }

      stage('Push') {
        docker.withRegistry('https://registry.example.com', 'registry-creds') {
          image.push(gitSha)
          image.push('latest')
        }
      }

      currentBuild.result = 'SUCCESS'
    } catch (err) {
      currentBuild.result = 'FAILURE'
      throw err
    } finally {
      cleanWs()
      if (currentBuild.result == 'FAILURE') {
        emailext to: 'team@example.com', subject: "FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME}"
      }
    }
  }

CONCEPT: Shared Libraries
---------------------------
Centralize reusable pipeline code. Stored in a separate Git repo.

Structure:
  jenkins-shared-lib/
  ├── vars/
  │   ├── dockerBuild.groovy      → global variable (single function)
  │   ├── deployToK8s.groovy
  │   └── slackNotify.groovy
  ├── src/
  │   └── com/company/
  │       └── PipelineUtils.groovy → class-based utilities
  └── resources/
      └── scripts/
          └── init.sh

  // vars/dockerBuild.groovy
  def call(Map config) {
    def tag = config.tag ?: env.GIT_COMMIT[0..7]
    def repo = config.repo ?: error("repo is required")
    sh "docker build -t ${repo}:${tag} ."
    return tag
  }

  // Usage in Jenkinsfile (after loading library):
  @Library('jenkins-shared-lib@main') _
  pipeline {
    stages {
      stage('Build') {
        steps {
          script {
            dockerBuild(repo: 'myapp', tag: env.GIT_COMMIT[0..7])
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }

  Register in Jenkins: Manage Jenkins → System → Global Pipeline Libraries

CONCEPT: Kubernetes Pod Agents
--------------------------------
Define build environment as a YAML pod spec — ephemeral, no persistent agents:

  pipeline {
    agent {
      kubernetes {
        yaml """
  apiVersion: v1
  kind: Pod
  spec:
    serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
    containers:
    - name: jnlp
      image: jenkins/inbound-agent:latest
      resources:
        requests: { cpu: '200m', memory: '256Mi' }
        limits:   { cpu: '500m', memory: '512Mi' }
    - name: docker
      image: docker:24-dind
      securityContext:
        privileged: true
      env:
      - name: DOCKER_TLS_CERTDIR
        value: ""
    - name: kubectl
      image: bitnami/kubectl:latest
      command: ['sleep', '9999']
  """
      }
    }
    stages {
      stage('Build') {
        steps {
          container('docker') {
            sh 'docker build -t myapp:latest .'
          }
        }
      }
      stage('Deploy') {
        steps {
          container('kubectl') {
            sh 'kubectl apply -f k8s/'
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }

CONCEPT: Jenkins Security
--------------------------
  Authentication:
    - LDAP / Active Directory integration
    - GitHub OAuth plugin
    - SAML 2.0 (Okta, Azure AD)
    - Local users (for service accounts only)

  Authorization (RBAC):
    - Role-Based Authorization Strategy plugin
    - Global roles: admin, developer, read-only
    - Item roles: per-folder or per-job permissions
    - Node roles: who can use which agent

  Credentials management:
    - Credentials Plugin → stores secrets encrypted in JENKINS_HOME
    - Types: Username/Password, Secret text, SSH key, Certificate, AWS
    - Scope: Global, System (controller only), Folder (scoped to folder)
    - NEVER pass credentials as pipeline parameters (visible in logs)
    - Use: withCredentials([...]) { } block

  Hardening:
    - Enable CSRF protection (crumb)
    - Disable script console access for non-admins
    - Use HTTPS (put nginx/ALB in front)
    - Restrict agent-to-controller access
    - Set JAVA_OPTS: -Djenkins.model.Jenkins.buildsDir=...
    - Keep Jenkins and plugins updated
    - Script Security plugin (sandbox for scripts)

CONCEPT: Jenkins as Code — JCasC
----------------------------------
Jenkins Configuration as Code plugin: configure Jenkins from YAML.

  # jenkins.yaml
  jenkins:
    numExecutors: 0
    agentProtocols: ["JNLP4-connect"]
    securityRealm:
      ldap:
        configurations:
          - server: ldap://ldap.company.com
            rootDN: dc=company,dc=com
    authorizationStrategy:
      roleBased:
        roles:
          global:
            - name: admin
              permissions: ["Overall/Administer"]
    globalLibraries:
      libraries:
        - name: jenkins-shared-lib
          defaultVersion: main
          retriever:
            modernSCM:
              scm:
                git:
                  remote: https://github.com/org/jenkins-shared-lib.git

  credentials:
    system:
      domainCredentials:
        - credentials:
            - basicSSHUserPrivateKey:
                id: github-deploy-key
                privateKeySource:
                  directEntry:
                    privateKey: ${GITHUB_DEPLOY_KEY}

  Mount YAML as ConfigMap in Kubernetes, Jenkins auto-applies on boot.

HANDS-ON TASKS (Jenkins):
  1. Install Jenkins in Docker, configure first agent via JNLP
  2. Write a declarative Jenkinsfile with 6 stages + post actions
  3. Set up a Kubernetes pod agent with Docker-in-Docker
  4. Create a shared library with a reusable Docker build function
  5. Configure RBAC: admin, developer, read-only roles
  6. Use JCasC to define entire Jenkins config as YAML

================================================================================
SECTION B: GITLAB CI
================================================================================

CONCEPT: GitLab CI Architecture
---------------------------------
GitLab CI is deeply integrated into GitLab. No separate server needed.

Components:
  GitLab Instance   → stores code, runs the CI/CD coordinator
  GitLab Runner     → executes jobs; registered with GitLab via token
  .gitlab-ci.yml    → pipeline definition in the repository root

Runner executors:
  shell      → jobs run directly on runner's OS
  docker     → each job in a fresh Docker container (recommended)
  kubernetes → each job in a Kubernetes pod (production standard)
  docker+machine → auto-scale EC2/GCP instances (legacy; use K8s)

Runner scope:
  Shared runners   → available to all projects (GitLab SaaS provides these)
  Group runners    → available to all projects in a group
  Project runners  → dedicated to a specific project

CONCEPT: .gitlab-ci.yml — Complete Reference
----------------------------------------------

  # Global defaults
  default:
    image: alpine:3.18
    tags: [linux, docker]
    before_script:
      - apk add --no-cache curl
    retry:
      max: 2
      when: [runner_system_failure, stuck_or_timeout_failure]

  variables:
    APP_NAME: myapp
    IMAGE_TAG: $CI_COMMIT_SHORT_SHA
    ECR_REGISTRY: 123456789.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com

  stages:
    - validate
    - build
    - test
    - security
    - publish
    - deploy-staging
    - integration-test
    - deploy-production

  # ─── VALIDATE ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  lint:
    stage: validate
    image: golangci/golangci-lint:v1.55
    script:
      - golangci-lint run ./...
    rules:
      - if: $CI_MERGE_REQUEST_ID
      - if: $CI_COMMIT_BRANCH == $CI_DEFAULT_BRANCH

  # ─── BUILD ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  build-image:
    stage: build
    image: docker:24
    services:
      - docker:24-dind
    variables:
      DOCKER_TLS_CERTDIR: "/certs"
    before_script:
      - docker login -u $CI_REGISTRY_USER -p $CI_REGISTRY_PASSWORD $CI_REGISTRY
    script:
      - docker build -t $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:$IMAGE_TAG -t $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:latest .
      - docker push $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:$IMAGE_TAG
      - docker push $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:latest
    rules:
      - if: $CI_COMMIT_BRANCH == $CI_DEFAULT_BRANCH

  # ─── TEST ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  unit-tests:
    stage: test
    image: golang:1.21
    services:
      - name: postgres:15
        alias: db
        variables:
          POSTGRES_DB: testdb
          POSTGRES_USER: test
          POSTGRES_PASSWORD: test
    variables:
      DATABASE_URL: postgresql://test:test@db:5432/testdb
    script:
      - go test ./... -v -coverprofile=coverage.out
      - go tool cover -func=coverage.out
    coverage: '/total:\s+\(statements\)\s+(\d+\.\d+)%/'
    artifacts:
      when: always
      reports:
        junit: test-results.xml
        coverage_report:
          coverage_format: cobertura
          path: coverage.xml
      paths:
        - coverage.out
      expire_in: 1 week

  # ─── SECURITY ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  trivy-scan:
    stage: security
    image: aquasec/trivy:latest
    script:
      - trivy image --exit-code 1 --severity HIGH,CRITICAL
          --no-progress $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:$IMAGE_TAG
    allow_failure: false

  sast:
    stage: security
    include:
      - template: Security/SAST.gitlab-ci.yml

  # ─── DEPLOY STAGING ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  deploy-staging:
    stage: deploy-staging
    image: bitnami/kubectl:latest
    environment:
      name: staging
      url: https://staging.myapp.example.com
      on_stop: stop-staging
    script:
      - kubectl set image deployment/$APP_NAME $APP_NAME=$CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:$IMAGE_TAG -n staging
      - kubectl rollout status deployment/$APP_NAME -n staging --timeout=5m
    rules:
      - if: $CI_COMMIT_BRANCH == $CI_DEFAULT_BRANCH

  stop-staging:
    stage: deploy-staging
    script:
      - kubectl scale deployment/$APP_NAME --replicas=0 -n staging
    environment:
      name: staging
      action: stop
    when: manual

  # ─── DEPLOY PRODUCTION ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  deploy-production:
    stage: deploy-production
    image: bitnami/kubectl:latest
    environment:
      name: production
      url: https://myapp.example.com
    script:
      - kubectl set image deployment/$APP_NAME $APP_NAME=$CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE:$IMAGE_TAG -n production
      - kubectl rollout status deployment/$APP_NAME -n production --timeout=10m
    rules:
      - if: $CI_COMMIT_BRANCH == $CI_DEFAULT_BRANCH
        when: manual
    allow_failure: false

CONCEPT: GitLab CI Rules & Conditions
----------------------------------------
rules replace (and supersede) only/except. Evaluated top-down; first match wins.

  rules:
    - if: '$CI_COMMIT_TAG =~ /^v[0-9]+\.[0-9]+\.[0-9]+$/'
      when: on_success
    - if: '$CI_COMMIT_BRANCH == "main"'
      when: on_success
    - if: '$CI_MERGE_REQUEST_ID'
      changes:
        - src/**/*
        - Dockerfile
      when: on_success
    - when: never           → default: don't run

  when values:
    on_success   → default; run if previous stages passed
    on_failure   → run only if previous stage failed
    always       → run regardless (cleanup jobs)
    manual       → require manual trigger
    delayed      → run after a delay (start_in: '30 minutes')
    never        → don't run

  Predefined CI variables (key ones):
    $CI_COMMIT_SHA           → full commit SHA
    $CI_COMMIT_SHORT_SHA     → 8-char SHA
    $CI_COMMIT_BRANCH        → branch name
    $CI_COMMIT_TAG           → tag name (if building a tag)
    $CI_DEFAULT_BRANCH       → default branch (main/master)
    $CI_MERGE_REQUEST_ID     → set only for MR pipelines
    $CI_PIPELINE_SOURCE      → push/web/schedule/trigger/merge_request_event
    $CI_REGISTRY             → GitLab Container Registry URL
    $CI_REGISTRY_IMAGE       → image path (registry/namespace/project)
    $CI_REGISTRY_USER        → login user for registry
    $CI_REGISTRY_PASSWORD    → login password for registry
    $CI_PROJECT_DIR          → clone directory
    $CI_ENVIRONMENT_NAME     → current environment name

CONCEPT: Caching & Artifacts
------------------------------
Cache (shared between jobs/pipelines; speeds up builds):
  cache:
    key:
      files:
        - go.sum                 → cache key based on go.sum content
    paths:
      - .go-cache/
    policy: pull-push            → pull at start, push at end
                                   pull = download only; push = upload only

Artifacts (passed between stages in same pipeline; stored in GitLab):
  artifacts:
    paths:
      - bin/myapp
      - dist/
    reports:
      junit: test-results.xml
    expire_in: 1 week
    when: always

  Download artifacts in later job:
  deploy-job:
    needs:
      - job: build-job
        artifacts: true         → download artifacts from build-job

CONCEPT: needs & DAG Pipelines
---------------------------------
By default, all jobs in a stage wait for the previous stage to complete.
needs: creates a DAG (Directed Acyclic Graph) — jobs run as soon as
their dependencies are complete, regardless of stage ordering.

  unit-tests:
    stage: test
    needs: [build-image]    → runs as soon as build-image passes

  integration-tests:
    stage: test
    needs: [build-image]    → runs in parallel with unit-tests

  deploy:
    stage: deploy
    needs:
      - unit-tests
      - integration-tests   → waits for BOTH, skips other test jobs

CONCEPT: GitLab Environments & Deployments
--------------------------------------------
  environment:
    name: production
    url: https://myapp.com
    kubernetes:
      namespace: production   → scope kubectl to namespace

  GitLab tracks deployments in Environments section.
  Shows: current deployed SHA, deploy history, who deployed, rollback button.

  Protected environments:
    - Require specific users/groups to approve deployments
    - Required approvals count (e.g., 2 approvals for production)
    - Prevent unreviewed code reaching production

CONCEPT: GitLab Runner on Kubernetes
--------------------------------------
  # Register runner:
  helm repo add gitlab https://charts.gitlab.io
  helm install gitlab-runner gitlab/gitlab-runner \
    --set gitlabUrl=https://gitlab.example.com \
    --set runnerRegistrationToken=<token> \
    --set rbac.create=true \
    --set runners.executor=kubernetes \
    --set runners.namespace=gitlab-runners \
    --set runners.tags="k8s,linux"

  # Custom runner config (values.yaml):
  runners:
    config: |
      [[runners]]
        [runners.kubernetes]
          image = "alpine:3.18"
          pull_policy = "if-not-present"
          namespace = "gitlab-runners"
          service_account = "gitlab-runner"
          [runners.kubernetes.node_selector]
            "kubernetes.io/arch" = "amd64"
          [[runners.kubernetes.volumes.empty_dir]]
            name = "docker-certs"
            mount_path = "/certs/client"
            medium = "Memory"

CONCEPT: GitLab CI Security
-----------------------------
  Secret variables:
    Settings → CI/CD → Variables
    Types: Variable (env var), File (written to disk), masked, protected

    masked:    value hidden in job logs
    protected: only injected into protected branches/tags
    Combine masked + protected for prod secrets

  GitLab Secret Detection (SAST):
    include:
      - template: Security/Secret-Detection.gitlab-ci.yml

  Dependency Scanning:
    include:
      - template: Security/Dependency-Scanning.gitlab-ci.yml

  Container Scanning:
    include:
      - template: Security/Container-Scanning.gitlab-ci.yml

  All results appear in the MR security report widget.

HANDS-ON TASKS (GitLab CI):
  1. Write a full .gitlab-ci.yml with 8 stages for a Go microservice
  2. Configure caching for Go modules with go.sum-based cache key
  3. Use needs: to create a DAG pipeline (not sequential)
  4. Set up a protected environment for production with required approvals
  5. Install GitLab Runner on Kubernetes with pod executor
  6. Include all security scanning templates; review findings in MR

================================================================================
SECTION C: GITHUB ACTIONS
================================================================================

CONCEPT: GitHub Actions Architecture
---------------------------------------
GitHub Actions is GitHub's native CI/CD, deeply integrated with GitHub.

Components:
  Workflow      → YAML file in .github/workflows/; defines the automation
  Event         → trigger (push, PR, schedule, workflow_dispatch, etc.)
  Job           → group of steps running on ONE runner
  Step          → individual task (shell command or action)
  Action        → reusable unit (JavaScript, Docker, or composite)
  Runner        → machine executing jobs
                   GitHub-hosted: ubuntu-latest, windows-latest, macos-latest
                   Self-hosted: your own machines/pods

Job isolation:
  Each job runs on a fresh runner (no shared state between jobs by default).
  Data sharing between jobs → via artifacts or outputs.
  Steps within a job share the filesystem and environment.

CONCEPT: Workflow Triggers (Events)
--------------------------------------
  on:
    push:
      branches: [main, 'release/**']
      paths: ['src/**', 'Dockerfile']       → only trigger on these paths
      tags: ['v*']
    pull_request:
      branches: [main]
      types: [opened, synchronize, reopened]
    schedule:
      - cron: '0 2 * * 1'                   → every Monday at 2 AM UTC
    workflow_dispatch:                       → manual trigger
      inputs:
        environment:
          description: 'Target environment'
          required: true
          default: 'staging'
          type: choice
          options: [staging, production]
        debug:
          type: boolean
          default: false
    workflow_call:                           → called by another workflow
      inputs:
        image-tag: { required: true, type: string }
      secrets:
        deploy-token: { required: true }
    repository_dispatch:                    → triggered via API
      types: [deploy-event]
    release:
      types: [published]

CONCEPT: Complete Production Workflow
---------------------------------------

  # .github/workflows/ci-cd.yml
  name: CI/CD Pipeline

  on:
    push:
      branches: [main]
    pull_request:
      branches: [main]

  env:
    APP_NAME: myapp
    ECR_REGISTRY: 123456789.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com
    AWS_REGION: us-east-1

  jobs:
    # ── LINT ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    lint:
      name: Lint
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        - uses: actions/setup-go@v5
          with:
            go-version: '1.21'
            cache: true
        - uses: golangci/golangci-lint-action@v4
          with:
            version: v1.55

    # ── TEST ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    test:
      name: Test
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      services:
        postgres:
          image: postgres:15
          env:
            POSTGRES_DB: testdb
            POSTGRES_USER: test
            POSTGRES_PASSWORD: test
          ports: ['5432:5432']
          options: >-
            --health-cmd pg_isready
            --health-interval 10s
            --health-timeout 5s
            --health-retries 5
      steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        - uses: actions/setup-go@v5
          with:
            go-version: '1.21'
            cache: true
        - name: Run tests
          env:
            DATABASE_URL: postgresql://test:test@localhost:5432/testdb
          run: |
            go test ./... -v -coverprofile=coverage.out
        - name: Upload coverage
          uses: codecov/codecov-action@v4
          with:
            files: ./coverage.out

    # ── BUILD & PUSH ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    build:
      name: Build & Push
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      needs: [lint, test]
      if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
      outputs:
        image-tag: ${{ steps.meta.outputs.tags }}
        image-digest: ${{ steps.build.outputs.digest }}
      steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v4

        - name: Docker meta
          id: meta
          uses: docker/metadata-action@v5
          with:
            images: ${{ env.ECR_REGISTRY }}/${{ env.APP_NAME }}
            tags: |
              type=sha,prefix=,format=short
              type=ref,event=branch
              type=semver,pattern={{version}}

        - name: Configure AWS credentials
          uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v4
          with:
            role-to-assume: arn:aws:iam::123456789:role/github-actions-role
            aws-region: ${{ env.AWS_REGION }}

        - name: Login to ECR
          uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v2

        - name: Build and push
          id: build
          uses: docker/build-push-action@v5
          with:
            context: .
            push: true
            tags: ${{ steps.meta.outputs.tags }}
            labels: ${{ steps.meta.outputs.labels }}
            cache-from: type=gha
            cache-to: type=gha,mode=max

    # ── SECURITY ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    security:
      name: Security Scan
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      needs: [build]
      steps:
        - uses: aquasecurity/trivy-action@master
          with:
            image-ref: ${{ env.ECR_REGISTRY }}/${{ env.APP_NAME }}:${{ github.sha }}
            format: sarif
            output: trivy-results.sarif
            severity: HIGH,CRITICAL
            exit-code: '1'
        - uses: github/codeql-action/upload-sarif@v3
          with:
            sarif_file: trivy-results.sarif

    # ── DEPLOY STAGING ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    deploy-staging:
      name: Deploy to Staging
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      needs: [build, security]
      environment:
        name: staging
        url: https://staging.myapp.example.com
      steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        - name: Deploy
          run: |
            kubectl set image deployment/$APP_NAME \
              $APP_NAME=$ECR_REGISTRY/$APP_NAME:${{ github.sha }} \
              -n staging
            kubectl rollout status deployment/$APP_NAME -n staging --timeout=5m

    # ── DEPLOY PRODUCTION ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    deploy-production:
      name: Deploy to Production
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      needs: [deploy-staging]
      environment:
        name: production
        url: https://myapp.example.com
      steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        - name: Deploy
          run: |
            kubectl set image deployment/$APP_NAME \
              $APP_NAME=$ECR_REGISTRY/$APP_NAME:${{ github.sha }} \
              -n production
            kubectl rollout status deployment/$APP_NAME -n production --timeout=10m

CONCEPT: Actions — Types & Creation
--------------------------------------
JavaScript Action:
  - Fastest (no container spin-up)
  - Uses @actions/core, @actions/github, @actions/exec
  action.yml:
    name: 'My Action'
    inputs:
      token: { required: true }
    outputs:
      result: { description: 'Output value' }
    runs:
      using: 'node20'
      main: 'dist/index.js'

Docker Action:
  - Full control over runtime environment
  - Slower (container startup)
  runs:
    using: 'docker'
    image: 'Dockerfile'
    args:
      - ${{ inputs.my-input }}

Composite Action:
  - Sequences of steps; reusable workflow logic without JS/Docker
  runs:
    using: 'composite'
    steps:
      - run: echo "step 1"
        shell: bash
      - uses: some/action@v1

CONCEPT: Contexts & Expressions
---------------------------------
  ${{ github.sha }}            → commit SHA
  ${{ github.ref }}            → full ref (refs/heads/main)
  ${{ github.ref_name }}       → branch or tag name
  ${{ github.actor }}          → user who triggered
  ${{ github.repository }}     → owner/repo
  ${{ github.event_name }}     → push/pull_request/etc
  ${{ github.run_id }}         → unique run ID
  ${{ github.run_number }}     → sequential run number
  ${{ secrets.MY_SECRET }}     → org/repo secret
  ${{ vars.MY_VAR }}           → configuration variable (not secret)
  ${{ env.MY_ENV }}            → environment variable
  ${{ inputs.my-input }}       → workflow_dispatch/workflow_call input
  ${{ job.status }}            → success/failure/cancelled
  ${{ steps.step-id.outputs.key }} → output from a step
  ${{ needs.job-id.outputs.key }}  → output from a job

  Conditional expressions:
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    if: contains(github.event.pull_request.labels.*.name, 'deploy')
    if: startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')
    if: always()               → run even if previous steps failed
    if: failure()              → run only on failure
    if: cancelled()

CONCEPT: Secrets & OIDC
-------------------------
Repository secrets: Settings → Secrets → Actions
  ${{ secrets.MY_SECRET }}   → injected as env var; masked in logs

Environment secrets: scoped to specific environments (staging/production)
  Require environment protection rules (required reviewers, wait timer)

OIDC (OpenID Connect) — keyless cloud auth (production standard):
  GitHub Actions can assume AWS/GCP/Azure roles WITHOUT storing cloud
  credentials as secrets. Uses short-lived OIDC tokens.

  AWS setup:
    1. Create IAM Identity Provider (OIDC) in AWS for GitHub
    2. Create IAM Role with trust policy:
       {
         "Principal": { "Federated": "arn:aws:iam::123:oidc-provider/token.actions.githubusercontent.com" },
         "Condition": {
           "StringEquals": { "token.actions.githubusercontent.com:sub": "repo:org/repo:ref:refs/heads/main" }
         }
       }
    3. In workflow:
       permissions:
         id-token: write
         contents: read
       steps:
         - uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v4
           with:
             role-to-assume: arn:aws:iam::123:role/github-actions-role
             aws-region: us-east-1
  No long-lived credentials stored. Token expires after job.

CONCEPT: Reusable Workflows
-----------------------------
Define once, call from multiple workflows:

  # .github/workflows/deploy.yml (reusable)
  on:
    workflow_call:
      inputs:
        environment: { required: true, type: string }
        image-tag:   { required: true, type: string }
      secrets:
        deploy-token: { required: true }
  jobs:
    deploy:
      runs-on: ubuntu-latest
      steps:
        - run: deploy.sh ${{ inputs.environment }} ${{ inputs.image-tag }}
          env:
            TOKEN: ${{ secrets.deploy-token }}

  # Caller workflow:
  jobs:
    deploy-staging:
      uses: ./.github/workflows/deploy.yml
      with:
        environment: staging
        image-tag: ${{ needs.build.outputs.tag }}
      secrets:
        deploy-token: ${{ secrets.DEPLOY_TOKEN }}

CONCEPT: Matrix Builds
------------------------
  jobs:
    test:
      strategy:
        fail-fast: false         → don't cancel others if one fails
        matrix:
          os: [ubuntu-latest, macos-latest, windows-latest]
          go-version: ['1.20', '1.21']
          exclude:
            - os: windows-latest
              go-version: '1.20'
          include:
            - os: ubuntu-latest
              go-version: '1.21'
              run-extra: true
      runs-on: ${{ matrix.os }}
      steps:
        - uses: actions/setup-go@v5
          with:
            go-version: ${{ matrix.go-version }}
        - run: go test ./...
        - if: matrix.run-extra
          run: make extra-tests

CONCEPT: Self-Hosted Runners
------------------------------
  # Register runner:
  mkdir actions-runner && cd actions-runner
  curl -o actions-runner-linux-x64.tar.gz -L <url>
  tar xzf ./actions-runner-linux-x64.tar.gz
  ./config.sh --url https://github.com/org/repo --token <TOKEN>
  ./svc.sh install && ./svc.sh start

  # Kubernetes (Actions Runner Controller — ARC):
  helm install arc \
    oci://ghcr.io/actions/actions-runner-controller-charts/gha-runner-scale-set-controller

  # Scale set (auto-scales 0 → N runners on demand):
  helm install arc-runner-set \
    oci://ghcr.io/actions/actions-runner-controller-charts/gha-runner-scale-set \
    --set githubConfigUrl=https://github.com/org/repo \
    --set githubConfigSecret.github_token=<PAT>

  Runner groups: isolate runners for specific repos or orgs
  Labels: runs-on: [self-hosted, linux, arm64, high-memory]

CONCEPT: GitHub Actions Security
----------------------------------
  Permissions (least privilege per job):
    permissions:
      contents: read
      id-token: write
      pull-requests: write
      packages: write

  Pin actions to SHA (not tag — tags can be moved):
    uses: actions/checkout@11bd71901bbe5b1630ceea73d27597364c9af683  # v4.2.2

  Dependabot for action updates:
    # .github/dependabot.yml
    updates:
      - package-ecosystem: github-actions
        directory: /
        schedule: { interval: weekly }

  Prevent script injection (user input in run:):
    DANGEROUS:
      run: echo "${{ github.event.pull_request.title }}"  → injection risk
    SAFE:
      env:
        PR_TITLE: ${{ github.event.pull_request.title }}
      run: echo "$PR_TITLE"                               → env var, not inline

  Third-party actions: review source before use; prefer official/verified
  GITHUB_TOKEN permissions: set minimum required per workflow

HANDS-ON TASKS (GitHub Actions):
  1. Build a full CI/CD workflow (lint → test → build → push → deploy)
  2. Set up OIDC for keyless AWS credential authentication
  3. Create a matrix build testing 3 OS × 2 language versions
  4. Write a reusable workflow; call it from 2 different workflows
  5. Create a composite action that wraps your Docker build + push steps
  6. Set up Actions Runner Controller on Kubernetes with auto-scaling
  7. Pin all actions to SHA; configure Dependabot for action updates
  8. Implement an environment with required reviewers for production

================================================================================
ADVANCED CI/CD PATTERNS (Across All Tools)
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Build Caching Strategies
-----------------------------------
  Docker layer caching:
    - Order Dockerfile from least to most frequently changed
    - COPY go.mod go.sum . && RUN go mod download  → before COPY . .
    - Use BuildKit cache mounts:
        RUN --mount=type=cache,target=/go/pkg/mod go build .

  GitHub Actions cache:
    - actions/cache: cache ~/.go/pkg/mod by go.sum hash
    - docker/build-push-action: cache-from/to: type=gha

  GitLab CI cache:
    - cache: key based on go.sum; paths: vendor/ or .go-cache/

  Jenkins cache:
    - Use shared NFS or S3-backed workspace; or mount cache volumes on K8s agents

CONCEPT: Artifact Promotion Pattern
--------------------------------------
Build ONCE. Promote the same immutable artifact through environments.
Never rebuild for prod — always deploy the artifact that passed staging tests.

  Pipeline:
    1. Build → tag with git SHA → push to registry
    2. Deploy SHA to dev → run dev tests
    3. Deploy SAME SHA to staging → run staging tests
    4. Deploy SAME SHA to production
    Optionally: re-tag with semver on production deploy

CONCEPT: Pipeline Notifications
----------------------------------
  Slack:
    - Jenkins: Slack Notification plugin
    - GitLab: Integrations → Slack webhook
    - GitHub Actions: slackapi/slack-github-action

  Notification content (what matters):
    - Service name, environment, commit SHA, deploy status
    - Link to pipeline run, link to commit
    - Who triggered
    - Duration

  Alert on: failure, recovery (first success after failure), deployment

CONCEPT: Dynamic Pipelines / Pipeline Generation
--------------------------------------------------
  GitLab CI: child pipelines
    generate-pipeline:
      script:
        - generate-ci-yaml.sh > generated-pipeline.yml
      artifacts:
        paths: [generated-pipeline.yml]

    trigger-child:
      trigger:
        include:
          - artifact: generated-pipeline.yml
            job: generate-pipeline

  GitHub Actions: matrix from JSON output
    jobs:
      generate:
        outputs:
          matrix: ${{ steps.gen.outputs.matrix }}
        steps:
          - id: gen
            run: echo "matrix=$(cat matrix.json)" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
      build:
        needs: generate
        strategy:
          matrix: ${{ fromJson(needs.generate.outputs.matrix) }}

REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS:
  SCENARIO A — Monorepo with path-based triggers:
    On PR:
      - Detect changed paths with git diff
      - Only run CI for changed services
      - Use matrix to run N service pipelines in parallel
      - Post per-service status checks to the PR
    On merge to main:
      - Build and push all changed service images
      - Deploy only changed services to staging

  SCENARIO B — Rollback pipeline:
    Triggered manually with: target-version (git SHA or tag)
    Steps:
      1. Validate the target image exists in registry
      2. kubectl rollout undo OR kubectl set image to target SHA
      3. Wait for rollout
      4. Smoke test
      5. Notify Slack with who rolled back, from what version, to what

  SCENARIO C — Release pipeline with approvals:
    1. Nightly build generates release candidate
    2. Automated regression tests run
    3. On pass: Slack message to release-managers channel
    4. Human clicks "Approve" in GitHub/GitLab
    5. Pipeline promotes image to production registry
    6. Deploys to production
    7. Creates GitHub release with changelog (generated from Conventional Commits)
