MULTI-TENANCY:
  [ ] Namespace-based isolation
  [ ] vCluster
  [ ] Cluster API (CAPI)

================================================================================
END OF PHASE 6: KUBERNETES (EXTREMELY DEEP)
================================================================================
>>> WAITING FOR: "NEXT" TO PROCEED TO PHASE 7: SERVICE MESH (ISTIO)
================================================================================


################################################################################
#                    PHASE 7: SERVICE MESH — ISTIO                            #
################################################################################

================================================================================
1. FOUNDATION — What is a Service Mesh & Why Istio
================================================================================

CONCEPT: The Service Mesh Problem
-----------------------------------
In microservices, every service-to-service call needs:
  - Mutual TLS (encryption + identity verification)
  - Load balancing (beyond kube-proxy's simple round-robin)
  - Retries, timeouts, circuit breakers (resilience)
  - Traffic splitting (canary, blue-green, A/B)
  - Observability (distributed tracing, metrics, access logs)

Without a mesh: each team implements this logic in every service, in every
language. Inconsistent, error-prone, hard to audit.

With a service mesh: all of the above is handled by the mesh infrastructure,
transparently, without application code changes.

CONCEPT: How Istio Works — Sidecar Model
------------------------------------------
Traditional Istio injects an Envoy proxy sidecar into every pod.
All inbound and outbound traffic flows through the Envoy proxy.
The application never knows the proxy is there.

  [App Container] ←→ [Envoy Sidecar] ←→ Network ←→ [Envoy Sidecar] ←→ [App Container]

  Data Plane:   All Envoy proxies that handle actual traffic
  Control Plane: istiod — configures all Envoy proxies

istiod (single binary, replaces Pilot + Citadel + Galley in older versions):
  Pilot    → translates Istio config → Envoy xDS configuration
  Citadel  → certificate authority; issues mTLS certs to workloads via SPIFFE
  Galley   → config validation and distribution

xDS API (Envoy's discovery API):
  LDS → Listener Discovery Service   → what ports/protocols to listen on
  RDS → Route Discovery Service      → how to route requests
  CDS → Cluster Discovery Service    → upstream service definitions
  EDS → Endpoint Discovery Service   → individual pod IPs per cluster
  SDS → Secret Discovery Service     → TLS certificates
  ADS → Aggregated Discovery Service → single gRPC stream for all

CONCEPT: SPIFFE & SPIRE — Workload Identity
---------------------------------------------
SPIFFE (Secure Production Identity Framework For Everyone):
  Standard for workload identity in dynamic environments.
  Every workload gets a SPIFFE Verifiable Identity Document (SVID).
  SPIFFE ID format: spiffe://trust-domain/path
  Example: spiffe://cluster.local/ns/production/sa/api-service

  Istio's SPIFFE IDs are derived from ServiceAccount:
    spiffe://cluster.local/ns/<namespace>/sa/<serviceaccount>

  mTLS certificates contain the SPIFFE ID in the Subject Alternative Name (SAN).
  This enables identity-based (not IP-based) authorization.

CONCEPT: Istio Installation
-----------------------------
  # Using istioctl:
  curl -L https://istio.io/downloadIstio | sh -
  istioctl install --set profile=production -y

  Profiles:
    minimal    → only istiod (no ingress/egress gateways)
    default    → istiod + ingress gateway (for most use cases)
    demo       → all features enabled (for learning; not production-sized)
    production → minimal + production-tuned resource settings

  # Using Helm:
  helm install istio-base istio/base -n istio-system --create-namespace
  helm install istiod istio/istiod -n istio-system
  helm install istio-ingress istio/gateway -n istio-ingress --create-namespace

  # Enable sidecar injection per namespace:
  kubectl label namespace production istio-injection=enabled

  # Verify:
  istioctl verify-install
  istioctl analyze                     → check for config issues
  kubectl get pods -n istio-system

  # Inject manually (without namespace label):
  istioctl kube-inject -f deployment.yaml | kubectl apply -f -

HANDS-ON TASKS (Foundation):
  1. Install Istio with default profile on a local cluster
  2. Enable sidecar injection on a namespace; deploy a sample app
  3. Verify Envoy sidecar is injected: kubectl get pod -o jsonpath='{.spec.containers[*].name}'
  4. Use istioctl proxy-status → see xDS sync state of all proxies
  5. Use istioctl analyze → detect misconfiguration

================================================================================
2. CORE CONCEPTS — Traffic Management
================================================================================

CONCEPT: VirtualService
------------------------
VirtualService defines routing rules for traffic addressed to a service.
It decouples traffic routing from service endpoints.

  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: VirtualService
  metadata:
    name: myapp-vs
    namespace: production
  spec:
    hosts:
    - myapp                           → matches Kubernetes service name
    - myapp.production.svc.cluster.local
    - myapp.example.com               → external hostname (with gateway)
    gateways:
    - myapp-gateway                   → traffic from this gateway
    - mesh                            → internal mesh traffic (default)
    http:
    - name: canary-route
      match:
      - headers:
          x-canary:
            exact: "true"            → header match → send to v2
      - uri:
          prefix: /api/v2            → path prefix match
      route:
      - destination:
          host: myapp
          subset: v2
        weight: 100
    - name: main-route
      route:
      - destination:
          host: myapp
          subset: v1
        weight: 90
      - destination:
          host: myapp
          subset: v2
        weight: 10                   → 10% canary traffic
      timeout: 10s
      retries:
        attempts: 3
        perTryTimeout: 3s
        retryOn: gateway-error,connect-failure,retriable-4xx,5xx
      fault:
        delay:
          percentage:
            value: 5                 → inject 5% delay for chaos testing
          fixedDelay: 5s
        abort:
          percentage:
            value: 1                 → abort 1% of requests
          httpStatus: 503
      corsPolicy:
        allowOrigins:
        - exact: https://myapp.example.com
        allowMethods: [GET, POST, PUT, DELETE]
        allowHeaders: [Authorization, Content-Type]
        maxAge: 24h
      headers:
        request:
          add:
            x-request-start: "%START_TIME%"
          remove: [x-internal-secret]
        response:
          add:
            strict-transport-security: "max-age=31536000"

CONCEPT: DestinationRule
--------------------------
DestinationRule configures what happens AFTER routing decides the destination.
Defines subsets (versions), load balancing, connection pools, TLS settings.

  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: DestinationRule
  metadata:
    name: myapp-dr
    namespace: production
  spec:
    host: myapp
    trafficPolicy:
      connectionPool:
        http:
          http1MaxPendingRequests: 1024
          http2MaxRequests: 10000
          maxRequestsPerConnection: 100
          h2UpgradePolicy: UPGRADE     → upgrade to HTTP/2 if possible
        tcp:
          maxConnections: 1000
          connectTimeout: 30ms
          tcpKeepalive:
            time: 7200s
            interval: 75s
      loadBalancer:
        simple: LEAST_REQUEST          → ROUND_ROBIN/LEAST_REQUEST/RANDOM/PASSTHROUGH
      outlierDetection:                → circuit breaker (passive health checking)
        consecutive5xxErrors: 5        → eject after 5 consecutive 5xx
        interval: 30s                  → scan interval
        baseEjectionTime: 30s          → min ejection duration
        maxEjectionPercent: 50         → max 50% of hosts ejected
        splitExternalLocalOriginErrors: true
      tls:
        mode: ISTIO_MUTUAL             → use Istio's mTLS
    subsets:
    - name: v1
      labels:
        version: v1
      trafficPolicy:
        loadBalancer:
          simple: ROUND_ROBIN
    - name: v2
      labels:
        version: v2
      trafficPolicy:
        connectionPool:
          http:
            http2MaxRequests: 100      → subset-level override

  Load balancing algorithms:
    ROUND_ROBIN    → default; even distribution
    LEAST_REQUEST  → routes to host with fewest active requests
    RANDOM         → random; good for stateless high-throughput
    PASSTHROUGH    → bypass load balancing; connect directly

CONCEPT: Gateway
-----------------
Istio Gateway manages ingress/egress traffic at the mesh boundary.
It replaces the Kubernetes Ingress resource for mesh-managed clusters.

  # Ingress Gateway:
  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: Gateway
  metadata:
    name: myapp-gateway
    namespace: istio-ingress
  spec:
    selector:
      istio: ingressgateway            → selects the gateway pod
    servers:
    - port:
        number: 443
        name: https
        protocol: HTTPS
      tls:
        mode: SIMPLE                   → terminate TLS
        credentialName: myapp-tls     → K8s TLS secret in istio-ingress ns
      hosts:
      - "myapp.example.com"
    - port:
        number: 80
        name: http
        protocol: HTTP
      tls:
        httpsRedirect: true           → redirect all HTTP to HTTPS
      hosts:
      - "myapp.example.com"

  TLS modes on Gateway:
    PASSTHROUGH   → forward TLS to backend (SNI routing); backend terminates TLS
    SIMPLE        → gateway terminates TLS; backend receives plain HTTP
    MUTUAL        → gateway terminates mTLS (external clients with certs)
    ISTIO_MUTUAL  → use Istio's built-in mTLS

  Egress Gateway (control outbound traffic):
  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: Gateway
  metadata:
    name: egress-gateway
    namespace: istio-system
  spec:
    selector:
      istio: egressgateway
    servers:
    - port:
        number: 443
        name: https
        protocol: HTTPS
      tls:
        mode: PASSTHROUGH
      hosts:
      - api.external-service.com

CONCEPT: ServiceEntry
----------------------
ServiceEntry adds external services into the Istio service registry.
Without it: Envoy treats external traffic as "PassthroughCluster" (no policies apply).

  # Allow traffic to external API:
  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: ServiceEntry
  metadata:
    name: external-api
    namespace: production
  spec:
    hosts:
    - api.stripe.com
    ports:
    - number: 443
      name: https
      protocol: HTTPS
    location: MESH_EXTERNAL
    resolution: DNS

  # Block all external traffic by default (egress control):
  # Set: meshConfig.outboundTrafficPolicy.mode: REGISTRY_ONLY
  # Only explicitly registered external services are reachable.

  # ServiceEntry for VM workload (non-K8s):
  spec:
    hosts: [legacy-db.company.internal]
    ports:
    - number: 5432
      name: tcp-postgres
      protocol: TCP
    location: MESH_INTERNAL
    resolution: STATIC
    endpoints:
    - address: 10.0.50.100              → VM IP
      labels:
        version: legacy

HANDS-ON TASKS (Traffic Management):
  1. Deploy two versions of an app (v1, v2); split traffic 90/10
  2. Route canary traffic based on HTTP header
  3. Implement retries + timeouts on a VirtualService
  4. Inject faults (delay + abort) to test service resilience
  5. Configure circuit breaker with outlierDetection; trigger ejection
  6. Route to external service via ServiceEntry + EgressGateway

================================================================================
3. ADVANCED — Security, Observability, Advanced Traffic
================================================================================

CONCEPT: mTLS — Mutual TLS Deep Dive
---------------------------------------
mTLS provides:
  1. Encryption in transit (data cannot be intercepted)
  2. Service identity verification (prevents spoofing)
  3. No code changes required (transparent to applications)

How Istio mTLS works:
  1. istiod (Citadel) acts as CA; issues X.509 certs to each sidecar
  2. Certs contain SPIFFE ID (workload identity)
  3. Envoy sidecars handle TLS handshake transparently
  4. Applications communicate on localhost; Envoy handles mTLS externally

PeerAuthentication — configure mTLS mode per namespace/workload:

  # Strict mTLS for entire namespace:
  apiVersion: security.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: PeerAuthentication
  metadata:
    name: default
    namespace: production
  spec:
    mtls:
      mode: STRICT                     → reject all non-mTLS connections

  mTLS modes:
    PERMISSIVE → accept both mTLS and plain text (migration mode)
    STRICT     → only mTLS; reject plain text
    DISABLE    → no mTLS (not recommended)

  # Per-port exception:
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: myapp
    mtls:
      mode: STRICT
    portLevelMtls:
      8080:
        mode: PERMISSIVE               → allow plain HTTP on port 8080

  # Mesh-wide strict mTLS (apply to istio-system namespace):
  metadata:
    namespace: istio-system            → applies to entire mesh

  Verify mTLS:
    istioctl authn tls-check <pod> <service>
    kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- openssl s_client \
      -connect myservice:8080 -CAfile /var/run/secrets/istio/root-cert.pem

CONCEPT: Authorization Policy
--------------------------------
AuthorizationPolicy controls WHAT traffic is allowed between services.
Works at the application layer (L4 + L7). Replaces NetworkPolicy for mesh traffic.

  # Default deny all in namespace:
  apiVersion: security.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: AuthorizationPolicy
  metadata:
    name: deny-all
    namespace: production
  spec: {}                             → empty spec = deny all

  # Allow specific services:
  apiVersion: security.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: AuthorizationPolicy
  metadata:
    name: allow-api-to-db
    namespace: production
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: postgres
    action: ALLOW
    rules:
    - from:
      - source:
          principals:
          - cluster.local/ns/production/sa/api-service   → SPIFFE-based
          namespaces: [production]
      to:
      - operation:
          ports: ["5432"]

  # L7 policy (requires mTLS or JWT):
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: api
    action: ALLOW
    rules:
    - from:
      - source:
          principals: ["cluster.local/ns/production/sa/frontend"]
      to:
      - operation:
          methods: ["GET", "POST"]
          paths: ["/api/*"]
          notPaths: ["/api/admin/*"]
      when:
      - key: request.headers[x-request-id]
        notValues: [""]

  action values:
    ALLOW  → allow matching requests
    DENY   → deny matching requests (evaluated before ALLOW)
    AUDIT  → log matching requests (without affecting allow/deny)
    CUSTOM → delegate to external auth (OPA, etc.) via extensionProvider

  AuthorizationPolicy precedence:
    1. CUSTOM rules (external authz)
    2. DENY rules
    3. ALLOW rules (if no ALLOW rules: allow; if any: must match at least one)

CONCEPT: JWT Authentication (RequestAuthentication)
-----------------------------------------------------
Validate JWTs in incoming requests.

  apiVersion: security.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: RequestAuthentication
  metadata:
    name: jwt-auth
    namespace: production
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: api
    jwtRules:
    - issuer: "https://accounts.google.com"
      jwksUri: "https://www.googleapis.com/oauth2/v3/certs"
      audiences: ["myapp"]
      forwardOriginalToken: true       → pass JWT to backend
    - issuer: "https://auth.company.com"
      jwksUri: "https://auth.company.com/.well-known/jwks.json"
      outputClaimToHeaders:
      - header: x-user-id
        claim: sub                     → extract claim into header

  # AuthorizationPolicy to enforce JWT presence:
  spec:
    action: DENY
    rules:
    - from:
      - source:
          notRequestPrincipals: ["*"]  → deny if no valid JWT

CONCEPT: Istio Observability
------------------------------
Istio auto-generates metrics, traces, and access logs for all traffic.

Metrics (Prometheus):
  Standard metrics generated per service:
    istio_requests_total                    → request count by source, dest, code
    istio_request_duration_milliseconds     → latency histogram
    istio_request_bytes                     → request body size
    istio_response_bytes                    → response body size
    istio_tcp_connections_opened_total
    istio_tcp_connections_closed_total

  Labels: source_workload, destination_workload, response_code, reporter(source/destination)

  Useful PromQL:
    # Request rate:
    rate(istio_requests_total[5m])
    # Error rate:
    rate(istio_requests_total{response_code=~"5.."}[5m]) / rate(istio_requests_total[5m])
    # P99 latency:
    histogram_quantile(0.99, rate(istio_request_duration_milliseconds_bucket[5m]))

Distributed Tracing (Jaeger / Zipkin / Tempo):
  Envoy automatically propagates trace headers:
    x-request-id, x-b3-traceid, x-b3-spanid, x-b3-sampled
    traceparent (W3C Trace Context)

  IMPORTANT: Apps must forward these headers between service calls.
  Envoy creates spans; app must pass headers to next service.

  Configure sampling rate:
    meshConfig:
      defaultConfig:
        tracing:
          sampling: 1.0              → 1% sampling (production)
          zipkin:
            address: jaeger-collector:9411

Access Logs:
  Envoy generates access logs for every request:
    meshConfig:
      accessLogFile: /dev/stdout     → enable (disabled by default in production)
      accessLogFormat: |
        [%START_TIME%] "%REQ(:METHOD)% %REQ(X-ENVOY-ORIGINAL-PATH?:PATH)%
        %PROTOCOL%" %RESPONSE_CODE% %RESPONSE_FLAGS%
        %BYTES_RECEIVED% %BYTES_SENT% %DURATION%
        "%REQ(X-FORWARDED-FOR)%" "%REQ(USER-AGENT)%"
        "%REQ(X-REQUEST-ID)%" "%REQ(:AUTHORITY)%"
        "%UPSTREAM_HOST%"

  Response flags (critical for debugging):
    UH  → no healthy upstream
    UF  → upstream connection failure
    NR  → no route found
    NC  → upstream cluster not found
    RL  → rate limited
    URX → upstream retry exhausted
    DC  → downstream connection termination

Kiali (Service Mesh Observability UI):
  Visualizes service graph, traffic flows, health, configuration issues.
  Integrates with Prometheus + Grafana + Jaeger.

  kubectl apply -f https://raw.githubusercontent.com/istio/istio/release-1.20/samples/addons/kiali.yaml
  istioctl dashboard kiali

CONCEPT: Traffic Management — Advanced Patterns
------------------------------------------------
Session Affinity (consistent hashing):
  trafficPolicy:
    loadBalancer:
      consistentHash:
        httpCookie:
          name: session-cookie
          ttl: 86400s                  → hash on cookie value

  Alternatives: httpHeaderName, useSourceIp, minimumRingSize

Traffic Mirroring (dark launching):
  Send a copy of live traffic to a new version without affecting users.
  Mirror response is discarded; only primary response returned.

  http:
  - route:
    - destination:
        host: myapp
        subset: v1
    mirror:
      host: myapp
      subset: v2
    mirrorPercentage:
      value: 10.0                      → mirror 10% to v2

  Use case: validate v2 handles production traffic before routing users.

TCP traffic management:
  For non-HTTP services (databases, message brokers):
  spec:
    tcp:
    - match:
      - port: 5432
      route:
      - destination:
          host: postgres
          subset: primary
        weight: 100

Local Rate Limiting (per Envoy instance):
  apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
  kind: EnvoyFilter
  metadata:
    name: rate-limit
    namespace: production
  spec:
    workloadSelector:
      labels:
        app: api
    configPatches:
    - applyTo: HTTP_FILTER
      match:
        context: SIDECAR_INBOUND
        listener:
          filterChain:
            filter:
              name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager
      patch:
        operation: INSERT_BEFORE
        value:
          name: envoy.filters.http.local_ratelimit
          typed_config:
            "@type": type.googleapis.com/udpa.type.v1.TypedStruct
            type_url: type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.local_ratelimit.v3.LocalRateLimit
            value:
              stat_prefix: http_local_rate_limiter
              token_bucket:
                max_tokens: 100
                tokens_per_fill: 100
                fill_interval: 1s

EnvoyFilter:
  Low-level escape hatch to directly configure Envoy.
  Used for features not yet exposed in Istio API.
  Risky — bypasses Istio abstractions; use sparingly.
  applyTo: HTTP_FILTER, NETWORK_FILTER, LISTENER, CLUSTER, ROUTE_CONFIGURATION

CONCEPT: Multi-Cluster Istio
------------------------------
Istio can span multiple Kubernetes clusters for:
  - Geographic distribution
  - Fault isolation (cluster failure doesn't affect other clusters)
  - Cross-cluster service discovery

  Models:
    Single network, single control plane → clusters on same VPC; full mesh
    Multiple networks, single control plane → east-west gateway for cross-cluster
    Multiple control planes (replicated) → independent istiod per cluster; synced

  East-West Gateway:
    Special gateway that handles pod-to-pod traffic between clusters.
    Each cluster runs an east-west gateway; traffic tunneled between them.

  kubectl apply -f https://istio.io/samples/multicluster/east-west-gateway.yaml

HANDS-ON TASKS (Advanced):
  1. Enable strict mTLS mesh-wide; verify with istioctl authn tls-check
  2. Create AuthorizationPolicy: deny-all → allow specific service-to-service
  3. Implement JWT validation with RequestAuthentication + AuthorizationPolicy
  4. Set up Kiali + Prometheus + Jaeger; observe traces end-to-end
  5. Implement traffic mirroring for dark launch of v2
  6. Configure consistent hash load balancing on cookie
  7. Write an EnvoyFilter for custom request header manipulation
  8. Implement L7 rate limiting per-user using request headers

================================================================================
4. EXPERT LEVEL — Ambient Mesh, Debugging, Production Operations
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Ambient Mesh (Istio's New Architecture)
--------------------------------------------------
Sidecar model drawbacks:
  - Per-pod CPU/memory overhead (Envoy ~50-100MB per pod)
  - Restart required to inject sidecar
  - Operational complexity (sidecar upgrades require pod restarts)
  - Security boundary blurs container + sidecar

Ambient Mesh (stable in Istio 1.22+):
  Removes per-pod sidecar. Splits Envoy into two layers:

  Layer 1 — ztunnel (zero trust tunnel):
    - Per-node DaemonSet (NOT per pod)
    - Handles L4 mTLS + telemetry for ALL pods on the node
    - Very lightweight (<50MB per node vs per pod)
    - Provides: encryption, L4 AuthorizationPolicy, L4 telemetry

  Layer 2 — waypoint proxy (per-service-account, on-demand):
    - Full Envoy proxy; handles L7 features
    - Only deployed when L7 features are needed
    - Shared across all pods of a ServiceAccount

  Benefits:
    - 90%+ reduction in proxy resource usage
    - No sidecar injection → no pod restarts needed
    - Better isolation (ztunnel in kernel space via eBPF, not in pod)
    - Simpler operations

  Enable ambient mode:
    # Install with ambient profile:
    istioctl install --set profile=ambient

    # Enable for a namespace (no pod restart needed):
    kubectl label namespace production istio.io/dataplane-mode=ambient

    # Deploy waypoint for L7 features:
    istioctl waypoint apply --service-account api-sa -n production
    kubectl label service myapp istio.io/use-waypoint=waypoint

CONCEPT: Debugging Istio
--------------------------
istioctl tools:
  istioctl proxy-status                     → sync status of all proxies
  istioctl proxy-config all <pod>           → full Envoy config dump
  istioctl proxy-config listener <pod>      → listeners
  istioctl proxy-config route <pod>         → routes
  istioctl proxy-config cluster <pod>       → clusters (upstream services)
  istioctl proxy-config endpoint <pod>      → endpoints (pod IPs per cluster)
  istioctl proxy-config secret <pod>        → TLS certificates
  istioctl analyze -n production            → configuration issues
  istioctl experimental describe pod <pod>  → human-readable proxy summary
  istioctl dashboard envoy <pod>            → Envoy admin UI (port 15000)
  istioctl dashboard controlz               → istiod control UI

Envoy Admin API (port 15000 on sidecar):
  kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- curl localhost:15000/help
  kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- curl localhost:15000/stats | grep upstream
  kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- curl localhost:15000/clusters  → health of upstreams
  kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- curl localhost:15000/config_dump  → full Envoy config
  kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- curl -X POST localhost:15000/logging?level=debug

  Port semantics:
    15001  → Envoy outbound (traffic leaving the pod)
    15006  → Envoy inbound (traffic entering the pod)
    15008  → HBONE (ambient mesh tunneling)
    15090  → Prometheus metrics scrape
    15000  → Envoy admin (NOT exposed externally)
    15020  → Merged Prometheus metrics (Envoy + istiod)
    9080   → App port (arbitrary)

  iptables rules (how traffic is intercepted):
    kubectl exec -it <pod> -c istio-proxy -- iptables -t nat -L
    PREROUTING: redirect inbound → port 15006
    OUTPUT: redirect outbound → port 15001 (except from UID 1337 = Envoy itself)

Common issues + fixes:
  503 "no healthy upstream":
    → Check DestinationRule subsets match pod labels
    → istioctl proxy-config endpoint pod → are endpoints showing?
    → kubectl get endpoints myservice → is the service selecting pods?

  Connection refused / upstream connect failure:
    → Check if mTLS is configured on both sides (PeerAuthentication)
    → istioctl authn tls-check <pod> <service>
    → Is the sidecar injected? (PERMISSIVE allows both)

  RBAC denied (403):
    → Check AuthorizationPolicy; is source principal in the allow list?
    → Enable access logging to see exact denial reason + response flag

  Circuit breaker open (503 overflow):
    → istioctl proxy-config cluster pod → check ejected hosts count
    → Tune outlierDetection parameters or fix upstream service

CONCEPT: Istio Performance Tuning
-----------------------------------
  Resource requests for sidecars (mesh-wide default):
    meshConfig:
      defaultConfig:
        proxyMetadata: {}
        resources:
          requests:
            cpu: 10m
            memory: 40Mi
          limits:
            cpu: 2000m
            memory: 1Gi

  Per-pod override:
    annotations:
      sidecar.istio.io/proxyCPULimit: "500m"
      sidecar.istio.io/proxyMemoryLimit: "256Mi"
      sidecar.istio.io/proxyCPU: "10m"
      sidecar.istio.io/proxyMemory: "40Mi"

  Concurrency (Envoy worker threads):
    sidecar.istio.io/proxyConcurrency: "2"   → match app CPU limit

  Exclude ports from interception:
    traffic.sidecar.istio.io/excludeOutboundPorts: "3306,5432"  → bypass DB ports
    traffic.sidecar.istio.io/excludeInboundPorts: "9090"        → bypass metrics

  Protocol detection:
    Envoy auto-detects protocol (HTTP/TCP) with a delay.
    Set explicit protocol in Service spec to eliminate delay:
    ports:
    - port: 8080
      name: http                → name must start with protocol: http/grpc/tcp/tls/https/mongo/mysql

  Tracing overhead:
    Production: sampling 1% (1.0 in Istio config)
    High-traffic: 0.1% or less

CONCEPT: Istio Upgrades (In-Place & Canary)
---------------------------------------------
In-place upgrade:
  istioctl upgrade --set profile=default
  Upgrades istiod first; then restart pods to pick up new sidecar version.
  Risky: all traffic uses new Envoy immediately.

Canary upgrade (recommended for production):
  1. Install new Istio version with a different revision tag:
     istioctl install --revision=1-20 --set profile=default
  2. Label namespaces for the new revision:
     kubectl label namespace production istio.io/rev=1-20 istio-injection-
  3. Restart pods in that namespace (rolling restart):
     kubectl rollout restart deployment -n production
  4. Validate: check metrics, errors, proxy-status
  5. Migrate remaining namespaces progressively
  6. Uninstall old revision:
     istioctl uninstall --revision=1-19

  istioctl tag set stable --revision 1-20    → alias revision for easier management
  kubectl label namespace production istio.io/rev=stable

CONCEPT: Istio with External Authorization
--------------------------------------------
Delegate authorization decisions to an external service (OPA, custom authz).

  extensionProviders in meshConfig:
    - name: opa-authz
      envoyExtAuthzGrpc:
        service: opa.policy.svc.cluster.local
        port: 9191

  AuthorizationPolicy using CUSTOM action:
  apiVersion: security.istio.io/v1beta1
  kind: AuthorizationPolicy
  metadata:
    name: ext-authz
    namespace: production
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: api
    action: CUSTOM
    provider:
      name: opa-authz
    rules:
    - to:
      - operation:
          paths: ["/api/admin/*"]        → only external authz on admin paths

CONCEPT: Istio Production Checklist
--------------------------------------
  Security:
    [ ] Strict mTLS enabled mesh-wide (PeerAuthentication in istio-system)
    [ ] Default deny AuthorizationPolicy per namespace
    [ ] Explicit allow policies per service-to-service flow
    [ ] JWT validation on external-facing services
    [ ] Egress gateway with REGISTRY_ONLY outbound policy
    [ ] TLS on all Gateways (no plaintext external)
    [ ] Cert rotation tested (auto in Istio; 24h default rotation)

  Traffic:
    [ ] Retries configured (not on non-idempotent write operations)
    [ ] Timeouts set (never rely on defaults for production)
    [ ] Circuit breakers (outlierDetection) on all critical services
    [ ] PeerAuthentication for all namespaces
    [ ] VirtualService for all services with traffic splitting

  Observability:
    [ ] Prometheus scraping Istio metrics
    [ ] Grafana dashboards: Istio Service Dashboard, Istio Workload Dashboard
    [ ] Distributed tracing configured (sampling appropriate for load)
    [ ] Kiali for topology visualization
    [ ] Alerts: high error rate, high latency, circuit breaker open

  Operations:
    [ ] Canary upgrade strategy documented
    [ ] PodDisruptionBudget on istiod
    [ ] Resource limits on sidecars (prevent runaway memory)
    [ ] Exclude non-proxied ports (metrics, health endpoints)
    [ ] istioctl analyze in CI (catch config issues before deploy)

REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS:
  SCENARIO A — Migrating existing cluster to mTLS:
    1. Apply PeerAuthentication with PERMISSIVE mesh-wide
       → existing traffic continues; mTLS accepted where available
    2. Verify all services have sidecars injected
    3. Check istioctl authn tls-check for any services not using mTLS
    4. Fix remaining services (inject sidecars, fix DestinationRule TLS mode)
    5. Change PeerAuthentication to STRICT
    6. Monitor for errors (504s from services without sidecars)
    7. Enable default-deny AuthorizationPolicy namespace by namespace

  SCENARIO B — Debugging high error rate after deployment:
    1. kubectl get vs,dr,gw -n production → check config is deployed
    2. istioctl analyze -n production → any warnings?
    3. istioctl proxy-config route <new-pod> → is new subset in route table?
    4. istioctl proxy-config endpoint <pod> → is v2 subset populated?
    5. Check DestinationRule subset labels match new pod labels
    6. kubectl get endpoints myapp -n production → are pods selected?
    7. Enable debug logging on proxy: curl -X POST localhost:15000/logging?http=debug
    8. Tail access logs: kubectl logs <pod> -c istio-proxy | jq .
    Root cause 90% of the time: subset label mismatch in DestinationRule

  SCENARIO C — Zero-downtime canary rollout with Istio:
    Phase 1: Deploy v2 pods (0% traffic)
      kubectl apply -f deploy-v2.yaml
      VirtualService: v1=100%, v2=0%
    Phase 2: Route internal QA (header-based)
      VirtualService: x-canary: qa → v2; else → v1
    Phase 3: 5% traffic to v2
      Monitor: error rate, p99 latency, business metrics
    Phase 4: 25% → 50% → 100% progressively
      Automate with Argo Rollouts + Istio integration
    Phase 5: Remove v1 deployment + VirtualService weight config
    Rollback at any phase: set v2 weight to 0

################################################################################
#                      PHASE 8: GITOPS — ARGOCD                               #
################################################################################

================================================================================
1. FOUNDATION — GitOps Principles & ArgoCD Architecture
================================================================================

CONCEPT: GitOps — The Core Principles
---------------------------------------
GitOps is an operational framework where:
  1. The ENTIRE system state is declared in Git (single source of truth)
  2. Approved changes to Git are AUTOMATICALLY applied to the system
  3. Running state continuously reconciled against the desired Git state
  4. If the cluster drifts from Git → automatically corrected

Four GitOps Principles (OpenGitOps):
  1. Declarative:   Desired state expressed declaratively (YAML, Helm, Kustomize)
  2. Versioned:     Desired state stored in version control (immutable, auditable)
  3. Pulled:        Agents PULL changes; no push credentials into cluster
  4. Continuous:    Running agents detect + remediate drift continuously

Why pull-based (not push-based CI/CD):
  Push model: CI pipeline has cluster credentials; pushes changes.
    Risk: CI system has massive blast radius if compromised.
  Pull model: Agent in cluster pulls from Git; CI has no cluster access.
    Reduced attack surface; cluster credentials never leave the cluster.

GitOps vs Traditional CD:
  Traditional: Jenkins/GitHub Actions → kubectl apply → cluster (PUSH)
  GitOps:      Developer → git push → ArgoCD detects → applies (PULL)

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Architecture
------------------------------
ArgoCD is a declarative GitOps controller for Kubernetes.

Components:
  argocd-server
    - API server + gRPC server
    - Serves the web UI
    - Handles CLI requests (argocd CLI → argocd-server)
    - Handles webhook events from Git providers
    - Exposes: port 443 (HTTPS/gRPC-web), port 80 (HTTP redirect)

  argocd-repo-server
    - Clones Git repositories
    - Generates Kubernetes manifests (Helm, Kustomize, Jsonnet, plain YAML)
    - Caches rendered manifests
    - No K8s API access (security isolation)
    - Scales independently (CPU-intensive — rendering templates)

  argocd-application-controller
    - Watches live cluster state vs desired state
    - Compares and detects OutOfSync
    - Performs sync operations
    - Runs as StatefulSet (sharding support for many apps)

  argocd-dex-server
    - OpenID Connect provider / SSO bridge
    - Delegates to: GitHub, GitLab, LDAP, SAML, Okta, etc.

  argocd-redis
    - Cache layer for rendered manifests and cluster state
    - In-memory; not persistent (can be rebuilt)

  argocd-applicationset-controller
    - Manages ApplicationSet resources
    - Generates multiple Applications from a template + generators

  argocd-notifications-controller
    - Sends notifications on sync/health events
    - Integrations: Slack, PagerDuty, GitHub, GitLab, email

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Installation
------------------------------
  # Standard install:
  kubectl create namespace argocd
  kubectl apply -n argocd -f https://raw.githubusercontent.com/argoproj/argo-cd/stable/manifests/install.yaml

  # HA install (multiple replicas of all components):
  kubectl apply -n argocd -f https://raw.githubusercontent.com/argoproj/argo-cd/stable/manifests/ha/install.yaml

  # Helm install (recommended for production):
  helm repo add argo https://argoproj.github.io/argo-helm
  helm install argocd argo/argo-cd -n argocd --create-namespace \
    -f argocd-values.yaml

  # Initial admin password:
  kubectl -n argocd get secret argocd-initial-admin-secret \
    -o jsonpath='{.data.password}' | base64 -d

  # Port-forward UI:
  kubectl port-forward svc/argocd-server -n argocd 8080:443

  # Login with CLI:
  argocd login localhost:8080 --username admin --password <pass> --insecure

  # Change admin password:
  argocd account update-password

HANDS-ON TASKS (Foundation):
  1. Install ArgoCD with Helm; configure Ingress with TLS
  2. Log in via CLI; explore all argocd commands
  3. Connect a Git repository (HTTPS + SSH)
  4. Deploy a sample app; observe sync status in UI
  5. Manually edit a live Kubernetes resource; observe OutOfSync detection

================================================================================
2. CORE CONCEPTS — Applications, Sync, and Health
================================================================================

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Application — Full Spec
-----------------------------------------
  apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
  kind: Application
  metadata:
    name: myapp
    namespace: argocd
    finalizers:
    - resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io    → delete K8s resources on app deletion
  spec:
    project: production                          → ArgoCD project (RBAC boundary)
    source:
      repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
      targetRevision: main                       → branch, tag, or commit SHA
      path: apps/myapp/overlays/production       → path within repo
      # For Helm:
      chart: myapp
      helm:
        releaseName: myapp
        valueFiles: [values.yaml, values-prod.yaml]
        values: |
          image:
            tag: v1.2.3
        parameters:
        - name: replicaCount
          value: "3"
        ignoreMissingValueFiles: true
      # For Kustomize:
      kustomize:
        namePrefix: prod-
        images:
        - myapp=myregistry.com/myapp:v1.2.3      → image override
        commonLabels:
          env: production
    destination:
      server: https://kubernetes.default.svc     → in-cluster
      # OR for remote cluster:
      # server: https://k8s.production.example.com:6443
      namespace: production
    syncPolicy:
      automated:
        prune: true                              → delete resources removed from Git
        selfHeal: true                           → correct drift automatically
        allowEmpty: false                        → refuse to sync to empty state
      syncOptions:
      - CreateNamespace=true                     → auto-create destination namespace
      - PrunePropagationPolicy=foreground        → wait for dependent resources
      - PruneLast=true                           → prune after other resources synced
      - ApplyOutOfSyncOnly=true                  → only apply changed resources
      - RespectIgnoreDifferences=true
      - ServerSideApply=true                     → use server-side apply (K8s 1.16+)
      retry:
        limit: 5
        backoff:
          duration: 5s
          factor: 2
          maxDuration: 3m
    ignoreDifferences:
    - group: apps
      kind: Deployment
      jsonPointers:
      - /spec/replicas                           → ignore HPA-managed replica count
    - group: ""
      kind: Secret
      name: myapp-secret
      jsonPointers:
      - /data                                    → ignore externally managed secret data
    revisionHistoryLimit: 10
    info:
    - name: "Slack Channel"
      value: "#team-myapp"

CONCEPT: Sync Phases & Waves
------------------------------
ArgoCD processes resources in ordered waves during a sync.

  Sync Phases:
    PreSync   → run before applying resources (e.g., run DB migration Job)
    Sync      → apply the main resources
    PostSync  → run after all resources are healthy (e.g., smoke test Job)
    SyncFail  → run only if sync failed (e.g., notify on failure)

  Sync Waves (ordering within a phase):
    annotation: argocd.argoproj.io/sync-wave: "N"
    Lower number = synced first (default: 0)
    Resources in same wave applied simultaneously
    Next wave starts after ALL resources in current wave are healthy

  Example ordering:
    Wave -2: Namespace, RBAC         → infra first
    Wave -1: ConfigMap, Secret       → config before app
    Wave  0: Deployment, Service     → application (default)
    Wave  1: Ingress                 → routing after app is up
    Wave  2: Smoke test Job          → validate after everything ready

  # annotation on resource:
  metadata:
    annotations:
      argocd.argoproj.io/sync-wave: "-1"
      argocd.argoproj.io/hook: PreSync        → run as PreSync hook
      argocd.argoproj.io/hook-delete-policy: HookSucceeded  → delete after success

  Hook delete policies:
    HookSucceeded    → delete after hook succeeds
    HookFailed       → delete after hook fails
    BeforeHookCreation → delete before next sync creates it (prevents duplicates)

CONCEPT: Health Checks
------------------------
ArgoCD evaluates health of resources:

  Built-in health for: Deployment, ReplicaSet, StatefulSet, DaemonSet,
  Job, CronJob, Pod, Service, Ingress, PVC, HPA, etc.

  Health statuses:
    Healthy    → resource is ready + functioning
    Progressing → resource is being updated
    Degraded   → resource has failed (pod CrashLoopBackOff, etc.)
    Suspended  → resource is deliberately paused
    Missing    → resource exists in desired state but not in cluster
    Unknown    → health cannot be determined

  Custom health check (Lua script):
  # argocd-cm ConfigMap:
  resource.customizations.health.mycompany.io_MyResource: |
    hs = {}
    if obj.status ~= nil then
      if obj.status.ready == true then
        hs.status = "Healthy"
        hs.message = "Resource is ready"
      else
        hs.status = "Progressing"
        hs.message = "Resource is not yet ready"
      end
    end
    return hs

CONCEPT: Sync Strategies
--------------------------
  Manual sync:
    argocd app sync myapp
    argocd app sync myapp --force          → replace resources (delete + recreate)
    argocd app sync myapp --dry-run        → preview what would change
    argocd app sync myapp --resource apps:Deployment:myapp → sync specific resource
    argocd app sync myapp --prune         → also prune orphaned resources

  Automated sync (recommended for dev/staging; optional for prod):
    selfHeal: true  → sync when cluster state drifts from Git
    prune: true     → remove resources not in Git

    PRODUCTION PATTERN:
      dev/staging:    automated sync with selfHeal + prune
      production:     automated sync without selfHeal + manual approval gate
                      OR: fully manual sync via PR approval flow

  Sync Windows:
    Restrict when automated syncs can run:
    apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
    kind: AppProject
    spec:
      syncWindows:
      - kind: allow
        schedule: "10 1 * * *"            → cron: daily at 01:10
        duration: 1h
        applications: ['*']
        namespaces: ['production']
        clusters: ['*']
      - kind: deny
        schedule: "0 22 * * 5"            → every Friday 22:00
        duration: 48h                     → deny Friday night + weekend
        manualSync: false                 → still allow manual sync during window

CONCEPT: AppProject
--------------------
AppProject provides RBAC and deployment boundaries.

  apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
  kind: AppProject
  metadata:
    name: production
    namespace: argocd
  spec:
    description: Production workloads

    sourceRepos:
    - https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
    - https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami      → allow Helm repo
    - '*'                                       → allow any (not recommended)

    destinations:
    - namespace: production
      server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
    - namespace: istio-system
      server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
    - namespace: '*'
      server: https://k8s.prod-cluster.example.com

    clusterResourceWhitelist:
    - group: ''
      kind: Namespace
    - group: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
      kind: ClusterRole

    namespaceResourceBlacklist:
    - group: ''
      kind: ResourceQuota             → prevent apps from modifying quotas

    namespaceResourceWhitelist:
    - group: '*'
      kind: '*'                       → allow all namespace resources

    roles:
    - name: developer
      description: Developer access
      policies:
      - p, proj:production:developer, applications, get, production/*, allow
      - p, proj:production:developer, applications, sync, production/*, allow
      groups:
      - dev-team

    orphanedResources:
      warn: true                      → warn about K8s resources not tracked by any app
      ignore:
      - group: ''
        kind: ConfigMap
        name: kube-root-ca.crt

CONCEPT: Repository Configuration
------------------------------------
  # HTTPS with token:
  argocd repo add https://github.com/org/repo.git \
    --username git \
    --password <token>

  # SSH:
  argocd repo add git@github.com:org/repo.git \
    --ssh-private-key-path ~/.ssh/argocd-deploy-key

  # Helm OCI registry:
  argocd repo add registry-1.docker.io/org \
    --type helm \
    --name myrepo \
    --username myuser \
    --password mytoken \
    --enable-oci

  # Credentials template (apply to all repos in org):
  argocd repocreds add https://github.com/org/ \
    --username git --password <token>

  # In-cluster vs out-of-cluster:
  argocd cluster add <context-name>     → register external cluster
  # ArgoCD connects to external clusters via kubeconfig/ServiceAccount

HANDS-ON TASKS (Core):
  1. Create an Application deploying a Kustomize overlay
  2. Create an Application deploying a Helm chart with value overrides
  3. Configure sync waves: CRD → Namespace → Deployment → Ingress
  4. Create a PreSync hook for database migration
  5. Create an AppProject with source/destination restrictions + RBAC roles
  6. Configure sync windows to prevent weekend deployments
  7. Enable automated sync with selfHeal; manually edit a resource; observe correction

================================================================================
3. ADVANCED — App of Apps, ApplicationSet, Multi-Cluster
================================================================================

CONCEPT: App of Apps Pattern
------------------------------
Problem: how do you manage many ArgoCD Applications declaratively?
Solution: an "umbrella" Application that manages other Applications.

  Repository structure:
  k8s-configs/
  ├── apps/                              → App-of-Apps root
  │   ├── Chart.yaml
  │   ├── values.yaml
  │   └── templates/
  │       ├── myapp.yaml                 → Application manifest
  │       ├── postgres.yaml
  │       ├── redis.yaml
  │       └── monitoring.yaml
  ├── myapp/
  │   ├── base/
  │   └── overlays/
  │       ├── dev/
  │       ├── staging/
  │       └── production/
  └── postgres/

  # Root application (deployed once manually or via bootstrap):
  apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
  kind: Application
  metadata:
    name: root-app
    namespace: argocd
  spec:
    project: default
    source:
      repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
      targetRevision: main
      path: apps                         → Helm chart with Application templates
    destination:
      server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
      namespace: argocd                  → Applications live in argocd namespace
    syncPolicy:
      automated:
        prune: true
        selfHeal: true

  # apps/templates/myapp.yaml (child application):
  apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
  kind: Application
  metadata:
    name: myapp-production
    namespace: argocd
    finalizers:
    - resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io
  spec:
    project: production
    source:
      repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
      targetRevision: main
      path: myapp/overlays/production
    destination:
      server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
      namespace: production
    syncPolicy:
      automated:
        prune: true
        selfHeal: true

  Bootstrap flow:
    1. Admin: kubectl apply -f root-app.yaml  → single manual step
    2. ArgoCD syncs root-app → creates all child Applications
    3. ArgoCD syncs child Applications → deploys all workloads
    4. New app = add template to apps/ → commit → ArgoCD creates it automatically

CONCEPT: ApplicationSet — Templated Application Generation
------------------------------------------------------------
ApplicationSet generates multiple ArgoCD Applications from a single template
using generators. More powerful and flexible than App of Apps.

  apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
  kind: ApplicationSet
  metadata:
    name: myapp-all-envs
    namespace: argocd
  spec:
    generators:
    - list:
        elements:
        - env: dev
          cluster: https://k8s.dev.example.com
          ns: dev
        - env: staging
          cluster: https://k8s.staging.example.com
          ns: staging
        - env: production
          cluster: https://k8s.prod.example.com
          ns: production
    template:
      metadata:
        name: myapp-{{env}}
        namespace: argocd
      spec:
        project: "{{env}}"
        source:
          repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
          targetRevision: main
          path: myapp/overlays/{{env}}
        destination:
          server: "{{cluster}}"
          namespace: "{{ns}}"
        syncPolicy:
          automated:
            prune: true
            selfHeal: true

  Generators:
    List:       static list of parameter sets
    Cluster:    generates an Application per registered ArgoCD cluster
    Git:        generates per directory or per file in a Git repo
    Matrix:     combines two generators (cartesian product)
    Merge:      merges outputs of two generators
    SCMProvider: generates per repo in a GitHub/GitLab org/group
    PullRequest: generates per open PR (preview environments!)
    ClusterDecision: uses ClusterDecisionResource (multi-cluster tools)

  Git generator (per directory):
    - git:
        repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
        revision: main
        directories:
        - path: apps/*/overlays/production    → wildcard matching

  Git generator (per file — config-driven):
    - git:
        repoURL: https://github.com/org/k8s-configs.git
        revision: main
        files:
        - path: apps/**/config.json           → each file provides template vars
    # config.json:
    # { "appName": "myapp", "env": "production", "namespace": "prod" }

  PR Generator (ephemeral preview environments):
    - pullRequest:
        github:
          owner: org
          repo: k8s-configs
          appSecretName: github-token
          labels: [deploy-preview]            → only PRs with this label
    template:
      metadata:
        name: preview-{{number}}
      spec:
        source:
          targetRevision: "{{branch}}"        → build from PR branch
        destination:
          namespace: preview-{{number}}
        syncPolicy:
          automated: {}

  Progressive Sync (ApplicationSet with sync strategies):
    syncPolicy:
      applicationsSync: sync              → create + update + delete
      preserveResourcesOnDeletion: false
    strategy:
      type: RollingSync
      rollingSync:
        steps:
        - matchExpressions:
          - key: env
            operator: In
            values: [dev]
        - matchExpressions:
          - key: env
            operator: In
            values: [staging]
          maxUpdate: 1                    → one at a time
        - matchExpressions:
          - key: env
            operator: In
            values: [production]
          maxUpdate: 25%                  → max 25% of prod apps at once

CONCEPT: Multi-Cluster Management
------------------------------------
  Register clusters:
    argocd cluster add <context> --name prod-us-east1
    # Creates a ServiceAccount + ClusterRoleBinding in the target cluster
    # ArgoCD stores kubeconfig in argocd namespace secret

  Cluster secret (declarative registration):
    apiVersion: v1
    kind: Secret
    metadata:
      name: prod-cluster
      namespace: argocd
      labels:
        argocd.argoproj.io/secret-type: cluster
    type: Opaque
    stringData:
      name: prod-us-east1
      server: https://k8s.prod.example.com:6443
      config: |
        {
          "bearerToken": "<token>",
          "tlsClientConfig": {
            "caData": "<base64-ca-cert>"
          }
        }

  Cluster labels for ApplicationSet generators:
    kubectl label secret prod-cluster -n argocd env=production region=us-east1

    ApplicationSet cluster generator:
    - clusters:
        selector:
          matchLabels:
            env: production
            region: us-east1

  Hub-and-Spoke: one ArgoCD instance manages many clusters
  Multi-instance: one ArgoCD per cluster (federation via ApplicationSet)

  ArgoCD in a GitOps fleet:
    Management cluster: ArgoCD + observability + security tools
    Workload clusters: only application workloads
    ArgoCD manages workload clusters from the management cluster

CONCEPT: Image Updater
------------------------
Argocd Image Updater automatically updates image tags in Git when new images
are pushed to a registry.

  Install:
    helm install argocd-image-updater argo/argocd-image-updater -n argocd

  Annotations on Application:
    annotations:
      argocd-image-updater.argoproj.io/image-list: myapp=myregistry.com/myapp
      argocd-image-updater.argoproj.io/myapp.update-strategy: semver
      argocd-image-updater.argoproj.io/myapp.allow-tags: regexp:^v[0-9]+\.[0-9]+\.[0-9]+$
      argocd-image-updater.argoproj.io/write-back-method: git
      argocd-image-updater.argoproj.io/git-branch: main

  Update strategies:
    semver      → latest semver tag (respects major/minor/patch constraints)
    latest      → most recently pushed tag
    digest      → track a mutable tag by updating to its digest (SHA)
    name        → alphabetically latest tag

  Write-back methods:
    argocd     → uses argocd API to update Application directly (no Git commit)
    git        → commits updated image tag back to Git repo (true GitOps)

  Git write-back creates a commit like:
    "chore: update image myapp to v1.3.5 [ci skip]"

HANDS-ON TASKS (Advanced):
  1. Set up full App of Apps pattern; bootstrap cluster with single apply
  2. Create ApplicationSet with Git directory generator (one app per folder)
  3. Create ApplicationSet with PR generator for preview environments
  4. Register 3 clusters; create ApplicationSet deploying to all of them
  5. Set up ArgoCD Image Updater with git write-back strategy
  6. Implement progressive ApplicationSet rollout (dev → staging → production)

================================================================================
4. EXPERT LEVEL — RBAC, Security, Notifications, Production Operations
================================================================================

CONCEPT: ArgoCD RBAC
----------------------
ArgoCD uses Casbin for RBAC. Policies defined in argocd-rbac-cm ConfigMap.

  # argocd-rbac-cm
  policy.default: role:readonly         → default role for authenticated users

  policy.csv: |
    # Format: p, subject, resource, action, object, effect

    # Resources: applications, clusters, repositories, accounts, gpgkeys, logs
    # Actions: get, create, update, delete, sync, override, action, *
    # Object: project/application (or * for all)

    # Admin role (built-in):
    p, role:admin, applications, *, */*, allow
    p, role:admin, clusters, *, *, allow
    p, role:admin, repositories, *, *, allow

    # Developer role:
    p, role:developer, applications, get, */*, allow
    p, role:developer, applications, sync, production/*, allow
    p, role:developer, applications, sync, staging/*, allow
    p, role:developer, logs, get, */*, allow

    # Read-only role (built-in):
    p, role:readonly, applications, get, */*, allow
    p, role:readonly, clusters, get, *, allow

    # Project-scoped developer:
    p, proj:production:developer, applications, get, production/*, allow
    p, proj:production:developer, applications, sync, production/*, allow

    # Group → role mapping:
    g, dev-team, role:developer
    g, ops-team, role:admin
    g, readonly-users, role:readonly

    # User → role mapping:
    g, alice@example.com, role:admin
    g, bob@example.com, proj:production:developer

  scopes: '[groups, email]'            → JWT claims to use for group binding

CONCEPT: SSO Configuration
----------------------------
  # argocd-cm ConfigMap — Dex config:
  dex.config: |
    connectors:
    - type: github
      id: github
      name: GitHub
      config:
        clientID: $dex.github.clientID      → reference a secret
        clientSecret: $dex.github.clientSecret
        orgs:
        - name: myorg
          teams:
          - platform-team
          - dev-team

    - type: saml
      id: okta
      name: Okta
      config:
        ssoURL: https://myorg.okta.com/app/sso/saml
        caData: <base64-cert>
        usernameAttr: email
        emailAttr: email
        groupsAttr: groups

    - type: ldap
      id: ldap
      name: Active Directory
      config:
        host: ldap.company.com:636
        bindDN: cn=argocd,dc=company,dc=com
        bindPW: $dex.ldap.bindPW
        userSearch:
          baseDN: ou=users,dc=company,dc=com
          username: sAMAccountName
          idAttr: DN
          emailAttr: mail
        groupSearch:
          baseDN: ou=groups,dc=company,dc=com
          nameAttr: cn
          userMatchers:
          - userAttr: DN
            groupAttr: member

  oidcConfig: |                              → direct OIDC (no Dex; simpler)
    name: Okta
    issuer: https://myorg.okta.com/oauth2/default
    clientID: <client-id>
    clientSecret: $oidc.okta.clientSecret
    requestedScopes: [openid, profile, email, groups]
    requestedIDTokenClaims:
      groups:
        essential: true

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Notifications
--------------------------------
  # argocd-notifications-cm ConfigMap:
  triggers: |
    - name: on-sync-failed
      condition: app.status.operationState.phase == 'Failed'
      template: app-sync-failed

    - name: on-deployed
      condition: app.status.operationState.phase == 'Succeeded' && app.status.health.status == 'Healthy'
      template: app-deployed

    - name: on-health-degraded
      condition: app.status.health.status == 'Degraded'
      template: app-health-degraded

  templates: |
    - name: app-sync-failed
      title: "{{.app.metadata.name}} sync failed"
      body: |
        App {{.app.metadata.name}} sync failed.
        Error: {{.app.status.operationState.message}}
        {{range .app.status.conditions}}
          * {{.message}}
        {{end}}
      slack:
        attachments: |
          [{
            "color": "danger",
            "title": "Sync Failed: {{.app.metadata.name}}",
            "fields": [
              {"title": "Environment", "value": "{{.app.spec.destination.namespace}}"},
              {"title": "Revision", "value": "{{.app.status.sync.revision}}"}
            ]
          }]

    - name: app-deployed
      github:
        repoURLPath: "{{.app.spec.source.repoURL}}"
        revisionPath: "{{.app.status.sync.revision}}"
        status:
          state: success
          label: "ArgoCD/{{.app.metadata.name}}"
          targetURL: "{{.context.argocdUrl}}/applications/{{.app.metadata.name}}"

  # Subscribe an application to notifications:
  metadata:
    annotations:
      notifications.argoproj.io/subscribe.on-sync-failed.slack: my-team-alerts
      notifications.argoproj.io/subscribe.on-deployed.github: ""
      notifications.argoproj.io/subscribe.on-health-degraded.pagerduty: ""

CONCEPT: Secrets Management with ArgoCD
-----------------------------------------
  Problem: secrets in Git = bad. But GitOps requires everything in Git.

  Solution 1: Sealed Secrets
    Encrypt secrets → commit ciphertext → ArgoCD deploys → controller decrypts
    kubeseal --cert pub-cert.pem < secret.yaml > sealed-secret.yaml
    ✓ Simple ✗ Key rotation is complex

  Solution 2: External Secrets Operator
    ArgoCD deploys ExternalSecret manifests (no sensitive data)
    ESO controller fetches actual values from AWS SM / Vault / etc.
    ✓ No secrets in Git ✓ Central secret management ✓ Rotation support

  Solution 3: Vault + ArgoCD Vault Plugin (AVP)
    ArgoCD repo-server plugin: replaces placeholders with Vault values at sync time.

    # secret.yaml in Git:
    apiVersion: v1
    kind: Secret
    metadata:
      name: db-secret
      annotations:
        avp.kubernetes.io/path: "secret/data/production/db"
    stringData:
      password: <password>             → AVP replaces with Vault value

    Install plugin in argocd-repo-server:
    # ConfigManagementPlugin in ArgoCD CM
    # Or as sidecar in argocd-repo-server

  Solution 4: SOPS (Secrets OPerationS)
    Encrypt files with AWS KMS / GCP KMS / Azure KeyVault / PGP.
    ArgoCD uses helm-secrets or kustomize-secret-generator plugin to decrypt.
    sops --encrypt --kms arn:aws:kms:us-east-1:123:key/abc secret.yaml > secret.enc.yaml
    Commit the .enc.yaml file; ArgoCD decrypts at sync time.

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Metrics & Monitoring
---------------------------------------
  Metrics exposed by argocd-server + argocd-application-controller:

  argocd_app_info{name, project, health_status, sync_status, dest_namespace}
  argocd_app_sync_total{name, phase}            → sync count by result
  argocd_app_reconcile_count{name}
  argocd_app_k8s_request_total                  → K8s API calls
  argocd_cluster_api_resource_objects           → objects tracked per cluster
  argocd_cluster_cache_age_seconds              → cache freshness

  Key alerts:
    App out of sync > 30 min:
      argocd_app_info{sync_status="OutOfSync"} == 1 for 30m
    App health degraded:
      argocd_app_info{health_status="Degraded"} == 1
    Sync failure:
      increase(argocd_app_sync_total{phase="Failed"}[5m]) > 0

  Grafana dashboard: ID 14584 (ArgoCD Notifications)

CONCEPT: ArgoCD Autopilot
---------------------------
argocd-autopilot bootstraps a full GitOps setup from scratch.
Creates the Git repository structure + installs ArgoCD + creates root App.

  argocd-autopilot repo bootstrap --repo https://github.com/org/gitops
  argocd-autopilot project create production
  argocd-autopilot app create myapp --app github.com/org/k8s-configs/myapp
    --project production --env production

  Generated structure:
  gitops-repo/
  ├── bootstrap/
  │   ├── argo-cd/               → ArgoCD installation
  │   └── cluster-resources/     → namespace, RBAC
  ├── projects/
  │   └── production.yaml        → AppProject
  └── apps/
      └── myapp/
          ├── base/
          └── overlays/
              └── production/

CONCEPT: Disaster Recovery for ArgoCD
----------------------------------------
  ArgoCD state stored in:
    - argocd-secret (server + Dex secrets)
    - ConfigMaps (argocd-cm, argocd-rbac-cm, argocd-notifications-cm)
    - Application/AppProject/ApplicationSet custom resources
    - Cluster secrets

  Since all Application specs are in Git, recovery is:
    1. Reinstall ArgoCD (helm install)
    2. Apply ConfigMaps + RBAC config from Git
    3. Apply cluster secrets
    4. Apply root App → ArgoCD re-creates everything

  Export all ArgoCD resources:
    kubectl get applications,appprojects,applicationsets -n argocd -o yaml > argocd-backup.yaml
    # Or use argocd export (argocd-autopilot)

  HA mode:
    argocd-server:                3 replicas + HPA
    argocd-application-controller: sharded (one shard per N clusters)
    argocd-repo-server:           3 replicas (stateless)
    argocd-redis:                 Redis HA (Sentinel or Redis Cluster)

HANDS-ON TASKS (Expert):
  1. Configure GitHub SSO via Dex; map GitHub teams to ArgoCD roles
  2. Implement complete RBAC: admin, developer, read-only with project scope
  3. Set up notifications: Slack on sync-failed, GitHub commit status on deploy
  4. Implement secrets management with External Secrets + ArgoCD
  5. Configure ApplicationSet with progressive rollout across environments
  6. Set up ArgoCD HA with 3 replicas; test with pod failures
  7. Implement sync windows for production change freezes
  8. Bootstrap full GitOps with argocd-autopilot; own the full repo structure

REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS:
  SCENARIO A — Implementing GitOps from scratch for a platform team:
    Phase 1: Bootstrap
      1. Create gitops-configs repo (infrastructure)
      2. Install ArgoCD via Helm; configure SSO + RBAC
      3. Create root App of Apps
      4. Migrate existing namespaces into GitOps management
    Phase 2: Developer workflow
      1. Developer updates image tag in Git → PR → review → merge
      2. ArgoCD detects change → syncs → deploys
      3. Or: Image Updater detects new image → opens PR automatically
    Phase 3: Governance
      1. Require PR approval for production changes
      2. Configure sync windows for production
      3. Set up notifications for all stakeholders

  SCENARIO B — Production sync is OutOfSync but automated:
    Symptoms: ArgoCD shows OutOfSync; continuous sync loop
    Diagnosis:
      argocd app diff myapp → what is different?
      Common causes:
        HPA changing replicas → add ignoreDifferences for /spec/replicas
        Operator mutating resource → ignoreDifferences for mutated fields
        Secret rotation changing Secret data → ignore /data in secrets
        Generated fields (creationTimestamp, resourceVersion) → ServerSideApply helps
    Fix: add appropriate ignoreDifferences; enable ServerSideApply

  SCENARIO C — Multi-team, multi-cluster platform GitOps:
    Structure:
      gitops-repo/
        clusters/
          prod-us-east1/         → cluster config
          prod-eu-west1/
          staging/
        apps/
          team-payments/         → one dir per team
          team-auth/
          team-notifications/
        platform/
          monitoring/
          security/
          cert-manager/
    ApplicationSet cluster generator:
      → Generates one application per team per cluster automatically
      → New cluster = add config to clusters/ → all apps auto-deployed
      → New app = add to apps/team-X/ → deployed to all clusters

################################################################################
#                         PHASE 9: HELM                                       #
