================================================================================
1. FOUNDATION — What Helm Is and How It Works
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Helm's Role
----------------------
Helm is the package manager for Kubernetes. It:
  - Packages Kubernetes manifests into reusable "charts"
  - Templates manifests with values (parameterization)
  - Manages installation lifecycle (install, upgrade, rollback, delete)
  - Tracks deployed releases with versioned history
  - Manages dependencies between charts

Core entities:
  Chart   → package of templated Kubernetes manifests + metadata
  Release → a deployed instance of a chart in a cluster
  Values  → configuration parameters overriding chart defaults
  Repo    → collection of charts (OCI registry or HTTP index)
  Revision → version of a release (increments on install/upgrade/rollback)

CONCEPT: Helm Architecture
----------------------------
Helm 3 (current — Tiller removed):
  helm CLI → directly talks to Kubernetes API server
  Release state → stored as Secrets in the release's namespace
  No server-side component; permissions = kubectl context's permissions

  kubectl get secrets -n production -l owner=helm   → see release secrets
  kubectl get secret sh.helm.release.v1.myapp.v3 -o jsonpath='{.data.release}' \
    | base64 -d | base64 -d | gzip -d | jq .   → decode release state

CONCEPT: Chart Structure
--------------------------
  mychart/
  ├── Chart.yaml              → chart metadata (name, version, description, deps)
  ├── values.yaml             → default values
  ├── values.schema.json      → JSON Schema validation for values
  ├── charts/                 → dependency charts (vendored)
  ├── crds/                   → CRD manifests (installed before templates; never templated)
  ├── templates/
  │   ├── NOTES.txt           → displayed after install (usage instructions)
  │   ├── _helpers.tpl        → named templates / partial templates (starts with _)
  │   ├── deployment.yaml
  │   ├── service.yaml
  │   ├── ingress.yaml
  │   ├── configmap.yaml
  │   ├── secret.yaml
  │   ├── serviceaccount.yaml
  │   ├── hpa.yaml
  │   └── tests/
  │       └── test-connection.yaml   → helm test jobs
  └── README.md

Chart.yaml:
  apiVersion: v2                    → Helm 3 (v1 = Helm 2)
  name: myapp
  description: My Application Chart
  type: application                 → application (deployable) or library (templates only)
  version: 1.3.0                   → chart version (SemVer; increment on chart changes)
  appVersion: "2.5.1"             → version of the app being packaged (informational)
  keywords: [web, api, backend]
  maintainers:
  - name: Platform Team
    email: platform@company.com
  dependencies:
  - name: postgresql
    version: "13.2.x"
    repository: https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
    condition: postgresql.enabled
    alias: db                       → use as .Values.db.*
  - name: redis
    version: "~18.0.0"
    repository: oci://registry-1.docker.io/bitnamicharts
    condition: redis.enabled

CONCEPT: Essential Helm Commands
----------------------------------
  Repo management:
    helm repo add bitnami https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
    helm repo add argo https://argoproj.github.io/argo-helm
    helm repo update                         → refresh all repos
    helm repo list
    helm repo remove bitnami
    helm search repo nginx                   → search across all repos
    helm search repo nginx --versions        → all available versions

  Install / Upgrade:
    helm install myrelease ./mychart
    helm install myrelease ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --set image.tag=v1.2.3
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --set-string image.tag="1.2.3"
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --set-json 'labels={"env":"prod"}'
    helm install myrelease ./mychart -n production --create-namespace
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --dry-run --debug   → render + validate; don't apply
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --wait              → wait for all resources healthy
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --timeout 5m        → custom wait timeout
    helm install myrelease ./mychart --atomic            → rollback on failure
    helm upgrade myrelease ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml --install  → upgrade-or-install
    helm upgrade myrelease ./mychart --reuse-values      → keep previous values
    helm upgrade myrelease ./mychart --reset-values      → reset to chart defaults

  Inspection:
    helm list -n production                  → list releases
    helm list -A                             → all namespaces
    helm status myrelease -n production      → release status + notes
    helm get values myrelease -n production  → current values
    helm get values myrelease -n production --all  → merged with defaults
    helm get manifest myrelease             → rendered K8s manifests
    helm get hooks myrelease                → hook manifests
    helm get notes myrelease                → NOTES.txt output
    helm history myrelease                  → revision history

  Rollback / Uninstall:
    helm rollback myrelease 3              → rollback to revision 3
    helm rollback myrelease 0              → rollback to previous revision
    helm uninstall myrelease               → delete release + all resources
    helm uninstall myrelease --keep-history  → keep history; allow rollback later

  Rendering / Debugging:
    helm template myrelease ./mychart -f values.yaml   → render locally (no K8s needed)
    helm template myrelease ./mychart | kubectl apply --dry-run=client -f -
    helm lint ./mychart                    → lint chart for errors
    helm lint ./mychart --strict           → treat warnings as errors

HANDS-ON TASKS (Foundation):
  1. Create a chart from scratch: helm create myapp → inspect structure
  2. Install, upgrade, and rollback a chart
  3. Use helm template to render manifests; pipe to kubectl diff
  4. Add bitnami repo; search and install PostgreSQL chart
  5. Explore helm get all commands on a deployed release

================================================================================
2. CORE CONCEPTS — Templating
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Go Template Syntax
------------------------------
Helm uses Go's text/template engine with Sprig functions added.

  Delimiters:  {{ }} (whitespace can be controlled with {{- -}})
  Values:      .Values.key.subkey
  Chart meta:  .Chart.Name, .Chart.Version, .Chart.AppVersion
  Release:     .Release.Name, .Release.Namespace, .Release.Revision,
               .Release.IsInstall, .Release.IsUpgrade, .Release.Service
  Files:       .Files.Get "config.yaml"
  Capabilities: .Capabilities.KubeVersion, .Capabilities.APIVersions.Has

  Whitespace control:
    {{-  → trim whitespace BEFORE the action
    -}}  → trim whitespace AFTER the action
    {{- if .Values.enabled -}}  → trim both sides

  Variables:
    {{- $name := .Release.Name -}}
    {{- $name | upper -}}

  Conditionals:
    {{- if .Values.ingress.enabled }}
    # ingress manifest
    {{- end }}

    {{- if and .Values.tls.enabled .Values.ingress.enabled }}
    {{- else if .Values.ingress.enabled }}
    {{- else }}
    {{- end }}

  Loops:
    {{- range .Values.hosts }}
    - host: {{ . }}
    {{- end }}

    {{- range $key, $val := .Values.annotations }}
    {{ $key }}: {{ $val | quote }}
    {{- end }}

  With (scoped context):
    {{- with .Values.resources }}
    resources:
      {{- toYaml . | nindent 6 }}
    {{- end }}

CONCEPT: Functions & Pipelines
--------------------------------
Helm adds Sprig (100+ functions) + custom functions:

  String functions:
    {{ .Values.name | upper }}               → MYAPP
    {{ .Values.name | lower }}               → myapp
    {{ .Values.name | title }}               → Myapp
    {{ .Values.name | trim }}                → strip whitespace
    {{ .Values.name | trunc 63 }}            → truncate to 63 chars
    {{ .Values.name | replace "_" "-" }}     → replace characters
    {{ printf "%s-%s" .Release.Name .Chart.Name }}
    {{ .Values.name | quote }}               → "wrapped in quotes"
    {{ .Values.name | b64enc }}              → base64 encode
    {{ .Values.encoded | b64dec }}           → base64 decode

  Default values:
    {{ .Values.replicas | default 1 }}
    {{ .Values.image.pullPolicy | default "IfNotPresent" }}

  Type conversion:
    {{ .Values.port | int }}
    {{ .Values.flag | toString }}
    {{ .Values.count | int64 }}

  YAML marshaling:
    {{ toYaml .Values.resources }}           → convert to YAML string
    {{ .Values.resources | toYaml | nindent 8 }}  → indent + newline prefix
    {{ fromYaml .Values.rawYaml }}           → parse YAML string to dict

  JSON:
    {{ toJson .Values.config }}
    {{ fromJson .Values.rawJson }}

  Validation:
    {{ required "image.tag is required" .Values.image.tag }}
    → fails with message if value is empty/nil

  List operations:
    {{ list "a" "b" "c" | join "," }}       → a,b,c
    {{ concat .Values.list1 .Values.list2 }}
    {{ .Values.list | uniq }}               → deduplicate
    {{ .Values.list | first }}
    {{ .Values.list | last }}
    {{ len .Values.list }}

  Dict operations:
    {{ dict "key1" "val1" "key2" "val2" }}
    {{ merge .Values.defaults .Values.overrides }}
    {{ keys .Values.config | sortAlpha | join "," }}
    {{ hasKey .Values.config "key" }}
    {{ .Values.config | pick "key1" "key2" }}  → subset of dict

  Crypto:
    {{ randAlphaNum 32 }}                   → random 32-char string
    {{ uuidv4 }}                            → UUID
    {{ sha256sum .Values.config }}

CONCEPT: Named Templates (_helpers.tpl)
-----------------------------------------
Named templates (partials) live in files starting with _.
They are defined with define and called with include or template.

  # templates/_helpers.tpl

  {{/*
  Expand the name of the chart.
  */}}
  {{- define "myapp.name" -}}
  {{- .Chart.Name | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" }}
  {{- end }}

  {{/*
  Full name: release-chart (truncated to 63 chars)
  */}}
  {{- define "myapp.fullname" -}}
  {{- if .Values.fullnameOverride }}
  {{- .Values.fullnameOverride | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" }}
  {{- else }}
  {{- $name := default .Chart.Name .Values.nameOverride }}
  {{- if contains $name .Release.Name }}
  {{- .Release.Name | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" }}
  {{- else }}
  {{- printf "%s-%s" .Release.Name $name | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" }}
  {{- end }}
  {{- end }}
  {{- end }}

  {{/*
  Common labels — applied to ALL resources
  */}}
  {{- define "myapp.labels" -}}
  helm.sh/chart: {{ include "myapp.chart" . }}
  {{ include "myapp.selectorLabels" . }}
  {{- if .Chart.AppVersion }}
  app.kubernetes.io/version: {{ .Chart.AppVersion | quote }}
  {{- end }}
  app.kubernetes.io/managed-by: {{ .Release.Service }}
  {{- end }}

  {{/*
  Selector labels — used in selector + template labels
  */}}
  {{- define "myapp.selectorLabels" -}}
  app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "myapp.name" . }}
  app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
  {{- end }}

  {{/*
  ServiceAccount name
  */}}
  {{- define "myapp.serviceAccountName" -}}
  {{- if .Values.serviceAccount.create }}
  {{- default (include "myapp.fullname" .) .Values.serviceAccount.name }}
  {{- else }}
  {{- default "default" .Values.serviceAccount.name }}
  {{- end }}
  {{- end }}

  # Usage in deployment.yaml:
  metadata:
    name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}
    labels:
      {{- include "myapp.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        {{- include "myapp.selectorLabels" . | nindent 6 }}

  include vs template:
    {{ include "myapp.labels" . }}   → returns string; can be piped (preferred)
    {{ template "myapp.labels" . }}  → outputs directly; cannot be piped

CONCEPT: Values Hierarchy & Merging
--------------------------------------
Values are merged in order (later overrides earlier):
  1. Chart's default values.yaml
  2. Parent chart's values (for subcharts)
  3. -f user-supplied values files (left to right)
  4. --set / --set-string / --set-json / --set-file flags

  Multiple value files:
  helm install myapp ./chart \
    -f values-base.yaml \
    -f values-production.yaml \    → overrides base
    --set image.tag=v1.2.3         → highest priority

  Subchart values:
  # values.yaml of parent chart:
  # Subchart values are nested under the subchart's alias/name:
  postgresql:
    auth:
      database: mydb
      username: appuser
      existingSecret: db-secret
    primary:
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: 500m
          memory: 512Mi

  Global values (accessible to chart AND all subcharts):
  global:
    imageRegistry: myregistry.example.com
    imagePullSecrets: [regcred]
    storageClass: gp3

  Access in template: {{ .Values.global.imageRegistry }}

CONCEPT: Complete Deployment Template
----------------------------------------
  # templates/deployment.yaml
  apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: Deployment
  metadata:
    name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}
    namespace: {{ .Release.Namespace }}
    labels:
      {{- include "myapp.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
    annotations:
      {{- with .Values.podAnnotations }}
      {{- toYaml . | nindent 4 }}
      {{- end }}
  spec:
    {{- if not .Values.autoscaling.enabled }}
    replicas: {{ .Values.replicaCount }}
    {{- end }}
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        {{- include "myapp.selectorLabels" . | nindent 6 }}
    strategy:
      {{- toYaml .Values.strategy | nindent 4 }}
    template:
      metadata:
        labels:
          {{- include "myapp.selectorLabels" . | nindent 8 }}
          {{- with .Values.podLabels }}
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
          {{- end }}
        annotations:
          checksum/config: {{ include (print $.Template.BasePath "/configmap.yaml") . | sha256sum }}
          {{- with .Values.podAnnotations }}
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
          {{- end }}
      spec:
        {{- with .Values.imagePullSecrets }}
        imagePullSecrets:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}
        serviceAccountName: {{ include "myapp.serviceAccountName" . }}
        securityContext:
          {{- toYaml .Values.podSecurityContext | nindent 8 }}
        containers:
        - name: {{ .Chart.Name }}
          securityContext:
            {{- toYaml .Values.securityContext | nindent 12 }}
          image: "{{ .Values.image.repository }}:{{ .Values.image.tag | default .Chart.AppVersion }}"
          imagePullPolicy: {{ .Values.image.pullPolicy }}
          ports:
          - name: http
            containerPort: {{ .Values.service.port }}
            protocol: TCP
          {{- with .Values.livenessProbe }}
          livenessProbe:
            {{- toYaml . | nindent 12 }}
          {{- end }}
          {{- with .Values.readinessProbe }}
          readinessProbe:
            {{- toYaml . | nindent 12 }}
          {{- end }}
          resources:
            {{- toYaml .Values.resources | nindent 12 }}
          env:
          - name: POD_NAME
            valueFrom:
              fieldRef:
                fieldPath: metadata.name
          {{- range $key, $val := .Values.env }}
          - name: {{ $key }}
            value: {{ $val | quote }}
          {{- end }}
          {{- with .Values.envFrom }}
          envFrom:
            {{- toYaml . | nindent 12 }}
          {{- end }}
          volumeMounts:
          {{- with .Values.volumeMounts }}
            {{- toYaml . | nindent 12 }}
          {{- end }}
        {{- with .Values.volumes }}
        volumes:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}
        {{- with .Values.nodeSelector }}
        nodeSelector:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}
        {{- with .Values.affinity }}
        affinity:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}
        {{- with .Values.tolerations }}
        tolerations:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}
        {{- with .Values.topologySpreadConstraints }}
        topologySpreadConstraints:
          {{- toYaml . | nindent 8 }}
        {{- end }}

  checksum annotation forces pod restart when ConfigMap changes:
    checksum/config: {{ include (print $.Template.BasePath "/configmap.yaml") . | sha256sum }}

HANDS-ON TASKS (Core):
  1. Build a full chart with all standard templates (_helpers, deployment, service, ingress, hpa, sa)
  2. Implement required validator for mandatory values
  3. Use checksum annotation to trigger pod restart on config change
  4. Use toYaml + nindent pattern for resources, affinity, tolerations
  5. Write conditional templates for optional features (ingress, hpa, pdb)
  6. Use range to generate multiple environment variables from a map

================================================================================
3. ADVANCED — Lifecycle, Hooks, Dependencies, Schema
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Helm Hooks
---------------------
Hooks allow running actions at specific points in the release lifecycle.

  Hook annotations:
    helm.sh/hook: pre-install      → before any resources created
    helm.sh/hook: post-install     → after all resources created
    helm.sh/hook: pre-upgrade      → before upgrade
    helm.sh/hook: post-upgrade     → after upgrade
    helm.sh/hook: pre-rollback     → before rollback
    helm.sh/hook: post-rollback    → after rollback
    helm.sh/hook: pre-delete       → before uninstall
    helm.sh/hook: post-delete      → after uninstall
    helm.sh/hook: test             → helm test

  helm.sh/hook-weight: "5"         → ordering (lower runs first; default 0)
  helm.sh/hook-delete-policy: before-hook-creation,hook-succeeded

  # Database migration hook:
  apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}-migrate
    labels:
      {{- include "myapp.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
    annotations:
      helm.sh/hook: pre-upgrade,pre-install
      helm.sh/hook-weight: "-5"
      helm.sh/hook-delete-policy: before-hook-creation,hook-succeeded
  spec:
    template:
      spec:
        restartPolicy: OnFailure
        containers:
        - name: migrate
          image: "{{ .Values.image.repository }}:{{ .Values.image.tag }}"
          command: ["/app/migrate", "up"]
          env:
          - name: DATABASE_URL
            valueFrom:
              secretKeyRef:
                name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}-db-secret
                key: url

  Hook resources are NOT managed by Helm after execution (unless deleted by policy).
  They do NOT appear in helm get manifest.

  helm test:
  # templates/tests/test-connection.yaml
  apiVersion: v1
  kind: Pod
  metadata:
    name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}-test-connection
    annotations:
      helm.sh/hook: test
      helm.sh/hook-delete-policy: before-hook-creation
  spec:
    restartPolicy: Never
    containers:
    - name: wget
      image: busybox
      command: ['wget']
      args: ['{{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}:{{ .Values.service.port }}']

  helm test myrelease -n production     → runs test pods; shows pass/fail

CONCEPT: Chart Dependencies
------------------------------
  # Chart.yaml:
  dependencies:
  - name: postgresql
    version: "13.2.x"              → x = patch-level wildcard
    repository: https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
    condition: postgresql.enabled  → only install if .Values.postgresql.enabled=true
    tags: [database]               → can enable/disable all tagged deps
    alias: db                      → .Values.db.* instead of .Values.postgresql.*
  - name: redis
    version: "~18.0.0"             → ~ = compatible patch versions
    repository: oci://registry-1.docker.io/bitnamicharts
    condition: redis.enabled
  - name: common
    version: "2.x.x"
    repository: https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
    import-values:
    - child: data                  → import subkey from dependency's exported values
      parent: common               → into .Values.common of parent

  # Manage dependencies:
  helm dependency update ./mychart   → download deps to charts/; update Chart.lock
  helm dependency build ./mychart    → install from Chart.lock (exact versions; CI)
  helm dependency list ./mychart     → show dep status

  Chart.lock:
    Generated by helm dep update.
    Locks exact versions of all dependencies.
    Commit Chart.lock (not charts/ directory) for reproducible builds.
    .gitignore: charts/

  Condition vs Tags:
    condition:  checked as dot-separated path in values; single dep control
    tags:       group of deps; enable/disable group at once
    # values.yaml:
    tags:
      database: true             → enable all deps tagged 'database'
    postgresql:
      enabled: true              → condition overrides tags (condition wins)

CONCEPT: Library Charts
------------------------
Library charts provide named templates for reuse across multiple charts.
They contain ONLY _helpers.tpl files (no deployable templates).
type: library in Chart.yaml.

  # company-common/Chart.yaml:
  apiVersion: v2
  name: company-common
  type: library
  version: 1.2.0

  # company-common/templates/_deployment.tpl:
  {{- define "company-common.deployment" -}}
  apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: Deployment
  metadata:
    name: {{ include "company-common.fullname" . }}
    labels:
      {{- include "company-common.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
  spec:
    ...all standard deployment config...
  {{- end }}

  # Consumer chart's Chart.yaml:
  dependencies:
  - name: company-common
    version: "1.x.x"
    repository: oci://myregistry.example.com/helm

  # Consumer chart's templates/deployment.yaml:
  {{ include "company-common.deployment" . }}

  Library charts enforce standards across all services:
    - Standard labels
    - Standard security context
    - Standard resource requests

CONCEPT: Values Schema Validation
------------------------------------
  # values.schema.json
  {
    "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema",
    "type": "object",
    "required": ["image"],
    "properties": {
      "image": {
        "type": "object",
        "required": ["repository", "tag"],
        "properties": {
          "repository": { "type": "string", "minLength": 1 },
          "tag":        { "type": "string", "minLength": 1 },
          "pullPolicy": {
            "type": "string",
            "enum": ["Always", "Never", "IfNotPresent"]
          }
        }
      },
      "replicaCount": {
        "type": "integer",
        "minimum": 1,
        "maximum": 100
      },
      "resources": {
        "type": "object",
        "properties": {
          "limits": {
            "type": "object",
            "required": ["cpu", "memory"]
          }
        }
      },
      "ingress": {
        "type": "object",
        "properties": {
          "enabled": { "type": "boolean" },
          "hosts": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
              "type": "object",
              "required": ["host"],
              "properties": {
                "host": { "type": "string", "format": "hostname" }
              }
            }
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }

  helm install enforces schema:
    helm install myapp . --set replicaCount=abc   → Error: replicaCount must be integer

CONCEPT: OCI Registry Support (Helm 3.8+)
-------------------------------------------
Store Helm charts in OCI registries (same as Docker images).

  # Login:
  helm registry login myregistry.example.com \
    --username myuser --password mytoken

  # Login to ECR:
  aws ecr get-login-password --region us-east-1 | \
    helm registry login 123.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com --username AWS --password-stdin

  # Package and push:
  helm package ./mychart                    → creates mychart-1.2.3.tgz
  helm push mychart-1.2.3.tgz oci://myregistry.example.com/charts

  # Pull and install from OCI:
  helm install myapp oci://myregistry.example.com/charts/mychart --version 1.2.3
  helm pull oci://myregistry.example.com/charts/mychart --version 1.2.3 --untar

  # In Chart.yaml dependencies:
  - name: mychart
    version: "1.2.3"
    repository: oci://myregistry.example.com/charts

  OCI is the production-recommended distribution method:
    - Integrates with existing container registry infrastructure
    - Image scanning applies to charts too
    - RBAC reuses registry IAM
    - No separate chart museum to operate

HANDS-ON TASKS (Advanced):
  1. Add a pre-upgrade database migration hook; test it works correctly
  2. Add helm test job; run helm test and verify
  3. Create a chart with postgresql + redis as conditional dependencies
  4. Create a library chart with standard templates; use it in 2 charts
  5. Write values.schema.json; test validation catches bad values
  6. Package and push a chart to AWS ECR OCI registry; install from it

================================================================================
4. EXPERT LEVEL — Production Patterns, Security, GitOps Integration
================================================================================

CONCEPT: Helm in GitOps (ArgoCD + Helm)
-----------------------------------------
ArgoCD natively renders Helm charts. Two approaches:

  1. Chart in app repo (simple):
     source:
       repoURL: https://github.com/org/myapp.git
       path: charts/myapp
       targetRevision: main
       helm:
         valueFiles: [values-production.yaml]

  2. Chart in registry + values in config repo (separation of concerns):
     source:
       repoURL: oci://myregistry.example.com/charts
       chart: myapp
       targetRevision: 1.2.3        → exact version pinned in Git
       helm:
         valueFiles: [values.yaml]
     # values.yaml lives in the config repo (separate source)

  Multiple sources (ArgoCD 2.6+):
    sources:
    - repoURL: oci://myregistry.example.com/charts
      chart: myapp
      targetRevision: 1.2.3
    - repoURL: https://github.com/org/gitops-configs.git
      targetRevision: main
      ref: values                    → reference name
    helm:
      valueFiles:
      - $values/apps/myapp/values-production.yaml  → uses 'values' ref

CONCEPT: Helm Release Naming & Namespace Conventions
------------------------------------------------------
  Release name conventions:
    <service>-<env>:    myapp-production, myapp-staging
    <service>:          if single env per namespace (namespace provides env context)
    <team>-<service>:   payments-api, payments-worker (for monorepo multi-service)

  Full name override (avoid duplication like "myapp-myapp"):
    # values.yaml:
    fullnameOverride: ""
    nameOverride: ""
    # In _helpers.tpl: if release name already contains chart name, use release name only

  Release names in Helm are unique per namespace.
  Different namespaces can have the same release name.

CONCEPT: Helm Diff Plugin
---------------------------
helm-diff shows what will change BEFORE applying an upgrade.
Critical for production changes review.

  helm plugin install https://github.com/databus23/helm-diff

  helm diff upgrade myrelease ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml
  helm diff upgrade myrelease ./mychart --set image.tag=v2.0.0 -n production
  helm diff rollback myrelease 3 -n production

  Output: colored diff of all Kubernetes manifest changes.
  Use in CI to generate change summary for PR review.

CONCEPT: Helm Secrets Plugin
------------------------------
Transparently encrypt/decrypt values files with SOPS.

  helm plugin install https://github.com/jkroepke/helm-secrets

  # Encrypt a values file:
  sops -e values-secrets.yaml > values-secrets.enc.yaml

  # Install with encrypted values:
  helm secrets install myapp ./mychart \
    -f values.yaml \
    -f secrets://values-secrets.enc.yaml   → decrypted at runtime

  # With AWS KMS:
  sops --kms arn:aws:kms:us-east-1:123:key/abc -e values-secrets.yaml

CONCEPT: Production values.yaml Best Practices
------------------------------------------------
  # values.yaml — what good defaults look like:
  replicaCount: 2                          → sensible default; override per env

  image:
    repository: myregistry.com/myapp
    pullPolicy: IfNotPresent
    tag: ""                                → EMPTY: force explicit override

  imagePullSecrets: []

  serviceAccount:
    create: true
    automount: false                       → secure default
    annotations: {}
    name: ""

  podAnnotations: {}
  podLabels: {}

  podSecurityContext:
    runAsNonRoot: true
    runAsUser: 1001
    fsGroup: 1001
    seccompProfile:
      type: RuntimeDefault

  securityContext:
    allowPrivilegeEscalation: false
    readOnlyRootFilesystem: true
    capabilities:
      drop: [ALL]

  service:
    type: ClusterIP
    port: 8080

  ingress:
    enabled: false
    className: ""
    annotations: {}
    hosts: []
    tls: []

  resources:
    limits:
      cpu: 500m
      memory: 512Mi
    requests:
      cpu: 100m
      memory: 128Mi

  livenessProbe:
    httpGet:
      path: /health
      port: http
    initialDelaySeconds: 10
    periodSeconds: 30
    timeoutSeconds: 5
    failureThreshold: 3

  readinessProbe:
    httpGet:
      path: /ready
      port: http
    initialDelaySeconds: 5
    periodSeconds: 10
    timeoutSeconds: 3
    failureThreshold: 3

  autoscaling:
    enabled: false
    minReplicas: 2
    maxReplicas: 10
    targetCPUUtilizationPercentage: 70

  pdb:
    enabled: true
    minAvailable: 1

  nodeSelector: {}
  tolerations: []
  affinity: {}
  topologySpreadConstraints: []

  # Environment-specific overrides (values-production.yaml):
  replicaCount: 5
  image:
    tag: "1.3.2"
  autoscaling:
    enabled: true
    minReplicas: 5
    maxReplicas: 50
  ingress:
    enabled: true
    className: nginx
    hosts:
    - host: myapp.example.com
      paths: [{path: /, pathType: Prefix}]
  resources:
    limits:
      cpu: 2
      memory: 2Gi
    requests:
      cpu: 500m
      memory: 1Gi

CONCEPT: Helm Testing Strategy
--------------------------------
  1. helm lint (static syntax + style):
     helm lint ./mychart
     helm lint ./mychart --strict

  2. helm template + kubeval/kubeconform (K8s schema validation):
     helm template myapp ./mychart -f values.yaml | kubeconform -strict -summary
     helm template myapp ./mychart | kubeconform -kubernetes-version 1.29.0

  3. helm template + conftest/OPA (policy validation):
     helm template myapp ./mychart | conftest test -p policy/ -
     # Policies: require labels, no :latest, require resources, no privileged

  4. Helm unit tests (helm-unittest plugin):
     helm plugin install https://github.com/helm-unittest/helm-unittest

     # tests/deployment_test.yaml:
     suite: deployment tests
     templates: [templates/deployment.yaml]
     tests:
     - it: should have correct image
       set:
         image.repository: myapp
         image.tag: v1.2.3
       asserts:
       - equal:
           path: spec.template.spec.containers[0].image
           value: myapp:v1.2.3
     - it: should have 3 replicas when autoscaling disabled
       set:
         autoscaling.enabled: false
         replicaCount: 3
       asserts:
       - equal:
           path: spec.replicas
           value: 3
     - it: should not set replicas when autoscaling enabled
       set:
         autoscaling.enabled: true
       asserts:
       - notExists:
           path: spec.replicas

  5. helm test (runtime integration test in cluster):
     helm test myrelease -n production --logs

  Full CI pipeline for a chart:
    lint → unit-test → template+kubeconform → conftest → package → push to OCI
    On deploy: helm diff → review → helm upgrade --atomic

CONCEPT: Chart Versioning & Release Process
---------------------------------------------
  Chart.version (chart packaging version): increment when chart templates change
  Chart.appVersion: the application version being packaged (informational)

  Semver for charts:
    PATCH (1.2.x): bug fix in templates; no user-visible change
    MINOR (1.x.0): new optional features; backwards compatible values
    MAJOR (x.0.0): breaking changes in values interface

  Automated versioning in CI:
    # chart-releaser (cr) — GitHub Actions:
    - uses: helm/chart-releaser-action@v1.6.0
      with:
        charts_dir: charts
    # Detects chart version changes; packages; creates GitHub release; updates index

  chart-testing (ct) — CI tool for chart testing:
    ct lint --charts ./charts
    ct install --charts ./charts    → installs in ephemeral kind cluster

CONCEPT: Helm Security
------------------------
  Verify chart provenance (signed charts):
    helm install --verify mychart.tgz  → verify GPG signature
    helm package --sign --key 'My Key' --keyring ~/.gnupg/pubring.gpg ./mychart
    # Creates mychart-1.0.0.tgz + mychart-1.0.0.tgz.prov

  OCI chart signing with cosign:
    helm push mychart.tgz oci://myregistry.com/charts
    cosign sign myregistry.com/charts/mychart:1.0.0
    cosign verify myregistry.com/charts/mychart:1.0.0

  Secrets in values:
    NEVER put plaintext secrets in values.yaml
    NEVER --set db.password=mysecret (visible in process list + Helm release secret)
    USE: external secrets operator / Vault / SOPS-encrypted values

  Namespace isolation:
    Helm release secrets stored in the release namespace
    Use separate namespaces per release for isolation

  Review installed chart before trusting:
    helm pull bitnami/postgresql --untar
    cat postgresql/templates/*.yaml    → inspect before installing

REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS:
  SCENARIO A — Rollback failure in production:
    Problem: helm upgrade failed; app is broken
    Steps:
      1. helm history myapp -n production → find last good revision
      2. helm rollback myapp 7 -n production → rollback to revision 7
      3. helm status myapp -n production → verify rollback succeeded
      4. kubectl rollout status deployment/myapp -n production → pods healthy?
      5. Investigate failed upgrade: helm get manifest myapp -n production
      6. Fix root cause; re-attempt with helm upgrade --dry-run first
      7. Use --atomic on future upgrades (auto-rollback on failure)

  SCENARIO B — Multi-environment chart deployment strategy:
    Directory structure:
      helm/
        myapp/
          Chart.yaml
          values.yaml             → defaults
          values-dev.yaml         → dev overrides
          values-staging.yaml
          values-production.yaml
          values-production-eu.yaml

    CI/CD flow:
      Branch push → helm diff (show changes) → post to PR
      Merge to main:
        helm upgrade --install myapp ./helm/myapp \
          -f helm/myapp/values.yaml \
          -f helm/myapp/values-${ENV}.yaml \
          --set image.tag=${GIT_SHA} \
          -n ${NAMESPACE} \
          --atomic --timeout 5m

    Production:
      Gate: human approval in CI (GitHub environment protection)
      After approval: same helm upgrade command with production values

  SCENARIO C — Migrating from raw manifests to Helm:
    1. Start with: helm create myapp (scaffold)
    2. Move existing manifests into templates/
    3. Parameterize values that differ between envs (image, replicas, resources)
    4. helm template → diff against existing manifests
    5. helm install --dry-run → validate against cluster
    6. First deploy to dev namespace; verify
    7. Adopt existing prod: helm install --replace (takes ownership)
       OR: use label annotation approach (annotate existing resources)
    8. Verify: helm list, helm status, helm get manifest

================================================================================
PHASE 9: HELM — SUMMARY CHECKLIST
================================================================================
FUNDAMENTALS:
  [ ] Helm architecture (CLI, release state in Secrets, no Tiller)
  [ ] Chart structure (all files + directories)
  [ ] Chart.yaml (all fields: type, version, appVersion, dependencies)
  [ ] Helm commands (install, upgrade, rollback, diff, lint, template, test)
  [ ] Values hierarchy + merging (files + --set priority)

TEMPLATING:
  [ ] Go template syntax (variables, conditionals, loops, with)
  [ ] Whitespace control ({{- -}})
  [ ] Sprig functions (string, list, dict, crypto, math)
  [ ] toYaml + nindent pattern
  [ ] required + default + quote functions
  [ ] Named templates in _helpers.tpl
  [ ] include vs template
  [ ] checksum annotation for config change detection
  [ ] .Files.Get for embedding files

LIFECYCLE:
  [ ] Hooks (all phases: pre/post install/upgrade/rollback/delete/test)
  [ ] Hook weights + delete policies
  [ ] helm test (test pods + helm test command)
  [ ] Upgrade strategies (--atomic, --wait, --timeout)
  [ ] Release history + rollback

DEPENDENCIES:
  [ ] Chart.yaml dependencies (condition, tags, alias, import-values)
  [ ] helm dependency update vs build
  [ ] Chart.lock (commit lock, not charts/)
  [ ] Subchart value namespacing
  [ ] Global values
  [ ] Library charts (type: library)

SCHEMA & VALIDATION:
  [ ] values.schema.json (JSON Schema validation)
  [ ] required validator in templates
  [ ] helm lint + strict mode

DISTRIBUTION:
  [ ] OCI registry push/pull (helm push, helm pull)
  [ ] chart-releaser for GitHub-hosted charts
  [ ] Chart signing (GPG + cosign)

PRODUCTION PATTERNS:
  [ ] Production values.yaml defaults (secure baseline)
  [ ] Environment-specific value files
  [ ] helm-diff plugin (review before upgrade)
  [ ] helm-secrets plugin (SOPS-encrypted values)
  [ ] Helm + ArgoCD integration (chart in OCI + values in Git)
  [ ] Testing pipeline (lint → unit-test → kubeconform → conftest → helm test)
  [ ] helm-unittest plugin (template assertion tests)
  [ ] chart-testing (ct) for CI
  [ ] Secrets management (never in values.yaml)
