SECTION 13.1 — FOUNDATION: KUBERNETES STORAGE PRIMITIVES & PERSISTENT VOLUMES
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.1.1 CONCEPTS: THE KUBERNETES STORAGE MODEL
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

STORAGE ARCHITECTURE IN KUBERNETES:

Kubernetes abstracts storage through a layered model:

  Pod Volume  →  PersistentVolumeClaim (PVC)  →  PersistentVolume (PV)  →  Backend Storage

Each layer serves a distinct purpose:
  - Pod Volume:     ephemeral or persistent mount inside container
  - PVC:            namespaced request for storage (capacity, access mode, StorageClass)
  - PV:             cluster-scoped resource representing actual storage
  - StorageClass:   defines provisioner, reclaim policy, volume binding mode, parameters
  - CSI Driver:     Container Storage Interface — pluggable driver translating K8s API calls to storage backend operations

VOLUME LIFECYCLE:
  1. Provisioning   — static (admin creates PV) or dynamic (StorageClass + CSI creates PV on demand)
  2. Binding        — PVC bound to matching PV (capacity ≥ requested, access modes match)
  3. Using          — Pod mounts PVC at specified path
  4. Releasing      — Pod deleted, PVC deleted, PV enters Released state
  5. Reclaiming     — based on reclaimPolicy: Retain | Recycle (deprecated) | Delete

ACCESS MODES:
  ReadWriteOnce (RWO)       — single node read/write (block storage: EBS, Longhorn volume)
  ReadOnlyMany  (ROX)       — many nodes read-only (NFS shares, S3 CSI)
  ReadWriteMany (RWX)       — many nodes read/write (NFS, CephFS, Longhorn with NFS provisioner)
  ReadWriteOncePod (RWOP)   — single pod read/write (K8s 1.22+, strictest)

VOLUME BINDING MODES:
  Immediate            — PV provisioned immediately when PVC created (ignores pod topology)
  WaitForFirstConsumer — PV provisioned when Pod scheduled (respects node topology constraints)
  → Use WaitForFirstConsumer for cloud block storage to co-locate volume with pod's AZ

STORAGE CLASSES:

  apiVersion: storage.k8s.io/v1
  kind: StorageClass
  metadata:
    name: fast-ssd
    annotations:
      storageclass.kubernetes.io/is-default-class: "true"
  provisioner: driver.longhorn.io
  reclaimPolicy: Delete
  allowVolumeExpansion: true
  volumeBindingMode: WaitForFirstConsumer
  parameters:
    numberOfReplicas: "3"
    staleReplicaTimeout: "2880"
    fromBackup: ""
    diskSelector: "ssd"
    nodeSelector: "storage"
    dataLocality: "best-effort"

CSI (CONTAINER STORAGE INTERFACE):
  - Industry-standard interface for exposing storage to container orchestrators
  - CSI driver consists of: Controller Plugin (runs once, provisions/attaches/snapshots)
    + Node Plugin (runs on each node, mounts volumes)
  - CSI operations: CreateVolume, DeleteVolume, ControllerPublishVolume (attach),
    NodeStageVolume (format), NodePublishVolume (bind-mount), CreateSnapshot, DeleteSnapshot

CSI DRIVER COMPONENTS:
  - external-provisioner:   watches PVC, calls CreateVolume
  - external-attacher:      watches VolumeAttachment, calls ControllerPublish/Unpublish
  - external-snapshotter:   watches VolumeSnapshot, calls CreateSnapshot
  - external-resizer:       watches PVC resize requests, calls ControllerExpandVolume
  - node-driver-registrar:  registers CSI driver with kubelet

VOLUME SNAPSHOT FRAMEWORK:
  VolumeSnapshotClass    — defines snapshot driver and parameters
  VolumeSnapshot         — namespaced request to snapshot a PVC
  VolumeSnapshotContent  — cluster-scoped resource representing actual snapshot

  apiVersion: snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1
  kind: VolumeSnapshot
  metadata:
    name: postgres-snap-$(date +%Y%m%d)
    namespace: production
  spec:
    volumeSnapshotClassName: longhorn-snapshot-class
    source:
      persistentVolumeClaimName: postgres-data

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.1.2 HANDS-ON: EXPLORING KUBERNETES STORAGE OBJECTS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

# List all StorageClasses
kubectl get storageclass

# Describe default StorageClass
kubectl describe storageclass longhorn

# List PVCs across all namespaces
kubectl get pvc -A

# Check PV binding status
kubectl get pv -o wide

# Describe a PVC with events
kubectl describe pvc postgres-data -n production

# Check CSI driver pods
kubectl get pods -n longhorn-system

# List VolumeSnapshotClasses
kubectl get volumesnapshotclass

# List snapshots
kubectl get volumesnapshot -A

# Check CSI node objects
kubectl get csinodes
kubectl describe csinode worker-01

# Check VolumeAttachments (shows which PV is attached to which node)
kubectl get volumeattachments

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.1.3 REAL-WORLD: STORAGE CLASS DESIGN FOR PRODUCTION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

Multi-tier storage class strategy:

  storage-class: standard     → Longhorn, 2 replicas, HDD, reclaim=Delete
  storage-class: fast         → Longhorn, 3 replicas, SSD, reclaim=Delete
  storage-class: critical     → Longhorn, 3 replicas, SSD, reclaim=Retain
  storage-class: backup       → NFS, reclaim=Retain
  storage-class: ephemeral    → local-path, reclaim=Delete (scratch space)

Naming convention for PVCs:
  {app}-{component}-{environment}  →  postgres-data-prod, redis-data-prod
  Tag with ownerReferences so PVC inherits from StatefulSet for cleanup safety

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.2 CORE: LONGHORN — DISTRIBUTED BLOCK STORAGE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.2.1 CONCEPTS: LONGHORN INTERNALS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

WHAT LONGHORN IS:
Longhorn is a cloud-native distributed block storage system for Kubernetes, donated to CNCF by Rancher/SUSE. It builds persistent volumes from local disk space across cluster nodes using a microservices architecture — every volume is managed independently, so there is no global storage cluster bottleneck.

KEY DESIGN PRINCIPLES:
  1. Per-volume controller:     each volume has its own controller (Longhorn Engine)
  2. Replica-per-node:          volume replicas spread across nodes for HA
  3. Thin provisioning:         only allocates actual disk as data is written
  4. Incremental snapshots:     copy-on-write snapshot chain for efficient backups
  5. Built-in replication:      synchronous iSCSI replication across replicas

LONGHORN ARCHITECTURE — COMPONENTS:

  longhorn-manager          DaemonSet on all storage nodes
  ├── Node controller       manages disks, monitors health, schedules replicas
  ├── Volume controller     reconciles volume CRs, creates engine/replica processes
  ├── Engine controller     manages Engine instances per volume
  └── Replica controller    manages replica instances per volume

  longhorn-driver-plugin    CSI driver DaemonSet (node plugin)
  longhorn-csi-plugin       CSI controller plugin (deployment)
  longhorn-ui               Web dashboard (deployment)

  Per-volume processes (run as child processes of longhorn-manager):
  longhorn-engine           iSCSI frontend — handles R/W from Kubernetes pod
  longhorn-replica          stores actual volume data blocks on node disk

VOLUME I/O PATH:
  Pod → tgt (iSCSI initiator, kernel module) → Longhorn Engine (in userspace)
      → Longhorn Replica 1 (node-A) [synchronous]
      → Longhorn Replica 2 (node-B) [synchronous]
      → Longhorn Replica 3 (node-C) [synchronous]

  Write is acknowledged to pod only after ALL replicas confirm write.
  Read is served from any one replica (round-robin or primary).

LONGHORN DATA PATH ON DISK:
  /var/lib/longhorn/
  ├── replicas/
  │   └── pvc-abc123-e8f4/   ← one directory per replica
  │       ├── volume.meta    ← metadata: size, created-at, spec
  │       ├── 000.img        ← base layer (full size, thin-provisioned)
  │       └── 001.img        ← snapshot delta layer
  └── engine-binaries/
      └── v1.6.2/
          └── longhorn        ← engine binary

SNAPSHOT MODEL:
  Snapshots in Longhorn are differential — each snapshot records only the blocks
  that changed since the previous snapshot. They form a chain:

    base  →  snap-1  →  snap-2  →  snap-3  →  (live volume head)

  Reverting to snap-2 means discarding snap-3 and live head.
  Deleting snap-2 merges its blocks into snap-1 (parent).

  Snapshot chain max depth:  255 snapshots (practical limit much lower for performance)
  Snapshot space:            sum of all changed blocks across chain

BACKUP MECHANISM:
  Backups are independent from snapshots — they are pushed to external storage (S3, NFS):
    1. Freeze live volume head (quiesce)
    2. Take incremental snapshot
    3. Send changed blocks since last backup to backup store (S3 bucket / NFS share)
    4. Record backup metadata (blocks, snapshot chain) in backupstore

  Backup stores use a flat object model — efficient for S3.
  Backups are fully independent — can restore to any cluster.

LONGHORN VOLUMES — STATES:
  Creating      → Attaching → Attached → Detaching → Detached
                                ↓
                            Fault (all replicas failed)
                            Degraded (some replicas failed, still readable)

REPLICA SCHEDULING:
  Longhorn scheduler places replicas based on:
    - Node with most available disk space
    - Anti-affinity: no two replicas on same node (if nodeSelector allows it)
    - Disk selector: SSD vs HDD via disk tags
    - Node selector: filter nodes with specific labels

  Replica soft anti-affinity: if only 2 nodes available and replicaCount=3,
  allow placement of 2 replicas on same node (degraded but operational)

DATA LOCALITY MODES:
  disabled      — replicas spread freely (default)
  best-effort   — try to keep one replica on the same node as the pod
  strict-local  — always keep one replica local (pod won't start if local disk unavailable)

VOLUME EXPANSION:
  Longhorn supports online expansion for RWO volumes:
    kubectl patch pvc postgres-data -p '{"spec":{"resources":{"requests":{"storage":"50Gi"}}}}'
  Engine expands the volume. OS inside pod needs to resize filesystem:
    resize2fs /dev/longhorn/pvc-xxx

LONGHORN ENGINE UPGRADE (LIVE):
  Longhorn can upgrade the engine binary for a live volume without downtime:
    1. New engine binary deployed by upgrade manager
    2. Volume controller spawns new engine process with new binary
    3. Replicas migrated to new engine
    4. Old engine process terminated
  Pod continues serving I/O throughout.

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.2.2 HANDS-ON: INSTALLING AND OPERATING LONGHORN
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

PREREQUISITES CHECK:
  # Longhorn requires open-iscsi on all nodes
  # For Ubuntu/Debian:
  apt-get install -y open-iscsi
  systemctl enable --now iscsid

  # Check required kernel modules
  modprobe iscsi_tcp
  lsmod | grep iscsi

  # Check node readiness (official script)
  curl -sSfL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/longhorn/longhorn/master/scripts/environment_check.sh | bash

INSTALL VIA HELM:
  helm repo add longhorn https://charts.longhorn.io
  helm repo update

  # Create values.yaml
  cat > longhorn-values.yaml << 'EOF'
  defaultSettings:
    defaultReplicaCount: 3
    defaultDataPath: /var/lib/longhorn
    defaultDataLocality: best-effort
    replicaSoftAntiAffinity: true
    storageMinimalAvailablePercentage: 15
    upgradeChecker: false
    createDefaultDiskLabeledNodes: false
    backupTarget: s3://my-longhorn-backups@us-east-1/
    backupTargetCredentialSecret: aws-secret
    autoSalvage: true
    autoDeletePodWhenVolumeDetachedUnexpectedly: true
    defaultLonghornStaticStorageClass: longhorn-static
    taintToleration: "node-role.kubernetes.io/storage:NoSchedule"

  persistence:
    defaultClass: true
    defaultClassReplicaCount: 3
    defaultFsType: ext4
    defaultNodeSelector:
      enable: true
      selector: "storage"
    reclaimPolicy: Delete
    migratable: true

  ingress:
    enabled: true
    host: longhorn.internal.example.com
    tls: true
    tlsSecret: longhorn-tls

  resources:
    limits:
      cpu: 2
      memory: 2Gi
    requests:
      cpu: 100m
      memory: 128Mi
  EOF

  helm upgrade --install longhorn longhorn/longhorn \
    --namespace longhorn-system \
    --create-namespace \
    --values longhorn-values.yaml \
    --version 1.6.2

LABEL NODES FOR STORAGE:
  # Tag nodes that should host Longhorn replicas
  kubectl label node worker-01 node.longhorn.io/create-default-disk=true
  kubectl label node worker-02 node.longhorn.io/create-default-disk=true
  kubectl label node worker-03 node.longhorn.io/create-default-disk=true

  # Add disk to a node via Longhorn node manifest
  kubectl -n longhorn-system edit node.longhorn.io worker-01
  # Add disk entry in spec.disks section

CONFIGURE S3 BACKUP TARGET:
  # Create secret with AWS credentials
  kubectl create secret generic aws-secret \
    --namespace longhorn-system \
    --from-literal=AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID=AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE \
    --from-literal=AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY=wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY \
    --from-literal=AWS_ENDPOINTS=https://s3.us-east-1.amazonaws.com

  # Set backup target via Longhorn settings
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting backup-target \
    --type=merge \
    -p '{"value":"s3://my-longhorn-backups@us-east-1/"}'

  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting backup-target-credential-secret \
    --type=merge \
    -p '{"value":"aws-secret"}'

WORKING WITH VOLUMES:
  # Create a PVC using Longhorn StorageClass
  kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: v1
  kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
  metadata:
    name: test-pvc
    namespace: default
  spec:
    accessModes: [ReadWriteOnce]
    storageClassName: longhorn
    resources:
      requests:
        storage: 10Gi
  EOF

  # Check volume in Longhorn
  kubectl get volumes.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system
  kubectl describe volumes.longhorn.io pvc-abc123 -n longhorn-system

  # Check replicas
  kubectl get replicas.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system \
    -l longhornvolume=pvc-abc123

SNAPSHOT OPERATIONS VIA KUBERNETES:
  # Create VolumeSnapshot
  kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1
  kind: VolumeSnapshot
  metadata:
    name: postgres-snap-manual
    namespace: production
  spec:
    volumeSnapshotClassName: longhorn
    source:
      persistentVolumeClaimName: postgres-data
  EOF

  # Check snapshot status
  kubectl get volumesnapshot postgres-snap-manual -n production
  kubectl describe volumesnapshot postgres-snap-manual -n production

  # Restore from snapshot into new PVC
  kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: v1
  kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
  metadata:
    name: postgres-data-restored
    namespace: production
  spec:
    storageClassName: longhorn
    dataSource:
      name: postgres-snap-manual
      kind: VolumeSnapshot
      apiGroup: snapshot.storage.k8s.io
    accessModes: [ReadWriteOnce]
    resources:
      requests:
        storage: 50Gi
  EOF

RECURRING JOBS (SCHEDULED SNAPSHOTS & BACKUPS):
  kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: longhorn.io/v1beta2
  kind: RecurringJob
  metadata:
    name: daily-backup
    namespace: longhorn-system
  spec:
    cron: "0 2 * * *"       # daily at 2am
    task: backup
    groups: [default]
    retain: 14              # keep 14 backups
    concurrency: 5          # max 5 concurrent backup jobs
    labels: {}
  ---
  apiVersion: longhorn.io/v1beta2
  kind: RecurringJob
  metadata:
    name: hourly-snapshot
    namespace: longhorn-system
  spec:
    cron: "0 * * * *"       # every hour
    task: snapshot
    groups: [default]
    retain: 24              # keep 24 hourly snapshots
    concurrency: 10
    labels: {}
  EOF

  # Assign volume to recurring job group
  kubectl -n longhorn-system label volume.longhorn.io pvc-abc123 \
    recurring-job-group.longhorn.io/default=enabled

LONGHORN CLI (longhornctl) — FOR DEBUGGING:
  # Install longhornctl
  curl -Lo longhornctl https://github.com/longhorn/cli/releases/download/v0.1.0/longhornctl-linux-amd64
  chmod +x longhornctl

  # Check cluster health
  longhornctl check preflight
  longhornctl get volume
  longhornctl get replica
  longhornctl inspect node worker-01

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.2.3 REAL-WORLD: LONGHORN IN PRODUCTION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

PRODUCTION TOPOLOGY:
  - Dedicated storage nodes with NVMe SSDs (tainted: storage:NoSchedule)
  - Worker nodes use default disks only for system/scratch volumes
  - Longhorn manager runs on all nodes (DaemonSet), replicas only on tagged nodes
  - Minimum 3 storage nodes for quorum
  - Network: dedicated 10GbE interface for storage traffic (Longhorn supports
    storage network via Multus CNI to isolate replication from workload traffic)

STORAGE NETWORK ISOLATION:
  # Longhorn storage network (uses Multus)
  apiVersion: k8s.cni.cncf.io/v1
  kind: NetworkAttachmentDefinition
  metadata:
    name: longhorn-storage-network
    namespace: longhorn-system
  spec:
    config: |
      {
        "cniVersion": "0.3.1",
        "name": "longhorn-storage-network",
        "type": "macvlan",
        "master": "eth1",
        "mode": "bridge",
        "ipam": {
          "type": "whereabouts",
          "range": "192.168.200.0/24"
        }
      }

  # Tell Longhorn to use this network
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting storage-network \
    --type=merge \
    -p '{"value":"longhorn-system/longhorn-storage-network"}'

PERFORMANCE TUNING:
  # Increase concurrent rebuild limit
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting concurrent-volume-backup-restore-per-node-limit \
    --type=merge -p '{"value":"5"}'

  # Replica rebuild timeout
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting replica-replenishment-wait-interval \
    --type=merge -p '{"value":"600"}'  # 10 minutes

  # I/O timeout (seconds before replica is considered failed)
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting storage-network-for-iSCSI \
    --type=merge -p '{"value":"true"}'

  # Guaranteed engine CPU (prevent throttling)
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch setting guaranteed-engine-cpu-overhead \
    --type=merge -p '{"value":"0.25"}'

ALERTS FOR LONGHORN (Prometheus):
  # ServiceMonitor
  apiVersion: monitoring.coreos.com/v1
  kind: ServiceMonitor
  metadata:
    name: longhorn-prometheus-servicemonitor
    namespace: monitoring
    labels:
      app: longhorn-manager
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: longhorn-manager
    namespaceSelector:
      matchNames: [longhorn-system]
    endpoints:
    - port: manager

  # Key PromQL alerts
  # Volume degraded
  longhorn_volume_robustness{robustness!="healthy"} > 0

  # Disk space low
  (longhorn_node_storage_usage_bytes / longhorn_node_storage_capacity_bytes) > 0.85

  # Replica rebuild in progress
  longhorn_volume_actual_size_bytes{condition="rebuilding"} > 0

  # Backup failed
  longhorn_backup_state{state!="Completed"} > 0

DISASTER RECOVERY SCENARIO — NODE FAILURE:
  1. Node worker-02 fails (disk failure, kernel panic)
  2. Longhorn detects: replicas on worker-02 are stale/unavailable
  3. Volume enters Degraded state (replica count: 2/3)
  4. Longhorn starts new replica on available node (worker-04 or worker-01)
  5. Sync: replica rebuilt from healthy copies (rate-limited to not impact I/O)
  6. Volume returns to Healthy state (3/3 replicas)

  Monitoring this:
  kubectl get volumes.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system \
    -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,STATE:.status.state,ROBUSTNESS:.status.robustness

MIGRATING VOLUMES BETWEEN NODES (maintenance):
  # Cordon a storage node (drain its replicas first)
  kubectl -n longhorn-system patch node.longhorn.io worker-01 \
    --type=merge \
    -p '{"spec":{"allowScheduling":false,"evictionRequested":true}}'

  # Monitor eviction progress
  kubectl get replicas.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system \
    -l longhornnode=worker-01

  # Once all replicas migrated, cordon Kubernetes node
  kubectl cordon worker-01
  kubectl drain worker-01 --ignore-daemonsets --delete-emptydir-data

LONGHORN BACKUP RESTORE TO NEW CLUSTER:
  # 1. On source cluster: ensure backups exist in S3
  # 2. On target cluster: install Longhorn, point to same S3 backup target
  # 3. List available backups
  kubectl get backups.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system

  # 4. Restore from backup
  kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: longhorn.io/v1beta2
  kind: Volume
  metadata:
    name: postgres-data-restored
    namespace: longhorn-system
  spec:
    fromBackup: "s3://my-longhorn-backups@us-east-1/?backup=backup-abc123&volume=pvc-xyz"
    numberOfReplicas: 3
    size: "53687091200"  # 50Gi in bytes
    accessMode: rwo
  EOF

  # 5. Create PV/PVC pair pointing to restored volume
  # (Longhorn creates PV automatically when volume is attached)

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 13.3 — ADVANCED: VELERO — KUBERNETES BACKUP AND DISASTER RECOVERY
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.3.1 CONCEPTS: VELERO ARCHITECTURE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

WHAT VELERO IS:
Velero (formerly Heptio Ark) is a Kubernetes-native tool for:
  1. Backup:         snapshot K8s API objects (all resources) + PV data
  2. Restore:        recreate K8s resources from backup in same or different cluster
  3. Migration:      move workloads between clusters (version upgrades, cloud migration)
  4. DR:             recover from cluster failure or accidental deletion

WHAT VELERO BACKS UP:
  Kubernetes Resources:
  - All API objects: Deployments, Services, ConfigMaps, Secrets, PVCs, Namespaces, CRDs, CRs
  - Cluster-scoped: ClusterRoles, ClusterRoleBindings, StorageClasses, CRDs, Namespaces
  - Namespaced:     all objects within selected namespaces

  Persistent Volume Data (2 methods):
  Method 1 — File System Backup (Restic/Kopia):
    - Backs up PV data by streaming files from pod volume mounts
    - Works with any storage backend
    - Slower, requires pod to be running (or opt-in for paused pods)
    - Restic: well-established, deduplicated, encrypted
    - Kopia: newer, faster, better UI

  Method 2 — CSI Volume Snapshot:
    - Uses VolumeSnapshot API (snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1)
    - Storage-level snapshot (much faster — seconds vs minutes)
    - Requires CSI driver with snapshot capability (Longhorn, EBS, etc.)
    - Snapshot stored in cloud provider's snapshot store, not Velero's object storage

VELERO ARCHITECTURE — COMPONENTS:

  velero-deployment       Core server — processes backup/restore operations
  ├── BackupController    Watches Backup CRs, executes backup job
  ├── RestoreController   Watches Restore CRs, executes restore job
  ├── ScheduleController  Watches Schedule CRs, creates Backup on cron
  └── GCController        Garbage-collects expired backups from object store

  restic-daemonset        (or node-agent DaemonSet in newer versions)
                          Runs on every node, mounts pod volumes, streams to object store

  BackupStorageLocation   CR defining object store (S3, GCS, Azure Blob)
  VolumeSnapshotLocation  CR defining where volume snapshots are stored

VELERO BACKUP PROCESS (STEP BY STEP):
  1. User creates Backup CR (or Schedule fires)
  2. BackupController:
     a. Calls Kubernetes API to list all matching resources
     b. Serializes resources to JSON files (tarball)
     c. Executes BackupItemActions plugins (e.g., rewrite PV references)
     d. If file-system backup: node-agent pods stream PV data via Restic/Kopia
     e. If CSI snapshot: calls VolumeSnapshot API, waits for ReadyToUse=true
     f. Uploads tarball + metadata to BackupStorageLocation (S3)
  3. Backup object updated with status: Completed / Failed / PartiallyFailed

VELERO RESTORE PROCESS:
  1. User creates Restore CR pointing to a Backup
  2. RestoreController:
     a. Downloads backup tarball from object store
     b. Filters resources based on restore spec (namespace mapping, label selector)
     c. Executes RestoreItemActions plugins (e.g., rewrite image registry)
     d. Applies resources to Kubernetes API (skips existing by default)
     e. If file-system backup: node-agent restores PV data from object store
     f. If CSI snapshot: creates PVC from VolumeSnapshotContent
  3. Restore object updated with status

BACKUP STORAGE LOCATION (BSL):
  apiVersion: velero.io/v1
  kind: BackupStorageLocation
  metadata:
    name: default
    namespace: velero
  spec:
    provider: aws
    objectStorage:
      bucket: my-velero-backups
      prefix: cluster-prod/
    config:
      region: us-east-1
      s3ForcePathStyle: "false"
      s3Url: ""  # leave empty for AWS S3
    accessMode: ReadWrite   # or ReadOnly (for DR target cluster)
    credential:
      name: cloud-credentials
      key: cloud

VOLUME SNAPSHOT LOCATION (VSL):
  apiVersion: velero.io/v1
  kind: VolumeSnapshotLocation
  metadata:
    name: aws-ebs
    namespace: velero
  spec:
    provider: aws
    config:
      region: us-east-1

BACKUP OBJECT:
  apiVersion: velero.io/v1
  kind: Backup
  metadata:
    name: full-cluster-backup-20240110
    namespace: velero
  spec:
    includedNamespaces: ["*"]          # all namespaces
    excludedNamespaces: [kube-system, longhorn-system]
    includedResources: ["*"]           # all resource types
    excludedResources: [events, events.events.k8s.io]
    storageLocation: default
    volumeSnapshotLocations: [aws-ebs]
    ttl: 720h                          # 30 days retention
    snapshotVolumes: true
    defaultVolumesToFsBackup: false    # prefer CSI snapshots
    labelSelector:
      matchLabels: {}                  # empty = all
    hooks:
      resources: []                    # pre/post backup hooks

BACKUP SCHEDULE:
  apiVersion: velero.io/v1
  kind: Schedule
  metadata:
    name: daily-backup
    namespace: velero
  spec:
    schedule: "0 1 * * *"             # daily at 1am
    template:
      includedNamespaces: ["*"]
      excludedNamespaces: [kube-system, monitoring, longhorn-system]
      storageLocation: default
      ttl: 720h
      snapshotVolumes: true
      defaultVolumesToFsBackup: false
    useOwnerReferencesInBackup: false  # don't block GC of parent objects

PRE/POST BACKUP HOOKS:
  Hooks pause applications for consistent backups (e.g., flush DB, freeze FS):

  metadata:
    annotations:
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/container: postgres
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/command: '["/bin/bash", "-c", "pg_dump -U postgres mydb > /backup/mydb.sql && psql -U postgres -c CHECKPOINT"]'
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/on-error: Fail
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/timeout: 120s
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/container: postgres
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/command: '["/bin/bash", "-c", "rm -f /backup/mydb.sql"]'
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/on-error: Continue

  Hooks can also use exec in exec containers or init containers.

  Spec-level hooks (applied to all pods in a backup):
  spec:
    hooks:
      resources:
      - name: freeze-postgres
        includedNamespaces: [production]
        labelSelector:
          matchLabels:
            app: postgres
        pre:
        - exec:
            container: postgres
            command: ["/bin/bash", "-c", "psql -U postgres -c 'CHECKPOINT; SELECT pg_start_backup(''velero'');'"]
            onError: Fail
            timeout: 30s
        post:
        - exec:
            container: postgres
            command: ["/bin/bash", "-c", "psql -U postgres -c \"SELECT pg_stop_backup();\""]
            onError: Continue
            timeout: 30s

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.3.2 HANDS-ON: INSTALLING AND USING VELERO
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

INSTALL VELERO CLI:
  # macOS
  brew install velero

  # Linux
  curl -Lo velero.tar.gz https://github.com/vmware-tanzu/velero/releases/download/v1.13.0/velero-v1.13.0-linux-amd64.tar.gz
  tar -xzf velero.tar.gz
  mv velero-v1.13.0-linux-amd64/velero /usr/local/bin/
  chmod +x /usr/local/bin/velero

INSTALL VELERO SERVER (AWS S3):
  # Create S3 bucket and IAM policy
  # IAM policy for Velero:
  cat > velero-policy.json << 'EOF'
  {
    "Version": "2012-10-17",
    "Statement": [
      {
        "Effect": "Allow",
        "Action": [
          "ec2:DescribeVolumes", "ec2:DescribeSnapshots",
          "ec2:CreateTags", "ec2:CreateVolume",
          "ec2:CreateSnapshot", "ec2:DeleteSnapshot"
        ],
        "Resource": "*"
      },
      {
        "Effect": "Allow",
        "Action": ["s3:GetObject","s3:DeleteObject","s3:PutObject","s3:AbortMultipartUpload",
                   "s3:ListMultipartUploadParts","s3:ListBucket","s3:ListBucketMultipartUploads",
                   "s3:GetBucketLocation"],
        "Resource": ["arn:aws:s3:::my-velero-backups", "arn:aws:s3:::my-velero-backups/*"]
      }
    ]
  }
  EOF

  # Create credentials file
  cat > credentials-velero << 'EOF'
  [default]
  aws_access_key_id=AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE
  aws_secret_access_key=wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY
  EOF

  # Install Velero with AWS plugin and Restic (node-agent)
  velero install \
    --provider aws \
    --plugins velero/velero-plugin-for-aws:v1.9.0 \
    --bucket my-velero-backups \
    --backup-location-config region=us-east-1 \
    --snapshot-location-config region=us-east-1 \
    --secret-file ./credentials-velero \
    --use-node-agent \
    --default-volumes-to-fs-backup=false \
    --uploader-type=kopia

INSTALL VELERO WITH CSI PLUGIN (for Longhorn snapshots):
  velero install \
    --provider aws \
    --plugins velero/velero-plugin-for-aws:v1.9.0,velero/velero-plugin-for-csi:v0.7.0 \
    --bucket my-velero-backups \
    --backup-location-config region=us-east-1 \
    --snapshot-location-config region=us-east-1 \
    --secret-file ./credentials-velero \
    --use-node-agent \
    --features=EnableCSI \
    --uploader-type=kopia

  # Enable CSI feature flag
  kubectl -n velero patch deployment velero \
    --type=json \
    -p '[{"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/args/-","value":"--features=EnableCSI"}]'

BASIC BACKUP OPERATIONS:
  # Create an ad-hoc backup
  velero backup create my-backup \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --snapshot-volumes

  # Create backup with label selector
  velero backup create app-backup \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --selector app=myapp \
    --ttl 168h

  # Describe backup
  velero backup describe my-backup --details

  # Get backup logs
  velero backup logs my-backup

  # List all backups
  velero backup get

  # Delete a backup
  velero backup delete my-backup

  # Download backup tarball (for inspection)
  velero backup download my-backup

RESTORE OPERATIONS:
  # Restore all namespaces from backup
  velero restore create \
    --from-backup my-backup \
    --wait

  # Restore specific namespace
  velero restore create \
    --from-backup my-backup \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --wait

  # Restore with namespace mapping (migration)
  velero restore create \
    --from-backup my-backup \
    --namespace-mappings production:production-dr \
    --wait

  # Restore specific resources only
  velero restore create \
    --from-backup my-backup \
    --include-resources deployments,services,configmaps \
    --wait

  # Describe restore
  velero restore describe my-restore --details

  # Get restore logs
  velero restore logs my-restore

SCHEDULE OPERATIONS:
  # Create daily backup schedule
  velero schedule create daily-production \
    --schedule "0 2 * * *" \
    --include-namespaces production,staging \
    --ttl 720h \
    --snapshot-volumes

  # List schedules
  velero schedule get

  # Pause/resume a schedule
  velero schedule delete daily-production  # no pause; delete and recreate

  # Force schedule to run now
  velero backup create --from-schedule daily-production

DEBUGGING VELERO:
  # Check Velero server logs
  kubectl logs deployment/velero -n velero

  # Check node-agent logs (for file-system backup issues)
  kubectl logs daemonset/node-agent -n velero

  # Check BSL connectivity
  velero backup-location get
  velero backup-location get default -o yaml

  # Verify plugin loaded
  kubectl -n velero exec deployment/velero -- velero plugin get

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.3.3 REAL-WORLD: VELERO IN PRODUCTION — FULL DR STRATEGY
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

BACKUP STRATEGY MATRIX:
  ┌─────────────────────┬──────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────┐
  │ Resource Type        │ Backup Method    │ Frequency  │ Retention    │
  ├─────────────────────┼──────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────┤
  │ K8s API Objects      │ Velero tarball   │ hourly     │ 7 days       │
  │ Stateful PVs         │ CSI snapshot     │ hourly     │ 7 days       │
  │ Stateful PVs data    │ Kopia/Restic     │ daily      │ 30 days      │
  │ Critical DBs         │ App-level dump   │ 15 min     │ 7 days       │
  │ Cluster config       │ GitOps (ArgoCD)  │ always     │ git history  │
  │ Secrets              │ Vault + Velero   │ daily      │ 90 days      │
  └─────────────────────┴──────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────┘

MULTI-CLUSTER DR SETUP:
  Cluster A (primary):    BSL mode=ReadWrite  → writes backups to S3
  Cluster B (DR standby): BSL mode=ReadOnly   → reads backups from same S3

  # On DR cluster (read-only BSL)
  velero backup-location create default \
    --provider aws \
    --bucket my-velero-backups \
    --config region=us-east-1 \
    --access-mode ReadOnly

  # Sync backups from primary (DR cluster can see backups)
  velero backup get

  # DR drill: restore to DR cluster
  velero restore create production-dr-$(date +%Y%m%d) \
    --from-backup daily-production-20240110020000 \
    --namespace-mappings production:production \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --wait

VELERO WITH LONGHORN CSI SNAPSHOTS (BEST COMBO):
  # Label PVCs to use CSI snapshot (instead of file system backup)
  kubectl annotate pvc postgres-data \
    backup.velero.io/backup-volumes=postgres-data \
    -n production

  # OR: configure globally to prefer CSI snapshots
  # When --features=EnableCSI is set and VolumeSnapshotClass is annotated:
  kubectl annotate volumesnapshotclass longhorn \
    velero.io/csi-volumesnapshot-class=true

  # Now Velero will use CSI snapshot for Longhorn volumes automatically

  # Verify snapshot was taken with CSI
  velero backup describe my-backup --details | grep -A5 "CSI"

VELERO BACKUP HOOKS FOR DATABASES (PRODUCTION PATTERN):

  Database-aware backup using annotations on PostgreSQL StatefulSet:

  metadata:
    annotations:
      # Pre-backup: create consistent checkpoint
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/container: postgres
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/command: >-
        ["/bin/bash", "-c",
         "psql -U $POSTGRES_USER -c 'CHECKPOINT;' &&
          psql -U $POSTGRES_USER -c 'SELECT pg_start_backup(''velero-backup'', true, false);'"]
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/timeout: 60s
      pre.hook.backup.velero.io/on-error: Fail

      # Post-backup: stop backup mode
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/container: postgres
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/command: >-
        ["/bin/bash", "-c",
         "psql -U $POSTGRES_USER -c 'SELECT pg_stop_backup(false, true);'"]
      post.hook.backup.velero.io/on-error: Continue

PROTECTING SECRETS IN VELERO BACKUPS:
  Velero by default includes Secrets in backups (base64 encoded, NOT encrypted at rest in tarball).
  Options:
  1. Encrypt S3 bucket with SSE-KMS
  2. Use Velero encrypt plugin (experimental)
  3. Exclude secrets from Velero, manage separately with Vault or External Secrets Operator
  4. Enable S3 Object Lock on backup bucket (immutability for ransomware protection)

  # Exclude secrets from backup (manage via Vault/ESO)
  velero backup create my-backup \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --exclude-resources secrets \
    --snapshot-volumes

BACKUP VERIFICATION AUTOMATION:
  # Script to verify backup and test restore daily
  #!/bin/bash
  set -euo pipefail

  BACKUP=$(velero backup get --output json | \
    jq -r '[.items[] | select(.status.phase=="Completed")] | sort_by(.metadata.creationTimestamp) | last | .metadata.name')

  echo "Verifying backup: $BACKUP"

  # Create test namespace for restore verification
  kubectl create namespace velero-verify --dry-run=client -o yaml | kubectl apply -f -

  # Restore to test namespace
  velero restore create verify-$(date +%s) \
    --from-backup "$BACKUP" \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --namespace-mappings production:velero-verify \
    --wait

  # Check pods came up
  FAILED=$(kubectl get pods -n velero-verify --field-selector=status.phase!=Running | grep -c "." || true)
  if [[ $FAILED -gt 0 ]]; then
    echo "ERROR: Restore verification failed"
    kubectl get pods -n velero-verify
    exit 1
  fi

  echo "SUCCESS: Backup verified"
  kubectl delete namespace velero-verify

VELERO UPGRADE PROCEDURE:
  1. Scale down Velero deployment (prevents conflicts):
     kubectl scale deployment/velero --replicas=0 -n velero
  2. Upgrade CRDs:
     velero install --crds-only --dry-run  # preview
     kubectl apply -f /path/to/new-crds
  3. Upgrade plugins first (before server):
     kubectl -n velero set image deployment/velero \
       velero-plugin-for-aws=velero/velero-plugin-for-aws:v1.10.0
  4. Upgrade server:
     kubectl -n velero set image deployment/velero \
       velero=velero/velero:v1.13.0
  5. Scale back up:
     kubectl scale deployment/velero --replicas=1 -n velero

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 13.4 — EXPERT: DR ORCHESTRATION, RECLONE, AND ADVANCED PATTERNS
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.4.1 CONCEPTS: RECOVERY TIME & RECOVERY POINT OBJECTIVES
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RTO (Recovery Time Objective):    Maximum acceptable downtime after failure
RPO (Recovery Point Objective):   Maximum acceptable data loss (time window)

DR TIERS:
  Tier 0: Continuous replication (RPO ~0, RTO ~seconds)
          → Database streaming replication, Rook-Ceph with async replication
  Tier 1: Hourly snapshots + standby cluster (RPO ~1hr, RTO ~10min)
          → Longhorn CSI snapshots + Velero schedules
  Tier 2: Daily backup (RPO ~24hr, RTO ~30min)
          → Velero full backup to S3 + restore automation
  Tier 3: Weekly cold backup (RPO ~7days, RTO ~hours)
          → Offline S3 backups, archive tier

RECOVERY SCENARIOS:
  1. Namespace deleted accidentally:
     → Restore single namespace from latest Velero backup
     → RTO: 5-15 minutes
  
  2. StatefulSet PVC corrupted:
     → Restore PVC from Longhorn snapshot (seconds) or Velero file-system backup
     → RTO: 1-30 minutes depending on data size
  
  3. Cluster control plane failure:
     → Restore etcd from backup, or provision new cluster + restore Velero backup
     → RTO: 30-60 minutes
  
  4. Region failure:
     → Activate DR cluster in secondary region, restore from cross-region S3 backups
     → RTO: 1-2 hours

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.4.2 HANDS-ON: ETCD BACKUP AND RESTORE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

ETCD BACKUP (CRITICAL for cluster recovery):
  # On etcd node (or via kubectl exec into etcd pod)
  ETCDCTL_API=3 etcdctl snapshot save /backup/etcd-$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).db \
    --endpoints=https://127.0.0.1:2379 \
    --cacert=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/ca.crt \
    --cert=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/healthcheck-client.crt \
    --key=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/healthcheck-client.key

  # Verify snapshot
  ETCDCTL_API=3 etcdctl snapshot status /backup/etcd-20240110120000.db \
    --write-out=table

  # Upload to S3 after backup
  aws s3 cp /backup/etcd-20240110120000.db \
    s3://my-etcd-backups/cluster-prod/etcd-20240110120000.db

AUTOMATE ETCD BACKUP AS CRONJOB:
  apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: CronJob
  metadata:
    name: etcd-backup
    namespace: kube-system
  spec:
    schedule: "*/30 * * * *"
    jobTemplate:
      spec:
        template:
          spec:
            hostNetwork: true
            hostPID: true
            nodeSelector:
              node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane: ""
            tolerations:
            - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane
              operator: Exists
              effect: NoSchedule
            containers:
            - name: etcd-backup
              image: bitnami/etcd:3.5
              command:
              - /bin/bash
              - -c
              - |
                ETCDCTL_API=3 etcdctl snapshot save /backup/etcd-$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).db \
                  --endpoints=https://127.0.0.1:2379 \
                  --cacert=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/ca.crt \
                  --cert=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/healthcheck-client.crt \
                  --key=/etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd/healthcheck-client.key
                # Retain last 48 snapshots (24 hours at 30-minute intervals)
                ls -t /backup/etcd-*.db | tail -n +49 | xargs -r rm
                # Upload to S3
                aws s3 cp /backup/etcd-$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S).db s3://my-etcd-backups/
              volumeMounts:
              - name: etcd-certs
                mountPath: /etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd
                readOnly: true
              - name: backup-dir
                mountPath: /backup
              env:
              - name: AWS_DEFAULT_REGION
                value: us-east-1
            volumes:
            - name: etcd-certs
              hostPath:
                path: /etc/kubernetes/pki/etcd
            - name: backup-dir
              hostPath:
                path: /var/backups/etcd
            restartPolicy: OnFailure

ETCD RESTORE:
  # 1. Stop kube-apiserver on ALL control plane nodes
  # (move manifests away from /etc/kubernetes/manifests/)
  mv /etc/kubernetes/manifests/kube-apiserver.yaml /tmp/
  mv /etc/kubernetes/manifests/kube-controller-manager.yaml /tmp/
  mv /etc/kubernetes/manifests/kube-scheduler.yaml /tmp/
  mv /etc/kubernetes/manifests/etcd.yaml /tmp/

  # 2. Move old etcd data dir
  mv /var/lib/etcd /var/lib/etcd.bak

  # 3. Restore snapshot
  ETCDCTL_API=3 etcdctl snapshot restore /backup/etcd-20240110120000.db \
    --data-dir=/var/lib/etcd \
    --name=master-01 \
    --initial-cluster=master-01=https://10.0.1.10:2380 \
    --initial-cluster-token=etcd-cluster \
    --initial-advertise-peer-urls=https://10.0.1.10:2380

  # For multi-master restore, restore on EACH node with its own parameters:
  # master-01:
  ETCDCTL_API=3 etcdctl snapshot restore /backup/etcd.db \
    --data-dir=/var/lib/etcd \
    --name=master-01 \
    --initial-cluster="master-01=https://10.0.1.10:2380,master-02=https://10.0.1.11:2380,master-03=https://10.0.1.12:2380" \
    --initial-cluster-token=etcd-cluster \
    --initial-advertise-peer-urls=https://10.0.1.10:2380

  # 4. Fix ownership
  chown -R etcd:etcd /var/lib/etcd   # or appropriate user

  # 5. Restore control plane manifests
  mv /tmp/kube-apiserver.yaml /etc/kubernetes/manifests/
  mv /tmp/kube-controller-manager.yaml /etc/kubernetes/manifests/
  mv /tmp/kube-scheduler.yaml /etc/kubernetes/manifests/
  mv /tmp/etcd.yaml /etc/kubernetes/manifests/

  # 6. Verify cluster
  kubectl get nodes
  kubectl get pods -A

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.4.3 ADVANCED: VELERO WITH KOPIA — EFFICIENT LARGE-SCALE BACKUPS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

KOPIA VS RESTIC:
  Restic:
  - Chunk-based deduplication (content-defined chunking)
  - Global dedup pool across all backed-up hosts
  - Well-established, large community
  - Slower: single-threaded chunks for small files

  Kopia:
  - Content-addressable storage (similar to git objects)
  - Faster: parallel chunking and uploads
  - Better web UI (Kopia UI)
  - More configurable compression and encryption
  - Velero recommends Kopia for new installations

KOPIA COMPRESSION & ENCRYPTION (configured in repository):
  # View Kopia repository settings (on node-agent pod)
  kubectl exec -n velero daemonset/node-agent -- \
    kopia repository status

  # S3 repo initialization parameters passed via Velero:
  # compression: zstd (default), s2, gzip
  # encryption: AES256-GCM-HMAC-SHA256 (default)

OPTIMIZING NODE-AGENT PERFORMANCE:
  # Limit CPU/memory for node-agent to prevent starving workloads
  kubectl patch daemonset/node-agent -n velero \
    --type=json \
    -p='[{"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/resources","value":{"limits":{"cpu":"2","memory":"4Gi"},"requests":{"cpu":"500m","memory":"512Mi"}}}]'

  # Configure parallelism in Velero
  kubectl -n velero patch deployment velero \
    --type=json \
    -p='[{"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/args/-","value":"--fs-backup-timeout=4h"},
         {"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/args/-","value":"--default-backup-storage-location=default"},
         {"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/args/-","value":"--client-burst=100"},
         {"op":"add","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/args/-","value":"--client-qps=100"}]'

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.4.4 REAL-WORLD: COMPLETE DR RUNBOOK
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

SCENARIO: Production cluster (us-east-1) completely down. Activate DR cluster (us-west-2).

RUNBOOK — CLUSTER FAILOVER:

  STEP 1: ASSESS DAMAGE (5 minutes)
  ─────────────────────────────────
  - Confirm cluster is truly unreachable (not just kubectl context issue)
  - Identify last successful backup timestamp
    velero backup get | head -5  # on DR cluster
  - Estimate data loss (now - last backup = RPO gap)
  - Get approval from stakeholders to proceed with failover

  STEP 2: ACTIVATE DR CLUSTER (10 minutes)
  ─────────────────────────────────────────
  # On DR cluster (us-west-2):
  kubectl config use-context cluster-dr-us-west-2

  # Verify DR cluster is healthy
  kubectl get nodes
  kubectl get pods -A | grep -v Running

  # Confirm backup is visible
  velero backup get | grep Completed | head -3

  STEP 3: RESTORE WORKLOADS (15-30 minutes)
  ──────────────────────────────────────────
  # Restore from latest good backup
  LATEST=$(velero backup get --output json | \
    jq -r '[.items[] | select(.status.phase=="Completed")] | \
    sort_by(.metadata.creationTimestamp) | last | .metadata.name')

  echo "Restoring from: $LATEST"

  velero restore create production-failover-$(date +%s) \
    --from-backup "$LATEST" \
    --include-namespaces production,staging \
    --restore-volumes \
    --wait

  # Monitor restore
  velero restore describe production-failover-xxx --details

  STEP 4: VERIFY SERVICES (10 minutes)
  ─────────────────────────────────────
  # Check pods
  kubectl get pods -n production

  # Check PVCs bound
  kubectl get pvc -n production

  # Check services
  kubectl get svc -n production

  # Test critical endpoints
  curl -f https://api.example.com/health || echo "UNHEALTHY"

  STEP 5: REDIRECT TRAFFIC (5 minutes)
  ─────────────────────────────────────
  # Update Route53 (or DNS provider) to point to DR cluster's load balancer
  aws route53 change-resource-record-sets \
    --hosted-zone-id ZXXXXX \
    --change-batch file://dns-failover.json

  # Or update global load balancer (Cloudflare, AWS Global Accelerator)

  STEP 6: NOTIFY STAKEHOLDERS
  ────────────────────────────
  - Send incident update
  - Record actual RTO and RPO
  - Open post-mortem ticket

POST-FAILOVER TASKS:
  - Monitor DR cluster for 24 hours
  - Disable backup schedules on dead primary (avoid split-brain)
  - Plan failback once primary is repaired
  - Conduct post-mortem (why did primary fail, how to prevent)

FAILBACK PROCEDURE (when primary recovers):
  1. Ensure primary cluster healthy
  2. Take fresh backup on DR cluster (capture any new data)
  3. Restore DR backup to primary cluster
  4. Sync and verify data consistency
  5. Schedule maintenance window for DNS cutback
  6. Update Velero BSL on primary to ReadWrite, DR to ReadOnly
  7. Resume normal operations on primary

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.4.5 LONGHORN + VELERO INTEGRATION PATTERNS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

PATTERN 1 — TIERED BACKUPS (recommended production setup):
  Tier 1 (hourly, local): Longhorn recurring snapshots (no external transfer)
    → Fastest restore (seconds), local only, no DR protection

  Tier 2 (daily, remote): Longhorn backups to S3 via Longhorn backup store
    → Longhorn-native restore, no K8s API objects

  Tier 3 (daily, full): Velero backup (K8s objects + CSI snapshots via Longhorn)
    → Full cluster restore including all API objects

PATTERN 2 — VELERO + LONGHORN CSI SNAPSHOT FLOW:
  1. Velero triggers VolumeSnapshot via snapshot.storage.k8s.io/v1 API
  2. Longhorn CSI external-snapshotter creates Longhorn Snapshot
  3. Longhorn exports snapshot blocks to S3 (optional: via Longhorn backup)
  4. Velero stores VolumeSnapshotContent reference in backup metadata
  5. On restore: Velero creates PVC from VolumeSnapshotContent
  6. Longhorn restores volume from CSI snapshot

  This requires: VolumeSnapshotClass annotated with velero.io/csi-volumesnapshot-class=true
  And Longhorn configured with a backup store for cross-cluster restore

PATTERN 3 — NAMESPACE-LEVEL ISOLATION FOR BACKUPS:
  # Backup only production namespace
  velero backup create prod-backup \
    --include-namespaces production \
    --ordered-resources 'persistentvolumes=,persistentvolumeclaims=,secrets=,configmaps=,serviceaccounts=,deployments=,statefulsets=' \
    --snapshot-volumes \
    --default-volumes-to-fs-backup=false

  # Separate schedule for cluster-scoped resources
  velero backup create cluster-resources \
    --include-cluster-resources=true \
    --include-namespaces "" \
    --include-resources clusterroles,clusterrolebindings,storageclasses,crds,namespaces

LONGHORN SNAPSHOT VERIFICATION:
  # Verify snapshot integrity via Longhorn API
  kubectl -n longhorn-system exec deployment/longhorn-driver-deployer -- \
    longhorn-manager snapshot verify \
      --volume pvc-abc123 \
      --snapshot snap-xyz789

  # Check snapshot chain
  kubectl get snapshots.longhorn.io -n longhorn-system \
    -l longhornvolume=pvc-abc123 \
    -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,CREATED:.status.creationTime,SIZE:.status.size

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
13.5 STORAGE MONITORING & ALERTING
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

KEY LONGHORN METRICS (Prometheus):
  longhorn_volume_actual_size_bytes         — actual disk usage per volume
  longhorn_volume_capacity_bytes            — provisioned capacity per volume
  longhorn_volume_robustness{robustness}    — "healthy"/"degraded"/"faulted"
  longhorn_node_storage_capacity_bytes      — total disk capacity per node
  longhorn_node_storage_usage_bytes         — used disk per node
  longhorn_node_storage_reservation_bytes   — reserved for system per node
  longhorn_backup_state{state}              — backup state per volume
  longhorn_snapshot_count                   — number of snapshots per volume

CRITICAL PROMETHEUS ALERTS FOR STORAGE:
  # Volume not healthy
  - alert: LonghornVolumeNotHealthy
    expr: longhorn_volume_robustness{robustness!="healthy"} == 1
    for: 5m
    labels:
      severity: critical
    annotations:
      summary: "Longhorn volume {{ $labels.volume }} is {{ $labels.robustness }}"

  # Node disk almost full
  - alert: LonghornNodeDiskAlmostFull
    expr: >
      (longhorn_node_storage_usage_bytes /
       longhorn_node_storage_capacity_bytes) > 0.85
    for: 10m
    labels:
      severity: warning
    annotations:
      summary: "Node {{ $labels.node }} disk {{ $labels.disk }} is 85%+ full"

  # Backup failed
  - alert: LonghornBackupFailed
    expr: longhorn_backup_state{state=~"Error|Unknown"} == 1
    for: 0m
    labels:
      severity: critical
    annotations:
      summary: "Longhorn backup failed for volume {{ $labels.volume }}"

  # Velero backup failed (from Velero metrics)
  - alert: VeleroBackupFailed
    expr: velero_backup_failure_total > 0
    for: 0m
    labels:
      severity: critical
    annotations:
      summary: "Velero backup has failed"

VELERO METRICS:
  # Velero exposes Prometheus metrics on port 8085
  velero_backup_total                   — total backup count
  velero_backup_success_total           — successful backups
  velero_backup_failure_total           — failed backups
  velero_backup_partial_failure_total   — partial failures
  velero_backup_duration_seconds        — backup duration histogram
  velero_restore_total                  — total restore attempts
  velero_restore_success_total          — successful restores
  velero_restore_failed_total           — failed restores
  velero_volume_snapshot_success_total  — successful volume snapshots
  velero_volume_snapshot_failure_total  — failed volume snapshots

GRAFANA DASHBOARD QUERIES:
  # Storage fill rate (predict when disk will be full)
  predict_linear(
    longhorn_node_storage_usage_bytes{node="worker-01"}[1h],
    4 * 3600  # predict 4 hours ahead
  ) / longhorn_node_storage_capacity_bytes{node="worker-01"}

  # Backup age (hours since last successful backup)
  (time() - max(velero_backup_last_successful_timestamp)) / 3600

  # Volume IOPS (from node exporter + volume labels)
  rate(node_disk_reads_completed_total[5m]) + rate(node_disk_writes_completed_total[5m])

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
