SECTION 15.3 — ADVANCED: ANSIBLE AT SCALE AND COMPLEX PATTERNS
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.3.1 CONCEPTS: ADVANCED EXECUTION AND DELEGATION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

STRATEGY PLUGINS:
  linear    — default: run each task on all hosts before moving to next
  free      — each host runs at its own pace (faster, less predictable)
  debug     — interactive debugger (pause on each task)
  host_pinned — like free but limits parallelism per host

  # Per-play strategy
  - hosts: webservers
    strategy: free
    tasks: [...]

SERIAL — ROLLING UPDATES:
  Control how many hosts run in parallel:

  - hosts: webservers
    serial: 1              # one at a time (safest)
    # serial: 2            # two at a time
    # serial: "20%"        # 20% of hosts at a time
    # serial: [1, 5, "50%"]  # 1 first, then 5, then 50% (progressive rollout)
    max_fail_percentage: 30  # abort if >30% of hosts fail
    tasks:
    - name: drain from LB
      uri:
        url: "http://lb.internal/drain/{{ inventory_hostname }}"
        method: POST
    - name: deploy app
      # ...
    - name: add back to LB
      uri:
        url: "http://lb.internal/add/{{ inventory_hostname }}"
        method: POST

DELEGATION:
  Run a task on a different host than the current target:

  # Run on load balancer while iterating over web servers
  - name: Drain server from LB
    command: /usr/local/bin/lb-drain {{ inventory_hostname }}
    delegate_to: loadbalancer.example.com

  # Run on localhost (control node)
  - name: Record deployment event
    uri:
      url: https://api.pagerduty.com/events
      method: POST
      body: "{{ event_payload | to_json }}"
    delegate_to: localhost

  # delegate_facts: true — store gathered facts under the original host
  - name: Gather facts from DB server
    setup:
    delegate_to: db-01
    delegate_facts: true

RUN_ONCE — TASKS THAT RUN ONCE FOR A PLAY:
  - name: Create database schema
    community.postgresql.postgresql_db:
      name: myapp
      state: present
    run_once: true           # run on first host in group only
    delegate_to: db-01       # run on db server, not on current host

ASYNC TASKS — FIRE AND FORGET:
  - name: Run long backup (async)
    command: /usr/bin/backup.sh
    async: 3600    # max runtime seconds
    poll: 0        # 0 = don't wait, fire and forget

  - name: Check backup job
    async_status:
      jid: "{{ backup_job.ansible_job_id }}"
    register: job_result
    until: job_result.finished
    retries: 30
    delay: 60      # check every 60 seconds

UNTIL / RETRIES — WAIT FOR CONDITION:
  - name: Wait for service to be ready
    uri:
      url: http://localhost:8080/health
      return_content: true
    register: health_check
    until: health_check.status == 200
    retries: 30
    delay: 10

  - name: Wait for port to be open
    wait_for:
      host: "{{ ansible_host }}"
      port: 5432
      timeout: 300

  - name: Wait for cloud instance
    wait_for_connection:
      timeout: 300
      delay: 10

TAGS — SELECTIVE EXECUTION:
  # Tag tasks, roles, blocks, plays
  tasks:
  - name: Install packages
    apt:
      name: nginx
    tags: [install, nginx]

  - name: Configure nginx
    template:
      src: nginx.conf.j2
      dest: /etc/nginx/nginx.conf
    tags: [configure, nginx]

  # Apply tags to a role
  roles:
  - role: nginx
    tags: [nginx]

  # Run only 'configure' tagged tasks
  ansible-playbook site.yml --tags configure

  # Special tags:
  # always   → always runs (even with --skip-tags)
  # never    → only runs when explicitly specified with --tags
  # tagged   → run all tagged tasks
  # untagged → run all untagged tasks

INCLUDES VS IMPORTS:
  import_tasks / import_role / import_playbook:
    - Static: processed at playbook parse time
    - Tags and conditionals from parent apply to imported content
    - Cannot use with loops or dynamic variables

  include_tasks / include_role:
    - Dynamic: processed at runtime
    - Can use with loops, when conditions, vars
    - Tags must be applied directly to include statement

  # Dynamic include with loop
  - include_tasks: "configure_{{ item }}.yml"
    loop: [nginx, postgres, redis]

  # Import (static, tags work through)
  - import_tasks: configure_nginx.yml
    tags: [nginx]

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.3.2 HANDS-ON: ROLLING DEPLOYMENTS AND ORCHESTRATION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

ROLLING APPLICATION DEPLOYMENT:
  # deploy-app.yml
  ---
  - hosts: webservers
    serial: "25%"          # deploy to 25% of servers at a time
    max_fail_percentage: 0 # abort immediately if any host fails
    gather_facts: false

    vars:
      app_version: "{{ version | mandatory }}"   # must pass -e version=1.2.3
      app_deploy_dir: /opt/myapp
      app_user: appuser

    tasks:
    - name: Remove from load balancer
      uri:
        url: "http://{{ lb_host }}/api/servers/{{ inventory_hostname }}/drain"
        method: PUT
        status_code: 200
      delegate_to: localhost

    - name: Wait for connections to drain
      pause:
        seconds: 30

    - name: Download new version
      get_url:
        url: "https://artifacts.example.com/releases/{{ app_version }}/app.tar.gz"
        dest: /tmp/app-{{ app_version }}.tar.gz
        checksum: "sha256:{{ app_checksum }}"
        mode: '0644'

    - name: Extract to deploy dir
      unarchive:
        src: /tmp/app-{{ app_version }}.tar.gz
        dest: "{{ app_deploy_dir }}"
        remote_src: true
        owner: "{{ app_user }}"
        group: "{{ app_user }}"

    - name: Run database migrations (once, on first host)
      command: "{{ app_deploy_dir }}/bin/migrate"
      run_once: true
      delegate_to: "{{ groups['webservers'] | first }}"
      environment:
        DATABASE_URL: "{{ db_url }}"

    - name: Restart application
      systemd:
        name: myapp
        state: restarted
        daemon_reload: true

    - name: Wait for application to be healthy
      uri:
        url: "http://localhost:8080/health"
        return_content: true
      register: health
      until: health.status == 200 and (health.content | from_json).status == "ok"
      retries: 12
      delay: 10

    - name: Re-add to load balancer
      uri:
        url: "http://{{ lb_host }}/api/servers/{{ inventory_hostname }}/enable"
        method: PUT
        status_code: 200
      delegate_to: localhost

    - name: Clean up old archive
      file:
        path: "/tmp/app-{{ app_version }}.tar.gz"
        state: absent

OS PATCHING PLAYBOOK:
  # patch-os.yml — patch servers one at a time
  ---
  - hosts: all
    serial: 1
    gather_facts: true

    tasks:
    - name: Update all packages (apt)
      apt:
        upgrade: dist
        update_cache: true
        autoclean: true
        autoremove: true
      when: ansible_os_family == "Debian"
      register: apt_result

    - name: Update all packages (yum/dnf)
      dnf:
        name: "*"
        state: latest
        update_only: true
      when: ansible_os_family == "RedHat"
      register: dnf_result

    - name: Check if reboot needed (Debian)
      stat:
        path: /var/run/reboot-required
      register: reboot_required
      when: ansible_os_family == "Debian"

    - name: Reboot if needed
      reboot:
        reboot_timeout: 300
        test_command: whoami
      when:
      - ansible_os_family == "Debian"
      - reboot_required.stat.exists

USER AND SSH KEY MANAGEMENT:
  # users.yml
  ---
  - hosts: all
    become: true
    vars_files:
    - group_vars/all/users.yml  # list of user specs

    tasks:
    - name: Create users
      user:
        name: "{{ item.name }}"
        uid: "{{ item.uid }}"
        comment: "{{ item.full_name }}"
        shell: /bin/bash
        groups: "{{ item.groups | default([]) }}"
        append: true
        state: "{{ item.state | default('present') }}"
        password: "{{ item.password_hash | default('!') }}"
        update_password: on_create
      loop: "{{ users }}"
      loop_control:
        label: "{{ item.name }}"

    - name: Set up authorized keys
      authorized_key:
        user: "{{ item.name }}"
        key: "{{ item.ssh_key }}"
        exclusive: true     # remove all other keys not in this list
        state: present
      loop: "{{ users | selectattr('state', 'ne', 'absent') | list }}"
      loop_control:
        label: "{{ item.name }}"

    - name: Configure sudoers
      copy:
        dest: "/etc/sudoers.d/{{ item.name }}"
        content: "{{ item.name }} ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL\n"
        mode: '0440'
        validate: visudo -cf %s
      loop: "{{ users | selectattr('sudo', 'equalto', true) | list }}"
      loop_control:
        label: "{{ item.name }}"

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.3.3 REAL-WORLD: ANSIBLE FOR KUBERNETES NODE MANAGEMENT
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

CONFIGURING KUBERNETES NODES WITH ANSIBLE:

  # k8s-nodes.yml — prepare nodes for Kubernetes (for RKE2 or kubeadm)
  ---
  - hosts: k8s_nodes
    become: true

    vars:
      k8s_version: "1.29"
      cni_cidr: "10.244.0.0/16"
      kubelet_extra_args: |
        KUBELET_EXTRA_ARGS=--max-pods=110 --node-labels=node.kubernetes.io/role=worker

    tasks:
    - name: Disable swap
      command: swapoff -a
      changed_when: false

    - name: Remove swap from fstab
      replace:
        path: /etc/fstab
        regexp: '^([^#].*\s+swap\s+.*)$'
        replace: '# \1'

    - name: Load required kernel modules
      modprobe:
        name: "{{ item }}"
        state: present
      loop:
      - overlay
      - br_netfilter

    - name: Persist kernel modules
      copy:
        dest: /etc/modules-load.d/k8s.conf
        content: |
          overlay
          br_netfilter

    - name: Set sysctl parameters for Kubernetes
      sysctl:
        name: "{{ item.name }}"
        value: "{{ item.value }}"
        state: present
        reload: true
      loop:
      - { name: net.bridge.bridge-nf-call-iptables,  value: "1" }
      - { name: net.bridge.bridge-nf-call-ip6tables, value: "1" }
      - { name: net.ipv4.ip_forward,                 value: "1" }
      - { name: fs.inotify.max_user_watches,         value: "524288" }
      - { name: fs.inotify.max_user_instances,       value: "512" }
      - { name: vm.max_map_count,                    value: "262144" }

    - name: Install container runtime (containerd)
      apt:
        name:
        - containerd
        - runc
        state: present
        update_cache: true

    - name: Configure containerd
      shell: containerd config default | tee /etc/containerd/config.toml
      changed_when: false

    - name: Enable SystemdCgroup in containerd
      replace:
        path: /etc/containerd/config.toml
        regexp: 'SystemdCgroup = false'
        replace: 'SystemdCgroup = true'
      notify: restart containerd

    - name: Install open-iscsi for Longhorn
      apt:
        name: open-iscsi
        state: present
      notify: enable iscsid

    handlers:
    - name: restart containerd
      service:
        name: containerd
        state: restarted
        enabled: true

    - name: enable iscsid
      service:
        name: iscsid
        state: started
        enabled: true

ANSIBLE FOR KUBERNETES OBJECTS (kubernetes.core):
  # Apply Kubernetes manifests with Ansible
  - name: Create namespace
    kubernetes.core.k8s:
      api_version: v1
      kind: Namespace
      name: production
      state: present
      kubeconfig: /etc/kubernetes/admin.conf

  - name: Deploy application
    kubernetes.core.k8s:
      state: present
      definition: "{{ lookup('template', 'deployment.yaml.j2') | from_yaml }}"
      kubeconfig: /etc/kubernetes/admin.conf

  - name: Scale deployment
    kubernetes.core.k8s_scale:
      api_version: apps/v1
      kind: Deployment
      name: myapp
      namespace: production
      replicas: 5
      wait: true

  - name: Wait for deployment ready
    kubernetes.core.k8s_info:
      api_version: apps/v1
      kind: Deployment
      name: myapp
      namespace: production
    register: deploy_info
    until:
    - deploy_info.resources | length > 0
    - deploy_info.resources[0].status.readyReplicas is defined
    - deploy_info.resources[0].status.readyReplicas == deploy_info.resources[0].spec.replicas
    retries: 30
    delay: 10

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 15.4 — EXPERT: CUSTOM MODULES, PLUGINS, AND AWX/TOWER
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.4.1 CONCEPTS: CUSTOM MODULES AND PLUGIN TYPES
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

CUSTOM MODULE STRUCTURE:
  A module is a Python script that receives JSON args from stdin
  and returns JSON to stdout.

  #!/usr/bin/python3
  # library/my_module.py

  from ansible.module_utils.basic import AnsibleModule

  def run_module():
      module_args = dict(
          name=dict(type='str', required=True),
          state=dict(type='str', default='present', choices=['present', 'absent']),
          value=dict(type='int', required=False, default=0),
      )

      result = dict(
          changed=False,
          name='',
          value=0,
          message='',
      )

      module = AnsibleModule(
          argument_spec=module_args,
          supports_check_mode=True,  # honor --check flag
      )

      name  = module.params['name']
      state = module.params['state']

      # Check current state
      current_state = get_current_state(name)  # your logic here

      if module.check_mode:
          # Don't make changes in check mode
          result['changed'] = (current_state != state)
          module.exit_json(**result)

      # Make actual changes
      if state == 'present' and current_state != 'present':
          do_create(name)
          result['changed'] = True
          result['message'] = f"Created {name}"
      elif state == 'absent' and current_state == 'present':
          do_delete(name)
          result['changed'] = True
          result['message'] = f"Deleted {name}"

      module.exit_json(**result)

  def main():
      run_module()

  if __name__ == '__main__':
      main()

PLUGIN TYPES:
  connection:   how to connect to managed nodes (ssh, winrm, local, docker, kubectl)
  callback:     hook into playbook events (custom output, notifications)
  filter:       custom Jinja2 filters (| my_custom_filter)
  lookup:       fetch data from external sources ({{ lookup('my_lookup', 'key') }})
  vars:         dynamic variable loading
  inventory:    custom inventory sources
  action:       complex task logic (runs on control node)
  become:       privilege escalation methods (sudo, su, doas)

CUSTOM FILTER PLUGIN:
  # filter_plugins/custom_filters.py
  from ansible.errors import AnsibleError

  def to_cidr_list(networks):
      """Convert list of dicts with network/prefix to CIDR strings"""
      result = []
      for net in networks:
          result.append(f"{net['network']}/{net['prefix']}")
      return result

  def mask_password(value, visible_chars=4):
      """Mask a password, showing only first N chars"""
      if len(value) <= visible_chars:
          return '*' * len(value)
      return value[:visible_chars] + '*' * (len(value) - visible_chars)

  class FilterModule(object):
      def filters(self):
          return {
              'to_cidr_list': to_cidr_list,
              'mask_password': mask_password,
          }

  # Usage in playbook:
  # {{ my_networks | to_cidr_list }}
  # {{ my_password | mask_password }}

CUSTOM LOOKUP PLUGIN:
  # lookup_plugins/vault_kv.py
  from ansible.plugins.lookup import LookupBase
  import hvac

  class LookupModule(LookupBase):
      def run(self, terms, variables=None, **kwargs):
          client = hvac.Client(url=kwargs.get('url'))
          client.token = kwargs.get('token')
          results = []
          for term in terms:
              path, key = term.rsplit(':', 1)
              secret = client.secrets.kv.v2.read_secret_version(path=path)
              results.append(secret['data']['data'][key])
          return results

  # Usage:
  # {{ lookup('vault_kv', 'secret/prod/db:password', url='https://vault.example.com', token=vault_token) }}

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.4.2 HANDS-ON: MOLECULE — TESTING ANSIBLE ROLES
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

WHAT MOLECULE IS:
Molecule is a testing framework for Ansible roles. It:
  1. Creates a test environment (Docker, Vagrant, EC2, etc.)
  2. Applies the role
  3. Runs a linter (ansible-lint)
  4. Runs idempotency check (applies role twice, confirms no changes on 2nd run)
  5. Runs verifier (Testinfra or Ansible-based assertions)
  6. Destroys the environment

INSTALL:
  pip install molecule molecule-docker ansible-lint testinfra

INITIALIZE A ROLE WITH MOLECULE:
  # Create new role with molecule
  molecule init role myrole --driver-name docker
  # OR add molecule to existing role:
  cd roles/nginx
  molecule init scenario --driver-name docker

MOLECULE DIRECTORY STRUCTURE:
  roles/nginx/
  └── molecule/
      └── default/
          ├── molecule.yml        ← scenario config
          ├── converge.yml        ← playbook that applies the role
          ├── verify.yml          ← verification tests
          └── prepare.yml         ← (optional) pre-test setup

MOLECULE.YML:
  ---
  dependency:
    name: galaxy

  driver:
    name: docker

  platforms:
  - name: ubuntu-22-04
    image: geerlingguy/docker-ubuntu2204-ansible:latest
    pre_build_image: true
    command: /lib/systemd/systemd
    privileged: true
    volumes:
    - /sys/fs/cgroup:/sys/fs/cgroup:rw
    cgroupns_mode: host

  - name: ubuntu-20-04
    image: geerlingguy/docker-ubuntu2004-ansible:latest
    pre_build_image: true

  provisioner:
    name: ansible
    config_options:
      defaults:
        interpreter_python: auto_silent
    options:
      vvv: false

  verifier:
    name: ansible     # or testinfra

  lint: |
    set -e
    yamllint .
    ansible-lint

CONVERGE.YML:
  ---
  - name: Converge
    hosts: all
    become: true

    roles:
    - role: nginx
      vars:
        nginx_vhosts:
        - name: test-site
          server_name: test.example.com
          root: /var/www/html

VERIFY.YML (ansible-based):
  ---
  - name: Verify
    hosts: all
    become: true
    gather_facts: false

    tasks:
    - name: Check nginx is running
      service_facts:
      register: services_state

    - name: Assert nginx is running
      assert:
        that:
        - "'nginx' in services_state.ansible_facts.services"
        - "services_state.ansible_facts.services['nginx'].state == 'running'"
        fail_msg: "nginx is not running"

    - name: Test HTTP response
      uri:
        url: http://localhost
        return_content: true
      register: http_response

    - name: Assert HTTP OK
      assert:
        that:
        - http_response.status == 200
        fail_msg: "HTTP response was {{ http_response.status }}"

    - name: Check config file exists
      stat:
        path: /etc/nginx/nginx.conf
      register: conf_file

    - name: Assert config file present
      assert:
        that: conf_file.stat.exists
        fail_msg: "nginx.conf not found"

RUNNING MOLECULE:
  # Run full test suite
  molecule test

  # Individual phases
  molecule create        # create containers
  molecule converge      # apply role
  molecule idempotence   # check idempotency
  molecule verify        # run verify.yml
  molecule destroy       # tear down

  # Login to container for debugging
  molecule login --host ubuntu-22-04

  # Run tests against specific scenario
  molecule test --scenario-name ubuntu22

  # Run lint only
  molecule lint

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.4.3 AWX / ANSIBLE TOWER — ENTERPRISE ANSIBLE PLATFORM
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

WHAT AWX IS:
AWX is the open-source upstream of Red Hat Ansible Automation Platform (AAP/Tower).
It provides:
  - Web UI for running Ansible playbooks
  - RBAC — teams/orgs/permissions model
  - Job scheduling and recurring jobs
  - Centralized inventory management
  - Credentials vault (SSH keys, passwords, cloud credentials)
  - Workflow templates — chain multiple job templates
  - REST API + CLI (awx CLI)
  - Webhooks to trigger jobs from GitHub/GitLab/CI

AWX OBJECTS:
  Organization       — top-level grouping (like tenants)
  Team               — group of users within an org
  Credential         — stored secret (SSH key, AWS creds, vault password)
  Inventory          — hosts + groups (static or from dynamic source)
  Project            — Git repository containing playbooks
  Job Template       — playbook + inventory + credentials + extra vars
  Job                — execution of a Job Template
  Workflow Template  — DAG of Job Templates + approvals
  Notification       — alerts to Slack/email/webhook on job events
  Schedule           — cron-based job scheduling

AWX WORKFLOW TEMPLATES (DAG):
  Visual DAG connecting job templates:
    [Provision Nodes] → (success) → [Configure Base] → (success) → [Deploy App]
                                                                   ↓ (failure)
                                                              [Notify Team]

  Each node can have: success path, failure path, always path.
  Approval gates: pause workflow and require human approval before continuing.

AWX INSTALL (on Kubernetes via AWX Operator):
  # Install AWX Operator
  kubectl apply -k https://github.com/ansible/awx-operator/config/default?ref=2.17.0

  # Create AWX instance
  apiVersion: awx.ansible.com/v1beta1
  kind: AWX
  metadata:
    name: awx
    namespace: awx
  spec:
    service_type: ClusterIP
    ingress_type: ingress
    hostname: awx.example.com
    admin_user: admin
    admin_password_secret: awx-admin-password
    postgres_storage_class: longhorn
    web_replicas: 1
    task_replicas: 1
    resource_requirements:
      web:
        requests:
          cpu: 500m
          memory: 1Gi
        limits:
          cpu: 1000m
          memory: 2Gi
      task:
        requests:
          cpu: 500m
          memory: 2Gi
        limits:
          cpu: 2000m
          memory: 4Gi

AWX CLI USAGE:
  pip install awxkit

  # Login
  awx login --conf.host https://awx.example.com \
            --conf.username admin \
            --conf.password mypassword

  # List job templates
  awx job_templates list --all

  # Launch a job
  awx job_templates launch "Deploy Production App" \
    --extra_vars '{"version": "1.2.3"}' \
    --wait \
    --interval 5

  # Get job output
  awx jobs stdout <job_id>

  # List recent jobs
  awx jobs list --order_by -created --page_size 10

  # Create inventory
  awx inventory create \
    --name "Production" \
    --organization "Default" \
    --variables '{"env": "production"}'

AWX WEBHOOK TRIGGER (from GitHub Actions/GitLab CI):
  # In AWX: create Job Template with webhook enabled
  # Get the webhook URL: https://awx.example.com/api/v2/job_templates/{id}/github/

  # In GitHub Actions:
  - name: Trigger AWX deployment
    run: |
      curl -X POST \
        -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
        -H "X-GitHub-Event: push" \
        -H "X-Hub-Signature: sha1=$(echo -n '${{ github.event.ref }}' | openssl sha1 -hmac '${{ secrets.AWX_WEBHOOK_KEY }}' | awk '{print $2}')" \
        https://awx.example.com/api/v2/job_templates/42/github/ \
        -d '{"ref": "${{ github.ref }}", "after": "${{ github.sha }}"}'

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
15.4.4 REAL-WORLD: ANSIBLE BEST PRACTICES AND ANTI-PATTERNS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

BEST PRACTICES:

  1. IDEMPOTENCY FIRST
     - Always use modules, not shell/command, when a module exists
     - Add creates= or when: to shell/command to make them idempotent
     - Test idempotency with molecule idempotence

  2. SECRETS MANAGEMENT
     - Never commit plaintext secrets to Git
     - Use ansible-vault for secrets in repos
     - Prefer external vault (HashiCorp Vault) for production
     - Use --vault-password-file pointing to a file outside the repo

  3. VARIABLE PRECEDENCE DISCIPLINE
     - role/defaults/main.yml: all role defaults (always overridable)
     - group_vars/all.yml: site-wide defaults
     - group_vars/{group}.yml: group-specific vars
     - host_vars/{host}.yml: host-specific overrides
     - Never use role/vars/main.yml for user-configurable vars

  4. TASK NAMING
     - Every task must have a name: string
     - Use present tense, active voice: "Install nginx", not "nginx installation"
     - Name must be unique per play (for idempotency logs)

  5. TAGGING STRATEGY
     - Tag all tasks by component and action: tags: [nginx, configure]
     - Always tag role imports: import_role + tags: [nginx]
     - Use never tag for destructive tasks: tags: [never, nuke-db]

  6. TESTING WITH MOLECULE
     - Every role should have a molecule test scenario
     - Test on multiple OS versions
     - Include idempotency check in CI

  7. LINT WITH ANSIBLE-LINT
     - Run ansible-lint in CI on every PR
     - Use .ansible-lint config to tune rules
     - Address all CRITICAL/HIGH findings before merge

ANTI-PATTERNS TO AVOID:
  ❌ Using shell: for things modules can do (not idempotent, no error handling)
  ❌ ignore_errors: true everywhere (hides real problems)
  ❌ Hardcoding host names in playbooks (use group names)
  ❌ Using vars/ instead of defaults/ in roles (makes roles unoverridable)
  ❌ One giant playbook file (split into roles + task files)
  ❌ Not testing roles (no molecule = untested automation)
  ❌ Committing vault passwords or SSH keys
  ❌ Using raw: or shell: without changed_when: (marks everything as changed)
  ❌ No become: escalation control (either all sudo or explicitly specified)

  # Fix changed_when for shell tasks:
  - name: Check if service needs restart
    shell: systemctl is-active myservice
    register: service_status
    changed_when: false    # gathering info, not changing state
    failed_when: service_status.rc not in [0, 3]  # 0=active, 3=inactive

ANSIBLE-LINT CONFIGURATION:
  # .ansible-lint
  warn_list:
  - experimental

  skip_list:
  - yaml[truthy]      # allow yes/no
  - name[template]    # allow {{ }} in names

  exclude_paths:
  - .git/
  - molecule/

  use_default_rules: true

  rulesdir: []

  parseable: true
  quiet: false
  strict: false

  offline: false

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
PHASE 15 CHECKLIST
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

ANSIBLE FUNDAMENTALS:
  □ Understand agentless architecture (SSH + Python modules)
  □ Know how pipelining improves performance
  □ Explain variable precedence order (all 19 levels)
  □ Understand idempotency and when it breaks (shell/command)
  □ Configure ansible.cfg with pipelining, ControlMaster, fact caching
  □ Write static and dynamic inventory (aws_ec2 plugin)
  □ Use ad-hoc commands for quick operations

PLAYBOOKS AND TASKS:
  □ Write complete playbooks with handlers, tags, and conditions
  □ Use all loop types (loop, loop_control, dict2items)
  □ Use block/rescue/always for error handling
  □ Understand import_tasks vs include_tasks trade-offs
  □ Use delegation (delegate_to, run_once) for orchestration
  □ Implement rolling updates with serial and max_fail_percentage
  □ Use async tasks with async_status for long-running operations
  □ Write until/retries for health check polling

ROLES:
  □ Build a complete role with tasks/handlers/templates/defaults/meta
  □ Understand defaults/ vs vars/ precedence
  □ Use include_vars for OS-specific variables
  □ Apply Jinja2 templates with loops, conditionals, and filters
  □ Use ansible-galaxy to install and publish roles/collections

SECRETS:
  □ Encrypt files and strings with ansible-vault
  □ Use multiple vault IDs for different environments
  □ Integrate with HashiCorp Vault via lookup plugin

TESTING:
  □ Initialize molecule scenario for a role
  □ Write converge.yml and verify.yml
  □ Run full molecule test cycle (create/converge/idempotence/verify/destroy)
  □ Run ansible-lint in CI pipeline

AWX/TOWER:
  □ Understand AWX object model (org/team/credential/inventory/project/template)
  □ Install AWX via operator on Kubernetes
  □ Create job templates and launch via CLI
  □ Build workflow templates with success/failure paths
  □ Configure webhook triggers from GitHub/GitLab

KUBERNETES INTEGRATION:
  □ Prepare K8s nodes (kernel modules, sysctl, containerd, swap) with Ansible
  □ Use kubernetes.core collection to manage K8s objects
  □ Write deployment automation with rollout + health check

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 16.1 — FOUNDATION: RKE2 ARCHITECTURE AND DESIGN PHILOSOPHY
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.1.1 CONCEPTS: WHAT RKE2 IS AND WHY IT EXISTS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

WHAT RKE2 IS:
RKE2 (Rancher Kubernetes Engine 2, also called "RKE Government") is a fully
conformant, production-grade Kubernetes distribution focused on security and
compliance. It is the successor to RKE1, rebuilt from scratch with different
architectural principles.

RKE2 KEY DESIGN GOALS:
  1. Security-hardened by default:
     - CIS Kubernetes Benchmark compliance out of the box
     - Pod Security Standards enforced at cluster level
     - etcd encrypted at rest (secretbox/AES-CBC)
     - All components run inside containerd (no Docker dependency)
     - Minimal kernel modifications

  2. Simplified operations:
     - Single binary for server + agent
     - Self-contained: bundles all required components
     - No external dependency on Docker daemon
     - Helm charts for add-ons (CNI, kube-proxy, CoreDNS) managed internally

  3. Air-gapped support:
     - Designed for disconnected/air-gapped environments
     - All images bundled as tarball (rke2-images.tar.zst)
     - Can run completely offline after bootstrap

RKE2 VS RKE1 VS K3S:

  RKE1:
    - Older distribution, Docker-based
    - Config via cluster.yml, uses RKE as controller
    - Still widely used but in maintenance mode
    - Not as security-hardened as RKE2

  RKE2:
    - containerd-native (no Docker)
    - CIS hardened by default
    - systemd-native (no RKE controller needed)
    - Suitable for government/financial/compliance environments
    - Production-focused

  K3s:
    - Lightweight (< 100MB binary)
    - SQLite or embedded etcd
    - Designed for edge, IoT, dev
    - Less hardened than RKE2
    - Single-node or small clusters

  RKE2 vs kubeadm:
    - kubeadm: just a bootstrapper, user installs/manages all components
    - RKE2: full distribution — installs, bundles, hardens, and manages everything
    - RKE2 has built-in HA etcd bootstrap, kubeadm requires separate etcd setup

RKE2 BUNDLED COMPONENTS:
  containerd          — container runtime (CRI)
  runc                — low-level OCI container runner
  etcd                — cluster state store (embedded, clustered)
  kube-apiserver      — Kubernetes API server
  kube-controller-manager
  kube-scheduler
  kubelet
  kube-proxy          — (optional, can disable for Cilium)
  CoreDNS             — cluster DNS (deployed as pod via Helm chart)
  CNI: Canal          — default CNI (Flannel + Calico NetworkPolicy)
       Calico         — alternative
       Cilium         — alternative (eBPF)
  Ingress: NGINX      — default Ingress controller (optional)
  Metrics Server      — optional add-on
  Helm controller     — manages Helm charts as HelmChart CRDs

EVERYTHING RUNS UNDER CONTAINERD:
  In RKE2, even etcd, kube-apiserver, kube-controller-manager, and kube-scheduler
  run as static pods inside containerd — they are NOT system processes like in
  bare kubeadm. This means:
    - Clean uninstall: delete RKE2, all components gone
    - Consistent restart: systemd restarts RKE2 binary, which restarts everything
    - Resource limits: can apply containerd resource constraints to control plane pods

RKE2 PROCESS MODEL:
  systemd → rke2-server (single binary)
           ├── etcd (embedded, static pod in containerd)
           ├── kube-apiserver (static pod in containerd)
           ├── kube-controller-manager (static pod in containerd)
           ├── kube-scheduler (static pod in containerd)
           ├── kubelet (child process, manages all other pods)
           └── kube-proxy (pod managed by kubelet)

  On agent nodes:
  systemd → rke2-agent (single binary)
           ├── containerd (runs pods)
           └── kubelet (child process)

RKE2 DATA DIRECTORY:
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/
  ├── agent/
  │   ├── containerd/         ← containerd socket and data
  │   ├── images/             ← bundled images
  │   ├── pod-manifests/      ← static pod manifests (control plane)
  │   └── etc/                ← kubelet config, kubeconfig
  ├── server/
  │   ├── db/                 ← etcd data directory
  │   ├── cred/               ← certificates and tokens
  │   ├── manifests/          ← auto-deployed manifests (HelmChart CRDs)
  │   ├── static/             ← static assets
  │   └── tls/                ← TLS certificates for all components
  └── data/
      └── {version}/          ← RKE2 versioned binaries

RKE2 CERTIFICATES:
  RKE2 generates all cluster certificates at bootstrap time.
  Stored in /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/.

  Certificates include:
  - etcd peer + client certs
  - kube-apiserver serving cert
  - kube-apiserver client cert (for talking to kubelet)
  - kube-controller-manager client cert
  - kube-scheduler client cert
  - kubelet serving cert (per node)
  - front-proxy CA + client cert
  - Service Account signing key pair

  Certificate rotation:
    rke2 certificate rotate         # rotate all certs
    rke2 certificate rotate --service kube-apiserver  # rotate specific cert
    # Restart RKE2 after rotation

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.1.2 HANDS-ON: SINGLE-NODE RKE2 INSTALLATION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

PREREQUISITES:
  # OS: Ubuntu 22.04 / RHEL 9 / Rocky Linux 9 (recommended)
  # Min resources per node: 2 vCPU, 4GB RAM, 20GB disk

  # Disable swap
  swapoff -a
  sed -i '/swap/s/^/#/' /etc/fstab

  # Disable firewalld (or configure ports — see section 16.3)
  systemctl disable --now firewalld   # RHEL/Rocky
  ufw disable                          # Ubuntu

  # Set hostname properly
  hostnamectl set-hostname master-01
  echo "10.0.1.10 master-01" >> /etc/hosts

INSTALL RKE2 SERVER (CONTROL PLANE):
  # Method 1: install script
  curl -sfL https://get.rke2.io | sh -

  # Method 2: install specific version
  curl -sfL https://get.rke2.io | INSTALL_RKE2_VERSION=v1.29.4+rke2r1 sh -

  # Method 3: air-gapped (download packages first)
  # Download from: https://github.com/rancher/rke2/releases
  # - rke2.linux-amd64.tar.gz
  # - rke2-images.linux-amd64.tar.zst
  # - sha256sum-amd64.txt

  # Verify checksum
  sha256sum -c sha256sum-amd64.txt --ignore-missing

  # For air-gapped, copy images
  mkdir -p /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/images/
  cp rke2-images.linux-amd64.tar.zst /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/images/

  # Install from tarball
  tar -xzf rke2.linux-amd64.tar.gz
  INSTALL_RKE2_ARTIFACT_PATH=$(pwd) sh install.sh

CREATE CONFIGURATION:
  mkdir -p /etc/rancher/rke2/

  cat > /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml << 'EOF'
  # Server config
  write-kubeconfig-mode: "0644"
  tls-san:
  - 10.0.1.10          # this server's IP
  - master-01          # hostname
  - k8s.example.com    # VIP / load balancer hostname (for HA)

  # Cluster networking
  cluster-cidr: 10.42.0.0/16    # pod CIDR
  service-cidr: 10.43.0.0/16    # service CIDR
  cluster-dns: 10.43.0.10       # CoreDNS ClusterIP

  # CNI
  cni: canal                     # canal | calico | cilium | none

  # Disable default ingress if using Traefik
  disable:
  - rke2-ingress-nginx

  # etcd snapshot settings
  etcd-snapshot-schedule-cron: "0 */6 * * *"    # every 6 hours
  etcd-snapshot-retention: 10                    # keep 10 snapshots
  etcd-snapshot-dir: /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/db/snapshots

  # Security
  protect-kernel-defaults: true
  secrets-encryption: true        # encrypt secrets at rest

  # Node labels and taints
  node-label:
  - "node-role=control-plane"

  # Kubelet extra args
  kubelet-arg:
  - "max-pods=110"
  - "eviction-hard=memory.available<500Mi,nodefs.available<10%"
  - "system-reserved=cpu=500m,memory=500Mi"
  EOF

ENABLE AND START:
  # Enable and start RKE2 server
  systemctl enable rke2-server.service
  systemctl start rke2-server.service

  # Watch the startup
  journalctl -u rke2-server -f

  # Wait for node to be Ready (~2 minutes)
  # Set up kubectl
  export KUBECONFIG=/etc/rancher/rke2/rke2.yaml
  export PATH=$PATH:/var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin

  # Or copy to standard location
  mkdir -p ~/.kube
  cp /etc/rancher/rke2/rke2.yaml ~/.kube/config
  chmod 600 ~/.kube/config

  # Verify
  kubectl get nodes
  kubectl get pods -A

VERIFY COMPONENTS:
  # Check all system pods
  kubectl get pods -n kube-system
  kubectl get pods -n cattle-system   # if Rancher installed

  # Check etcd health
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/etcdctl \
    --endpoints https://127.0.0.1:2379 \
    --cacert /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-ca.crt \
    --cert /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-client.crt \
    --key /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-client.key \
    endpoint health

  # Check component status
  kubectl get cs   # ComponentStatus (deprecated but still works)

  # RKE2 status
  systemctl status rke2-server

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.1.3 REAL-WORLD: RKE2 NODE REGISTRATION TOKENS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RKE2 uses tokens for node authentication:

  Server token (used by all joining nodes):
    cat /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/node-token
    # K1087f1d3c8...  ← secret token

  Pre-shared token (set in config.yaml before first start):
    token: mysecrettoken123    # in config.yaml

  Agent-only token (for worker nodes, doesn't grant server access):
    agent-token: agentsecrettoken456    # in config.yaml

  # Store node-token in Vault or secrets manager
  # Rotate token: edit config.yaml, restart RKE2

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 16.2 — CORE: HIGH AVAILABILITY RKE2 CLUSTER
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.2.1 CONCEPTS: RKE2 HA ARCHITECTURE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RKE2 HA TOPOLOGY:

  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │           External Load Balancer                    │
  │    (HAProxy / kube-vip / cloud LB)                  │
  │    VIP: 10.0.1.100:9345 (registration)              │
  │    VIP: 10.0.1.100:6443 (API server)                │
  └──────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┘
             │
    ┌────────▼────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐
    │   master-01     │  │   master-02      │  │   master-03     │
    │  (first server) │◄─►  (server)        │◄─►  (server)       │
    │  etcd leader    │  │  etcd follower   │  │  etcd follower  │
    └─────────────────┘  └─────────────────┘  └─────────────────┘
             │                                         │
    ┌────────▼────────┐                     ┌─────────▼─────────┐
    │   worker-01     │    ...              │   worker-N        │
    │   (agent)       │                    │   (agent)          │
    └─────────────────┘                    └────────────────────┘

ETCD QUORUM IN HA:
  RKE2 uses embedded etcd (not external). etcd uses Raft consensus:
  - 3 servers: tolerates 1 failure (quorum = 2)
  - 5 servers: tolerates 2 failures (quorum = 3)
  - Minimum for HA: 3 server nodes
  - Never use even number of server nodes (split-brain risk)

REGISTRATION PORT 9345:
  RKE2 uses port 9345 for agent/server registration (NOT 6443).
  - Port 9345: RKE2 registration API (agent nodes join here)
  - Port 6443: Kubernetes API server (kubectl, apps)
  Both should be behind the load balancer VIP.

RKE2 HA BOOTSTRAP SEQUENCE:
  1. First server: start with --cluster-init flag (initializes new etcd cluster)
  2. Wait for first server to be Ready
  3. Get node-token from first server
  4. Second + third servers: start with --server pointing to first server (or VIP)
     and --token from step 3
  5. Workers: start with rke2-agent, point to VIP, use token

KUBE-VIP (VIRTUAL IP FOR BARE METAL HA):
  kube-vip provides a virtual IP (VIP) that floats between control plane nodes.
  Acts as L4 load balancer for kube-apiserver.

  kube-vip modes:
  ARP mode:   VIP assigned to leader node; ARP gratuitous broadcast on leader change
  BGP mode:   VIP advertised via BGP ECMP (load distributes across all masters)

  kube-vip runs as a static pod (DaemonSet on control plane nodes).

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.2.2 HANDS-ON: BUILDING A 3-SERVER HA CLUSTER
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

STEP 1: DEPLOY KUBE-VIP AS STATIC POD ON FIRST SERVER:
  # On master-01 BEFORE starting RKE2:
  # Create static pod manifest directory
  mkdir -p /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/pod-manifests

  # Pull kube-vip image and generate manifest
  export VIP=10.0.1.100
  export INTERFACE=eth0
  export KVVERSION=v0.7.2

  docker run --rm ghcr.io/kube-vip/kube-vip:${KVVERSION} manifest pod \
    --interface ${INTERFACE} \
    --vip ${VIP} \
    --controlplane \
    --services \
    --arp \
    --leaderElection | tee /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/pod-manifests/kube-vip.yaml

  # OR without Docker, use containerd (ctr):
  ctr image pull ghcr.io/kube-vip/kube-vip:${KVVERSION}
  ctr run --rm --net-host ghcr.io/kube-vip/kube-vip:${KVVERSION} vip \
    /kube-vip manifest pod \
    --interface ${INTERFACE} \
    --vip ${VIP} \
    --controlplane \
    --arp \
    --leaderElection | tee /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/pod-manifests/kube-vip.yaml

  # kube-vip needs RBAC to work with RKE2 (for leader election)
  # Create RBAC manifest in manifests auto-deploy directory:
  curl https://kube-vip.io/manifests/rbac.yaml > \
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/manifests/kube-vip-rbac.yaml

STEP 2: CONFIGURE AND START FIRST SERVER:
  # /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml on master-01
  cat > /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml << 'EOF'
  cluster-init: true            # initialize new etcd cluster
  token: MySecureClusterToken123!

  tls-san:
  - 10.0.1.100          # VIP
  - 10.0.1.10           # master-01 IP
  - 10.0.1.11           # master-02 IP
  - 10.0.1.12           # master-03 IP
  - k8s.example.com     # DNS name for VIP

  cni: cilium
  disable:
  - rke2-ingress-nginx

  cluster-cidr: 10.42.0.0/16
  service-cidr: 10.43.0.0/16

  secrets-encryption: true
  protect-kernel-defaults: true

  etcd-expose-metrics: true
  etcd-snapshot-schedule-cron: "0 */6 * * *"
  etcd-snapshot-retention: 10

  kubelet-arg:
  - "max-pods=110"
  - "eviction-hard=memory.available<500Mi,nodefs.available<10%"
  EOF

  systemctl enable --now rke2-server
  journalctl -u rke2-server -f

  # Wait until node is Ready
  export KUBECONFIG=/etc/rancher/rke2/rke2.yaml
  export PATH=$PATH:/var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin
  kubectl get nodes

  # Get token for other nodes
  cat /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/node-token

STEP 3: JOIN SECOND AND THIRD SERVERS:
  # On master-02 and master-03 — config WITHOUT cluster-init:
  cat > /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml << 'EOF'
  server: https://10.0.1.100:9345   # point to VIP (or first server initially)
  token: MySecureClusterToken123!

  tls-san:
  - 10.0.1.100
  - 10.0.1.10
  - 10.0.1.11
  - 10.0.1.12
  - k8s.example.com

  cni: cilium
  disable:
  - rke2-ingress-nginx

  cluster-cidr: 10.42.0.0/16
  service-cidr: 10.43.0.0/16

  secrets-encryption: true
  protect-kernel-defaults: true

  etcd-snapshot-schedule-cron: "0 */6 * * *"
  etcd-snapshot-retention: 10
  EOF

  # Copy kube-vip manifest to each master (same VIP, same interface):
  scp root@master-01:/var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/pod-manifests/kube-vip.yaml \
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/agent/pod-manifests/kube-vip.yaml

  systemctl enable --now rke2-server
  journalctl -u rke2-server -f

  # Verify all 3 masters joined:
  kubectl get nodes

STEP 4: JOIN WORKER NODES:
  # Install RKE2 as agent on worker nodes:
  curl -sfL https://get.rke2.io | INSTALL_RKE2_TYPE=agent sh -

  cat > /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml << 'EOF'
  server: https://10.0.1.100:9345   # VIP
  token: MySecureClusterToken123!

  node-label:
  - "node-role=worker"

  kubelet-arg:
  - "max-pods=110"
  EOF

  systemctl enable --now rke2-agent
  journalctl -u rke2-agent -f

  # Verify workers joined:
  kubectl get nodes -o wide

STEP 5: INSTALL CILIUM CNI (replacing Canal default):
  # If cni: cilium set in config, RKE2 deploys Cilium automatically via HelmChart CRD
  # Check:
  kubectl get helmchart -n kube-system
  kubectl get pods -n kube-system | grep cilium

  # OR install manually via Helm:
  helm repo add cilium https://helm.cilium.io/
  helm upgrade --install cilium cilium/cilium \
    --namespace kube-system \
    --set kubeProxyReplacement=true \
    --set k8sServiceHost=10.0.1.100 \
    --set k8sServicePort=6443 \
    --set ipam.mode=kubernetes \
    --set ipam.operator.clusterPoolIPv4PodCIDRList=10.42.0.0/16 \
    --set hubble.enabled=true \
    --set hubble.relay.enabled=true \
    --set hubble.ui.enabled=true

  # Check Cilium status
  cilium status
  cilium connectivity test

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.2.3 REAL-WORLD: CLUSTER NETWORKING CONFIGURATION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

REQUIRED FIREWALL PORTS:

  Control Plane Nodes → All Nodes:
    TCP 2376    — Docker (not used in RKE2, legacy)
    TCP 2379-2380 — etcd client + peer (between server nodes only)
    TCP 6443    — Kubernetes API server (kubectl, agents)
    TCP 9345    — RKE2 registration endpoint
    TCP 10250   — kubelet API (metrics server, kubectl logs/exec)
    UDP 8472    — VXLAN (CNI overlay, if using Flannel/Canal)
    TCP 4240    — Cilium health check
    UDP 8472    — Cilium VXLAN
    TCP 4244    — Hubble
    TCP 179     — BGP (if using Cilium BGP mode)

  Worker Nodes:
    TCP 10250   — kubelet API
    TCP 30000-32767 — NodePort range

  # Configure UFW (Ubuntu):
  ufw allow 6443/tcp
  ufw allow 9345/tcp
  ufw allow 2379:2380/tcp
  ufw allow 10250/tcp
  ufw allow 8472/udp
  ufw allow 4240/tcp
  ufw enable

NODE SELECTOR AND TAINT STRATEGY:
  # Label nodes at join time (in config.yaml):
  node-label:
  - "role=storage"
  - "disk=ssd"

  # Or label after joining:
  kubectl label node worker-03 role=storage disk=ssd

  # Taint control plane nodes (prevent workloads):
  kubectl taint node master-01 node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane:NoSchedule
  kubectl taint node master-02 node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane:NoSchedule
  kubectl taint node master-03 node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane:NoSchedule

  # Or set in config.yaml:
  node-taint:
  - "CriticalAddonsOnly=true:NoExecute"

RKE2 HELMCHART CRD (auto-deploy Helm charts):
  # RKE2 watches /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/manifests/ and auto-applies
  # manifests and HelmChart CRDs placed there.

  # Example: auto-deploy Longhorn after cluster starts
  cat > /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/manifests/longhorn.yaml << 'EOF'
  apiVersion: helm.cattle.io/v1
  kind: HelmChart
  metadata:
    name: longhorn
    namespace: kube-system
  spec:
    chart: longhorn
    repo: https://charts.longhorn.io
    targetNamespace: longhorn-system
    createNamespace: true
    version: 1.6.2
    valuesContent: |-
      defaultSettings:
        defaultReplicaCount: 3
  EOF

  # Check HelmChart status
  kubectl get helmchart -n kube-system
  kubectl get helmchartconfig -n kube-system

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
SECTION 16.3 — ADVANCED: SECURITY HARDENING AND CIS COMPLIANCE
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.3.1 CONCEPTS: RKE2 CIS HARDENING PROFILE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

CIS KUBERNETES BENCHMARK:
  The CIS (Center for Internet Security) Benchmark defines security configuration
  requirements for Kubernetes. RKE2 is designed to pass CIS 1.7 and 1.8 profiles
  with minimal extra configuration.

RKE2 BUILT-IN SECURITY FEATURES:
  1. etcd encrypted at rest (secrets-encryption: true)
     Encryption config: /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/cred/encryption-config.json
     Uses: secretbox (NaCl) for secrets, AES-CBC for other resources

  2. Audit logging:
     RKE2 ships a default audit policy. Events logged to:
     /var/log/kube-audit/audit.log (on control plane nodes)

  3. Pod Security Admission (PSA):
     Default Pod Security Standards enforced at namespace level.
     Configurable via PodSecurityConfiguration.

  4. Default TLS ciphers:
     Only strong cipher suites allowed (TLS 1.2+).

  5. Anonymous auth disabled:
     kube-apiserver --anonymous-auth=false

  6. Node restrictions:
     NodeRestriction admission plugin enabled by default.

ENABLING CIS PROFILE:
  # In config.yaml, add:
  profile: cis       # enables CIS 1.6 profile
  # OR:
  profile: cis-1.23  # specific CIS profile version

  # CIS profile sets:
  # kube-apiserver: additional security flags
  # etcd: tls peer auth
  # kubelet: additional security flags
  # Applies PodSecurityConfiguration restrictive profile to kube-system

OS PREPARATION FOR CIS:
  # Required for CIS profile — run on ALL nodes before starting RKE2:

  # 1. Set kernel parameters
  cat >> /etc/sysctl.d/60-rke2-cis.conf << 'EOF'
  vm.panic_on_oom = 0
  vm.overcommit_memory = 1
  kernel.panic = 10
  kernel.panic_on_oops = 1
  EOF
  sysctl --system

  # 2. Create etcd user (required by CIS profile for etcd ownership)
  useradd -r -c "etcd user" -s /sbin/nologin -M etcd -U

  # 3. Ensure etcd data dir is owned by etcd user
  mkdir -p /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/db/etcd
  chown -R etcd:etcd /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/db/etcd

  # 4. Set kernel dmesg restrictions
  echo "kernel.dmesg_restrict = 1" >> /etc/sysctl.d/60-rke2-cis.conf

AUDIT POLICY CUSTOMIZATION:
  # Custom audit policy — place at:
  # /etc/rancher/rke2/audit-policy.yaml

  apiVersion: audit.k8s.io/v1
  kind: Policy
  rules:
  # Log all requests to secrets at RequestResponse level
  - level: RequestResponse
    resources:
    - group: ""
      resources: [secrets]

  # Log pod exec/attach/portforward
  - level: RequestResponse
    verbs: [create]
    resources:
    - group: ""
      resources: [pods/exec, pods/attach, pods/portforward]

  # Log namespace changes
  - level: Request
    verbs: [create, update, patch, delete]
    resources:
    - group: ""
      resources: [namespaces]

  # Minimize metadata logging for other resources
  - level: Metadata
    omitStages: [RequestReceived]

  # In config.yaml reference it:
  kube-apiserver-arg:
  - "audit-policy-file=/etc/rancher/rke2/audit-policy.yaml"
  - "audit-log-path=/var/log/kube-audit/audit.log"
  - "audit-log-maxsize=100"
  - "audit-log-maxbackup=10"
  - "audit-log-maxage=30"

POD SECURITY STANDARDS IN RKE2:
  # Configure PSA at cluster level via AdmissionConfiguration
  # /etc/rancher/rke2/psa.yaml
  apiVersion: apiserver.config.k8s.io/v1
  kind: AdmissionConfiguration
  plugins:
  - name: PodSecurity
    configuration:
      apiVersion: pod-security.admission.config.k8s.io/v1
      kind: PodSecurityConfiguration
      defaults:
        enforce: baseline
        enforce-version: latest
        audit: restricted
        audit-version: latest
        warn: restricted
        warn-version: latest
      exemptions:
        usernames: []
        runtimeClasses: []
        namespaces:
        - kube-system
        - kube-public
        - kube-node-lease
        - cattle-system
        - longhorn-system

  # Reference in config.yaml:
  kube-apiserver-arg:
  - "admission-control-config-file=/etc/rancher/rke2/psa.yaml"

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.3.2 HANDS-ON: RUNNING CIS BENCHMARK SCANS
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

KUBE-BENCH (CIS BENCHMARK SCANNER):
  # kube-bench tests cluster configuration against CIS benchmark
  # Run on each node type

  # On control plane node:
  docker run --pid=host -v /etc:/etc:ro -v /var:/var:ro \
    -v /var/lib/rancher/rke2:/var/lib/rancher/rke2:ro \
    -v /usr/local/bin/kubectl:/usr/local/bin/kubectl:ro \
    --rm aquasec/kube-bench:latest \
    --config-dir /opt/kube-bench/cfg \
    --benchmark rke2-cis-1.7

  # On worker node:
  docker run --pid=host -v /etc:/etc:ro -v /var:/var:ro \
    --rm aquasec/kube-bench:latest \
    node --benchmark rke2-cis-1.7

  # Or as a Kubernetes Job:
  kubectl apply -f https://raw.githubusercontent.com/aquasecurity/kube-bench/main/job.yaml
  kubectl logs job/kube-bench

TRIVY OPERATOR (CONTINUOUS COMPLIANCE):
  helm repo add aquasecurity https://aquasecurity.github.io/helm-charts
  helm upgrade --install trivy-operator aquasecurity/trivy-operator \
    --namespace trivy-system \
    --create-namespace \
    --set trivy.ignoreUnfixed=true \
    --set operator.scanJobsConcurrentLimit=2

  # Trivy operator continuously scans:
  # - Container images for CVEs
  # - K8s resource configs (CIS compliance)
  # - RBAC risks
  # - Secrets in configs

  # View reports:
  kubectl get vulnerabilityreports -A
  kubectl get configauditreports -A
  kubectl get rbacassessmentreports -A

  # Detailed report:
  kubectl describe vulnerabilityreport myapp-deployment -n production

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.3.3 REAL-WORLD: SECRETS ENCRYPTION AT REST
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

HOW ENCRYPTION AT REST WORKS IN RKE2:
  When secrets-encryption: true:
    1. RKE2 generates encryption config at bootstrap:
       /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/cred/encryption-config.json
    2. kube-apiserver uses this config to encrypt secrets before storing in etcd
    3. Encryption: secretbox (NaCl XSalsa20+Poly1305) by default
    4. Key stored in encryption-config.json on control plane nodes

  Data flow:
    kubectl create secret → kube-apiserver → encrypts → stores ciphertext in etcd
    kubectl get secret → kube-apiserver → reads from etcd → decrypts → returns

  Backup of encryption key is CRITICAL — without it, secrets cannot be recovered!

ROTATING ENCRYPTION KEYS:
  # RKE2 supports key rotation without downtime

  # Step 1: Prepare new key
  rke2 secrets-encrypt prepare

  # Step 2: Restart RKE2 on all server nodes (one at a time)
  systemctl restart rke2-server

  # Step 3: Rotate (re-encrypt all secrets with new key)
  rke2 secrets-encrypt rotate

  # Step 4: Restart all server nodes again
  systemctl restart rke2-server

  # Step 5: Reencrypt (remove old key)
  rke2 secrets-encrypt reencrypt

  # Check encryption status:
  rke2 secrets-encrypt status

SECTION 16.4 — EXPERT: CLUSTER OPERATIONS AND LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.4.1 CONCEPTS: ETCD OPERATIONS IN RKE2
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RKE2 ETCD SNAPSHOT MANAGEMENT:

  # List snapshots
  rke2 etcd-snapshot list

  # Save snapshot manually
  rke2 etcd-snapshot save --name manual-snap-$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S)

  # Save to S3
  rke2 etcd-snapshot save \
    --name manual-snap \
    --s3 \
    --s3-bucket my-rke2-etcd-backups \
    --s3-region us-east-1 \
    --s3-access-key AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE \
    --s3-secret-key wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY

  # Enable scheduled S3 snapshots in config.yaml:
  etcd-snapshot-schedule-cron: "0 */6 * * *"
  etcd-snapshot-retention: 10
  etcd-s3: true
  etcd-s3-bucket: my-rke2-etcd-backups
  etcd-s3-region: us-east-1
  etcd-s3-access-key: AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE
  etcd-s3-secret-key: wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY

ETCD RESTORE IN RKE2:
  # CRITICAL: restore must happen on a STOPPED cluster

  # Step 1: Stop RKE2 on ALL server nodes
  systemctl stop rke2-server   # on master-01, master-02, master-03

  # Step 2: Restore from snapshot on ONE server node (master-01)
  rke2 server \
    --cluster-reset \
    --cluster-reset-restore-path=/var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/db/snapshots/manual-snap

  # For S3 snapshot:
  rke2 server \
    --cluster-reset \
    --cluster-reset-restore-path=s3://my-rke2-etcd-backups/manual-snap \
    --etcd-s3 \
    --etcd-s3-bucket=my-rke2-etcd-backups \
    --etcd-s3-region=us-east-1 \
    --etcd-s3-access-key=AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE \
    --etcd-s3-secret-key=wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY

  # Step 3: Start master-01
  systemctl start rke2-server

  # Step 4: Delete etcd data on other masters and re-join them
  # On master-02 and master-03:
  rm -rf /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/db/etcd
  systemctl start rke2-server
  # They rejoin as followers, etcd data syncs from master-01

  # Step 5: Verify cluster
  kubectl get nodes
  kubectl get pods -A

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.4.2 HANDS-ON: UPGRADING RKE2
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

MANUAL UPGRADE:
  # Upgrade procedure: servers first, then agents
  # ALWAYS upgrade one node at a time
  # Supported: skip at most 2 minor versions

  # Step 1: Drain server node
  kubectl drain master-01 --ignore-daemonsets --delete-emptydir-data

  # Step 2: Install new RKE2 version (keeps config.yaml)
  curl -sfL https://get.rke2.io | INSTALL_RKE2_VERSION=v1.30.1+rke2r1 sh -

  # Step 3: Restart service
  systemctl restart rke2-server

  # Step 4: Verify node is Ready with new version
  kubectl get node master-01 -o jsonpath='{.status.nodeInfo.kubeletVersion}'

  # Step 5: Uncordon
  kubectl uncordon master-01

  # Repeat for master-02, master-03, then all workers

AUTOMATED UPGRADE WITH SYSTEM UPGRADE CONTROLLER:
  # System Upgrade Controller (SUC) automates node upgrades via Plans

  # Install SUC
  kubectl apply -f https://github.com/rancher/system-upgrade-controller/releases/latest/download/system-upgrade-controller.yaml

  # Create upgrade Plan for servers
  apiVersion: upgrade.cattle.io/v1
  kind: Plan
  metadata:
    name: rke2-server-upgrade
    namespace: system-upgrade
  spec:
    concurrency: 1             # upgrade one server at a time
    cordon: true               # cordon before upgrading
    drain:
      force: true
    nodeSelector:
      matchExpressions:
      - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane
        operator: Exists
    serviceAccountName: system-upgrade
    upgrade:
      image: rancher/rke2-upgrade
    version: v1.30.1+rke2r1

  # Create upgrade Plan for agents
  apiVersion: upgrade.cattle.io/v1
  kind: Plan
  metadata:
    name: rke2-agent-upgrade
    namespace: system-upgrade
  spec:
    concurrency: 2             # upgrade 2 workers at a time
    cordon: true
    drain:
      force: true
      skipWaitForDeleteTimeout: 60
    nodeSelector:
      matchExpressions:
      - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane
        operator: DoesNotExist
    prepare:
      args: [prepare, rke2-server-upgrade]  # wait for server plan to complete
      image: rancher/rke2-upgrade
    serviceAccountName: system-upgrade
    upgrade:
      image: rancher/rke2-upgrade
    version: v1.30.1+rke2r1

  # Monitor upgrade progress
  kubectl get plans -n system-upgrade
  kubectl get jobs -n system-upgrade
  kubectl get nodes -o wide

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.4.3 HANDS-ON: RANCHER MULTI-CLUSTER MANAGEMENT
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RANCHER SERVER — MANAGING MULTIPLE RKE2 CLUSTERS:
  Rancher is the management plane for RKE2/K3s clusters. It provides:
  - Central Web UI for all clusters
  - Cluster provisioning (click-to-create RKE2 clusters)
  - Multi-cluster workload management
  - Centralized RBAC and SSO
  - Fleet (GitOps for multi-cluster)
  - Continuous Delivery (GitOps with Fleet)
  - App Catalog (Helm charts)
  - Monitoring stack deployment

INSTALL RANCHER ON DEDICATED MANAGEMENT CLUSTER:
  # Rancher runs on its own RKE2 cluster (not mixed with workload clusters)

  # Prerequisites: cert-manager
  kubectl apply -f https://github.com/cert-manager/cert-manager/releases/download/v1.14.5/cert-manager.crds.yaml
  helm repo add jetstack https://charts.jetstack.io
  helm upgrade --install cert-manager jetstack/cert-manager \
    --namespace cert-manager \
    --create-namespace \
    --version v1.14.5

  # Install Rancher
  helm repo add rancher-stable https://releases.rancher.com/server-charts/stable
  helm upgrade --install rancher rancher-stable/rancher \
    --namespace cattle-system \
    --create-namespace \
    --set hostname=rancher.example.com \
    --set replicas=3 \
    --set bootstrapPassword=admin \
    --set ingress.tls.source=letsEncrypt \
    --set letsEncrypt.email=devops@example.com \
    --set letsEncrypt.ingress.class=traefik

  # Wait for Rancher to be ready
  kubectl rollout status deployment/rancher -n cattle-system

  # Get initial password
  kubectl get secret --namespace cattle-system bootstrap-secret \
    -o go-template='{{.data.bootstrapPassword|base64decode}}'

IMPORTING EXISTING RKE2 CLUSTERS INTO RANCHER:
  # In Rancher UI: Cluster Management → Import Existing → Generic
  # Get the kubectl apply command from UI:
  kubectl apply -f https://rancher.example.com/v3/import/xxxxx.yaml

  # This installs cattle-cluster-agent and cattle-node-agent in the cluster
  # Cluster appears in Rancher UI after ~2 minutes

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.4.4 REAL-WORLD: COMPLETE RKE2 PRODUCTION AUTOMATION
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

ANSIBLE PLAYBOOK FOR FULL RKE2 CLUSTER DEPLOYMENT:

  # site.yml — complete cluster deployment
  ---
  - name: Prepare all nodes
    hosts: k8s_all
    become: true
    roles:
    - role: rke2-prereqs
      tags: [prereqs]

  - name: Bootstrap first server
    hosts: rke2_first_server
    become: true
    roles:
    - role: rke2-server
      vars:
        rke2_type: server
        rke2_cluster_init: true
      tags: [servers]

  - name: Join additional servers
    hosts: rke2_servers
    become: true
    serial: 1
    roles:
    - role: rke2-server
      vars:
        rke2_type: server
        rke2_cluster_init: false
      tags: [servers]

  - name: Join worker nodes
    hosts: rke2_agents
    become: true
    roles:
    - role: rke2-agent
      tags: [agents]

  - name: Deploy cluster add-ons
    hosts: rke2_first_server
    become: false
    roles:
    - role: cluster-addons
      tags: [addons]

  # roles/rke2-prereqs/tasks/main.yml
  ---
  - name: Disable swap
    command: swapoff -a
    changed_when: false

  - name: Remove swap from fstab
    replace:
      path: /etc/fstab
      regexp: '^([^#].*\s+swap\s+.*)$'
      replace: '# \1'

  - name: Load kernel modules
    modprobe:
      name: "{{ item }}"
    loop: [overlay, br_netfilter]

  - name: Set sysctl for Kubernetes
    sysctl:
      name: "{{ item.name }}"
      value: "{{ item.value }}"
      state: present
      reload: true
    loop:
    - { name: net.bridge.bridge-nf-call-iptables,  value: "1" }
    - { name: net.bridge.bridge-nf-call-ip6tables, value: "1" }
    - { name: net.ipv4.ip_forward,                 value: "1" }
    - { name: vm.max_map_count,                    value: "262144" }
    - { name: fs.inotify.max_user_watches,         value: "524288" }

  - name: Install open-iscsi for Longhorn
    apt:
      name: [open-iscsi, nfs-common]
      state: present
      update_cache: true

  - name: Enable iscsid
    service:
      name: iscsid
      state: started
      enabled: true

  # roles/rke2-server/tasks/main.yml
  ---
  - name: Create RKE2 config directory
    file:
      path: /etc/rancher/rke2
      state: directory
      mode: '0755'

  - name: Write RKE2 config
    template:
      src: config.yaml.j2
      dest: /etc/rancher/rke2/config.yaml
      owner: root
      group: root
      mode: '0640'

  - name: Install RKE2
    shell: |
      curl -sfL https://get.rke2.io | \
        INSTALL_RKE2_VERSION={{ rke2_version }} \
        INSTALL_RKE2_TYPE=server sh -
    args:
      creates: /usr/local/bin/rke2

  - name: Enable and start RKE2 server
    service:
      name: rke2-server
      state: started
      enabled: true

  - name: Wait for node to be Ready
    shell: |
      /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/kubectl \
        --kubeconfig /etc/rancher/rke2/rke2.yaml \
        get node {{ inventory_hostname }} \
        -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[?(@.type=="Ready")].status}'
    register: node_ready
    until: node_ready.stdout == "True"
    retries: 30
    delay: 15
    changed_when: false
    when: rke2_cluster_init | bool

  - name: Fetch node token (first server only)
    slurp:
      src: /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/node-token
    register: node_token_raw
    when: rke2_cluster_init | bool

  - name: Set token fact for other nodes
    set_fact:
      rke2_token: "{{ node_token_raw.content | b64decode | trim }}"
    when: rke2_cluster_init | bool
    delegate_to: "{{ item }}"
    delegate_facts: true
    with_items: "{{ groups['k8s_all'] }}"

TERRAFORM FOR RKE2 INFRASTRUCTURE (before Ansible runs):
  # Provision VMs (bare metal: use cloud-init or PXE)
  # On AWS/GCP/Azure: provision VMs via Terraform, then run Ansible

  # terraform/main.tf
  module "rke2_cluster" {
    source = "./modules/rke2"

    cluster_name   = "prod-cluster"
    server_count   = 3
    agent_count    = 5
    server_type    = "t3.xlarge"   # 4 vCPU, 16GB RAM
    agent_type     = "t3.2xlarge"  # 8 vCPU, 32GB RAM

    vpc_id         = module.vpc.vpc_id
    subnet_ids     = module.vpc.private_subnet_ids

    rke2_version   = "v1.29.4+rke2r1"
    ssh_key_name   = aws_key_pair.rke2.key_name
  }

  # After terraform apply, generate Ansible inventory from Terraform outputs:
  terraform output -json > tf_output.json
  python3 scripts/generate_inventory.py tf_output.json > inventory/production/hosts.yml

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.4.5 REAL-WORLD: RKE2 MONITORING AND TROUBLESHOOTING
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

MONITORING RKE2 CLUSTER:
  # Deploy kube-prometheus-stack (includes Prometheus, Grafana, Alertmanager)
  helm repo add prometheus-community https://prometheus-community.github.io/helm-charts
  helm upgrade --install kube-prometheus-stack \
    prometheus-community/kube-prometheus-stack \
    --namespace monitoring \
    --create-namespace \
    --set prometheus.prometheusSpec.storageSpec.volumeClaimTemplate.spec.storageClassName=longhorn \
    --set prometheus.prometheusSpec.storageSpec.volumeClaimTemplate.spec.resources.requests.storage=50Gi \
    --set grafana.persistence.enabled=true \
    --set grafana.persistence.storageClassName=longhorn \
    --set alertmanager.alertmanagerSpec.storage.volumeClaimTemplate.spec.storageClassName=longhorn

  # Key metrics for RKE2 control plane:
  # etcd:
  etcd_server_has_leader                         # 1 = has leader, 0 = no leader
  etcd_server_leader_changes_seen_total          # leader elections (high = instability)
  etcd_disk_backend_commit_duration_seconds      # etcd disk commit latency
  etcd_network_peer_round_trip_time_seconds      # peer communication latency
  etcd_mvcc_db_total_size_in_bytes               # database size (alert at >8GB)

  # kube-apiserver:
  apiserver_request_duration_seconds             # API request latency
  apiserver_request_total{code="5.."}            # API server errors
  apiserver_current_inflight_requests            # concurrent requests

  # Scheduler:
  scheduler_schedule_attempts_total{result}      # scheduling attempts by result

  # Controller manager:
  workqueue_depth                                # reconciliation queue depth

TROUBLESHOOTING COMMON RKE2 ISSUES:

  Issue 1: Node stuck in NotReady
    # Check kubelet logs
    journalctl -u rke2-server -n 100 --no-pager   # on server nodes
    journalctl -u rke2-agent -n 100 --no-pager    # on agent nodes

    # Check containerd
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl \
      --runtime-endpoint unix:///run/k3s/containerd/containerd.sock \
      ps

    # Check CNI
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl pods | grep canal
    kubectl get pods -n kube-system | grep -E "canal|calico|cilium"

  Issue 2: etcd unhealthy
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/etcdctl \
      --endpoints https://127.0.0.1:2379 \
      --cacert /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-ca.crt \
      --cert /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-client.crt \
      --key /var/lib/rancher/rke2/server/tls/etcd/server-client.key \
      endpoint health --cluster

    # Check etcd disk latency (>25ms = problem)
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/etcdctl \
      --endpoints https://127.0.0.1:2379 \
      ... \
      check perf

    # Check etcd member list
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/etcdctl ... member list

  Issue 3: API server unreachable
    # Check if kube-apiserver is running
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl ps | grep kube-apiserver

    # Check apiserver logs
    /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl logs \
      $(/var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl ps | awk '/kube-apiserver/{print $1}')

    # Check certificate expiry
    rke2 certificate check

    # Check kube-vip is running
    kubectl get pods -n kube-system | grep kube-vip

  Issue 4: Pods pending (scheduling failure)
    kubectl describe pod <pod-name> -n <ns>   # look at Events
    kubectl get events -n <ns> --sort-by='.lastTimestamp'

    # Check node resources
    kubectl describe nodes | grep -A5 "Allocated resources"
    kubectl top nodes

    # Check taints
    kubectl get nodes -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,TAINTS:.spec.taints

  Issue 5: CNI / networking issues
    # Test pod-to-pod connectivity
    kubectl run test --rm -it --image=nicolaka/netshoot -- ping <pod-ip>

    # Check CNI logs (Cilium)
    kubectl logs -n kube-system -l k8s-app=cilium --tail=50

    # Cilium connectivity check
    cilium connectivity test --test-namespace=cilium-test

RKE2 CRICTL COMMANDS (for containerd on RKE2 nodes):
  # Set CRICTL to use RKE2's containerd socket
  export CRI_CONFIG_FILE=/etc/crictl.yaml
  cat > /etc/crictl.yaml << 'EOF'
  runtime-endpoint: unix:///run/k3s/containerd/containerd.sock
  image-endpoint: unix:///run/k3s/containerd/containerd.sock
  timeout: 10
  debug: false
  EOF

  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl ps        # list running containers
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl pods      # list pods
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl images    # list images
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl logs <id> # container logs
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl exec -it <id> /bin/sh  # exec into container
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl pull <image>   # pull image into containerd
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl rmi <image>    # remove image
  /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl info           # containerd info

  # Add to PATH for convenience:
  ln -s /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/crictl /usr/local/bin/crictl
  ln -s /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/kubectl /usr/local/bin/kubectl
  ln -s /var/lib/rancher/rke2/bin/etcdctl /usr/local/bin/etcdctl

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
16.5 FULL STACK INTEGRATION: TYING ALL PHASES TOGETHER
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

COMPLETE PRODUCTION PLATFORM STACK ON RKE2:

  INFRASTRUCTURE LAYER:
    Terraform/Terragrunt  → provision VMs/cloud resources
    Ansible               → configure OS, install RKE2, join nodes

  CLUSTER LAYER (RKE2):
    3 server nodes        → HA etcd + control plane
    N worker nodes        → workload execution
    kube-vip              → control plane VIP (bare metal)
    MetalLB               → LoadBalancer service VIP

  NETWORKING LAYER:
    Cilium                → CNI (eBPF, NetworkPolicy, Hubble)
    CoreDNS               → cluster DNS
    Traefik               → Ingress controller + edge proxy
    cert-manager          → TLS certificate automation
    external-dns          → DNS record automation

  STORAGE LAYER:
    Longhorn              → distributed block storage (RWO)
    NFS provisioner       → shared storage (RWX, optional)

  GITOPS / DEPLOYMENT LAYER:
    ArgoCD                → GitOps continuous delivery
    Helm                  → package management (called by ArgoCD)
    Kustomize             → environment-specific overlays

  SERVICE MESH LAYER:
    Istio (optional)      → east-west mTLS, traffic management
    OR Cilium mesh        → eBPF-based service mesh (simpler)

  BACKUP / DR LAYER:
    Velero                → K8s resource + PV backup
    Longhorn recurring    → storage-level snapshots
    etcd snapshots        → cluster state backup (built into RKE2)

  OBSERVABILITY LAYER:
    Prometheus            → metrics collection (kube-prometheus-stack)
    Grafana               → dashboards
    Loki + Promtail/Alloy → log aggregation
    Tempo                 → distributed tracing
    Alertmanager          → alert routing

  SECURITY LAYER:
    CIS profile           → hardened RKE2 configuration
    PSA                   → Pod Security Admission
    NetworkPolicy         → namespace isolation (via Cilium)
    OPA/Gatekeeper        → policy enforcement
    Trivy Operator        → continuous CVE scanning
    Vault                 → secrets management

  CI/CD LAYER:
    GitHub Actions / GitLab CI → build, test, push images
    ArgoCD Image Updater  → detect new images, update GitOps repo
    ArgoCD                → deploy from GitOps repo to cluster

DEPLOYMENT ORDER FOR FRESH CLUSTER:
  1. Infrastructure (Terraform): VMs, networking, DNS
  2. OS preparation (Ansible): kernel modules, sysctl, packages
  3. RKE2 install (Ansible): servers + agents
  4. CNI (Cilium): networking comes first, nothing works without it
  5. MetalLB: LoadBalancer services
  6. cert-manager: TLS management
  7. Traefik: ingress
  8. external-dns: DNS automation
  9. Longhorn: storage
  10. ArgoCD: GitOps controller (manages remaining stack from Git)
  11. [via ArgoCD] Velero, Prometheus, Grafana, Loki, Tempo, Alertmanager
  12. [via ArgoCD] Application workloads

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

RKE2 FUNDAMENTALS:
  □ Explain RKE2 vs RKE1 vs K3s vs kubeadm differences
  □ Understand all bundled components and their roles
  □ Know RKE2's process model (everything in containerd)
  □ Understand data directory layout (/var/lib/rancher/rke2/)
  □ Install single-node RKE2 with custom config.yaml
  □ Set up kubectl and PATH for RKE2 binaries
  □ Use crictl with RKE2's containerd socket

SINGLE-NODE OPERATIONS:
  □ Configure tls-san, cluster-cidr, service-cidr, cni, secrets-encryption
  □ Disable default add-ons (rke2-ingress-nginx)
  □ Use HelmChart CRD for auto-deploying add-ons
  □ Configure etcd snapshots (local + S3)
  □ Rotate certificates with rke2 certificate rotate

HA CLUSTER:
  □ Understand 3-node etcd quorum and why odd numbers matter
  □ Know ports required (9345 registration, 6443 API, 2379-2380 etcd)
  □ Deploy kube-vip as static pod for control plane VIP
  □ Bootstrap first server with cluster-init: true
  □ Join additional servers pointing to VIP
  □ Join worker nodes with rke2-agent
  □ Understand token vs agent-token separation

SECURITY HARDENING:
  □ Enable CIS profile (profile: cis) and required OS prerequisites
  □ Configure audit logging with custom audit policy
  □ Configure Pod Security Admission via AdmissionConfiguration
  □ Understand etcd encryption at rest (secretbox/AES-CBC)
  □ Rotate encryption keys with rke2 secrets-encrypt workflow
  □ Run kube-bench for CIS compliance scanning
  □ Deploy Trivy Operator for continuous compliance

ETCD OPERATIONS:
  □ Take manual etcd snapshots with rke2 etcd-snapshot save
  □ Configure scheduled S3 snapshots in config.yaml
  □ Perform full cluster restore from snapshot (cluster-reset procedure)
  □ Use etcdctl commands for health checks and member management

UPGRADES:
  □ Perform manual rolling upgrade (drain → upgrade → restart → uncordon)
  □ Deploy System Upgrade Controller (SUC)
  □ Create Plans for automated server and agent upgrades
  □ Monitor upgrade progress via Plans and Jobs

OPERATIONS:
  □ Use Ansible for full automated cluster deployment
  □ Integrate with Terraform for infrastructure provisioning
  □ Deploy full monitoring stack (kube-prometheus-stack) on RKE2
  □ Troubleshoot NotReady nodes (kubelet, containerd, CNI)
  □ Troubleshoot etcd issues (health, latency, disk)
  □ Troubleshoot API server issues (cert expiry, kube-vip)
  □ Understand Rancher as multi-cluster management plane
  □ Import existing RKE2 cluster into Rancher

FULL STACK:
  □ Know deployment order for fresh cluster (CNI → MetalLB → Traefik → storage → ArgoCD)
  □ Integrate all 16 phases: Git → Linux → Bash → CI/CD → Containers →
    Kubernetes → Istio → ArgoCD → Helm → AWS → Terraform → Observability →
    Storage/DR → Networking → Ansible → RKE2

PHASES COVERED:
  Phase  1 → Git (internals, objects, workflows, hooks, GPG, LFS, filter-repo)

  Phase  6 → Kubernetes (full control plane, scheduling, networking, storage, RBAC)
  Phase  7 → Istio (xDS, SPIFFE/mTLS, traffic management, ambient mesh)
  Phase  8 → ArgoCD (App of Apps, ApplicationSet, sync waves, SSO, Image Updater)
  Phase  9 → Helm (Go templates, Sprig, hooks, library charts, OCI registry)
  Phase 10 → AWS (IAM/IRSA, VPC, EKS/Karpenter, S3, RDS, KMS, CloudTrail)
